where \(\Lambda\) is the absolute value of the angular momentum about the
source axis; a sign
\(\eta=\pm1\), denoted \(g/u\), for the combined operation which exchanges the
source and antisource and inverts about the midpoint; and, only for
\(\Lambda=0\), a reflection sign \(\epsilon=\pm\) for reflection through a
plane containing the source axis.  At finite lattice spacing with the axis
chosen along a lattice direction, \(D_{\infty h}\) is reduced to the
corresponding lattice subgroup.  The continuum labels are therefore continuum
and large-distance assignments obtained after subduction and extrapolation,
not exact labels of a single finite lattice calculation.

\begin{proposition}[Open flux-tube oscillator labels]
\label{prop:qcd-string-open-dinfty-labels}
Assume the Gaussian open-string sector in \(D=4\), with circular transverse
oscillators \(a_{n,+}^{\dagger}\) and \(a_{n,-}^{\dagger}\) of frequency
\(\pi n/L\), where \(n\geq1\) and the signs denote angular momentum
\(\pm1\) about the source axis.  For a Fock monomial
\[
  \prod_{n\geq1}
  \bigl(a_{n,+}^{\dagger}\bigr)^{N_{n,+}}
  \bigl(a_{n,-}^{\dagger}\bigr)^{N_{n,-}}\vac_{\rm str},
\]
the oscillator level, axial angular-momentum label, and \(g/u\) sign are
\begin{align}
  N&=\sum_{n\geq1}n(N_{n,+}+N_{n,-}),\\
  \Lambda&=\left|\sum_{n\geq1}(N_{n,+}-N_{n,-})\right|,\\
  \eta&=(-1)^{\sum_{n\geq1}n(N_{n,+}+N_{n,-})}.
  \label{eq:qcd-string-open-channel-bookkeeping}
\end{align}
For \(\Lambda=0\), reflection through a plane containing the source axis
exchanges \(+\) and \(-\) oscillators, so reflection eigenstates are the even
and odd combinations of each reflection orbit; if the monomial is pointwise
fixed by this exchange, only the even \(\Sigma^+\) state is obtained.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The level formula is the definition of the open-string oscillator level in
\eqref{eq:qcd-string-open-oscillator-level}.  A circular transverse
oscillator is built from
\[
  X^{+}=X^2+iX^3,\qquad X^{-}=X^2-iX^3 .
\]
Under a rotation by angle \(\alpha\) about the source axis,
\(X^{\pm}\mapsto \ee^{\pm i\alpha}X^{\pm}\).  A monomial with occupations
\(N_{n,\pm}\) therefore has axial angular momentum
\(\sum_n(N_{n,+}-N_{n,-})\), and the irreducible cylindrical label records
its absolute value \(\Lambda\).

The operation defining \(g/u\) exchanges the endpoints and sends
\((z,X^2,X^3)\mapsto(-z,-X^2,-X^3)\) in the static-source coordinate system.
The mode function transforms as
\[
  \sin\frac{\pi n(L-s)}{L}
  =
  (-1)^{n+1}\sin\frac{\pi ns}{L},
\]
while the transverse vector itself contributes the additional sign \(-1\).
Thus a single \(n\)-th transverse oscillator has eigenvalue \((-1)^n\) under
the combined operation, and multiplication over all occupied oscillators gives
the sign \(\eta\) in
\eqref{eq:qcd-string-open-channel-bookkeeping}.  Reflection through a plane
containing the axis complex-conjugates \(X^+\) and \(X^-\), hence exchanges
the two circular polarizations.  For \(\Lambda>0\) this reflection relates the
two helicity components of the same two-dimensional real representation.  For
\(\Lambda=0\) it can be diagonalized, giving \(\epsilon=\pm\) when the
reflection orbit has two monomials and only the even state when the monomial
is fixed.
\end{proof}

For the first oscillator levels in \(D=4\) this gives
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{c|c|c}
level \(N\) & \(D_{\infty h}\) content of the Gaussian reference sector
& total oscillator degeneracy\\
\hline
0 & \(\Sigma_g^+\) & \(1\)\\
1 & \(\Pi_u\) & \(2\)\\
2 & \(\Sigma_g^+\oplus\Pi_g\oplus\Delta_g\) & \(5\)\\
3 &
\(\Sigma_u^+\oplus\Sigma_u^-\oplus2\Pi_u\oplus\Delta_u\oplus\Phi_u\)
& \(10\)
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The table is a long-string reference decomposition.  A measured hybrid static
potential in the same \(\Lambda_\eta^\epsilon\) channel may contain massive
surface excitations, endpoint-local excitations, or short-distance gluelump
physics that are not present in the free transverse oscillator Hilbert space.
Conversely, the free oscillator labels become useful at large \(L\) only
after a transfer-matrix calculation has isolated the corresponding static
sector and after the effective-string expansion is within its declared
regime.

For a closed flux tube winding a spatial circle, the quadratic theory has
left- and right-moving oscillators.  Define
\[
  N_L=\sum_{i=1}^{c_\perp}\sum_{n\ge1}n\,N^L_{n,i},
  \qquad
  N_R=\sum_{i=1}^{c_\perp}\sum_{n\ge1}n\,N^R_{n,i}.
\]
Translation along the winding circle gives a quantized longitudinal momentum
\[
  p_\parallel=\frac{2\pi q}{L},
  \qquad q\in\mathbb Z,
\]
and the residual worldsheet translation constraint imposes the level-matching
condition
\begin{equation}
  N_L-N_R=q .
  \label{eq:qcd-string-closed-level-matching}
\end{equation}
At Gaussian order the closed-string energy is
\begin{equation}
  E_{N_L,N_R,q}^{\mathrm{closed}}(L)
  =
  \sigma_kL
  +
  \frac{2\pi}{L}
  \left(
    N_L+N_R-\frac{c_\perp}{12}
  \right)
  +O(L^{-3}),
  \label{eq:qcd-string-closed-gaussian-levels}
\end{equation}
with the \(q\)-dependent kinetic contribution first entering at order
\(L^{-3}\) in the large-\(L\) expansion.  The \(N_L=N_R=0\) case recovers
\eqref{eq:qcd-string-closed-luscher}.

In the Nambu--Goto reference theory these oscillator levels are packaged into
the square-root formulas
\begin{align}
  E_N^{\mathrm{NG,open}}(L)
  &=
  \sigma_R L
  \sqrt{
    1+
    \frac{2\pi}{\sigma_RL^2}
    \left(N-\frac{c_\perp}{24}\right)
  },
  \label{eq:qcd-string-ng-open-levels}\\
  E_{N_L,N_R,q}^{\mathrm{NG,closed}}(L)
  &=
  \sigma_k L
  \sqrt{
    1+
    \frac{4\pi}{\sigma_kL^2}
    \left(N_L+N_R-\frac{c_\perp}{12}\right)
    +
    \left(\frac{2\pi q}{\sigma_kL^2}\right)^2
  },
  \label{eq:qcd-string-ng-closed-levels}
\end{align}
with \eqref{eq:qcd-string-closed-level-matching} imposed in the closed case.
Expanding these formulas gives
\begin{align}
  E_N^{\mathrm{NG,open}}(L)
  &=
  \sigma_RL
  +
  \frac{\pi}{L}
  \left(N-\frac{c_\perp}{24}\right)
  -
  \frac{\pi^2}{2\sigma_RL^3}
  \left(N-\frac{c_\perp}{24}\right)^2
  +O(L^{-5}),
  \label{eq:qcd-string-ng-open-level-expansion}\\
  E_{N_L,N_R,q}^{\mathrm{NG,closed}}(L)
  &=
  \sigma_kL
  +
  \frac{2\pi}{L}
  \left(N_L+N_R-\frac{c_\perp}{12}\right)
  \notag\\
  &\quad
  +
  \frac{2\pi^2}{\sigma_kL^3}
  \left[
    q^2-
    \left(N_L+N_R-\frac{c_\perp}{12}\right)^2
  \right]
  +O(L^{-5}).
  \label{eq:qcd-string-ng-closed-level-expansion}
\end{align}
The square-root formulas are useful because they organize a large set of
levels with the same conventions, but the QCD statement is weaker and more
precise: the Gaussian \(1/L\) structure follows from the assumed gapless
transverse modes, while the \(1/L^3\) and later terms are effective-string
matching data unless a universality theorem for the relevant order and
boundary condition has been established.

\subsection{Oscillator Growth and the Flux-String Hagedorn Scale}

The degeneracy of the oscillator levels in
\eqref{eq:qcd-string-open-oscillator-generating} grows exponentially.  This
growth is a statement about the effective long-string Hilbert space.  The
deconfinement transition of the four-dimensional gauge theory is a property of
the thermal gauge-theory transfer matrix and is discussed in Volume~X.  The
calculation here gives the scale at which a gas of arbitrarily long
effective-string states ceases to have a finite canonical partition function
inside the regime where the long-string description is used.

\begin{proposition}[Colored-partition growth and the string Hagedorn scale]
\label{prop:qcd-string-hagedorn-growth}
Let \(p_c(N)\) be the coefficient of \(q^N\) in
\[
  \prod_{n=1}^\infty(1-q^n)^{-c},
  \qquad c\in\mathbb Z_{>0}.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
  \log p_c(N)
  =
  2\pi\sqrt{\frac{cN}{6}}+O(\log N)
  \qquad (N\to\infty).
  \label{eq:qcd-string-colored-partition-asymptotic}
\end{equation}
For the Nambu--Goto reference spectrum of a long confining flux string with
\(c_\perp=D-2\) transverse massless fields and tension \(\sigma\), the
oscillator density has the exponential scale
\begin{equation}
  \rho(E)\sim \exp(\beta_{\rm H}^{\rm ws} E),
  \qquad
  \beta_{\rm H}^{\rm ws}
  =
  \sqrt{\frac{\pi c_\perp}{3\sigma}} .
  \label{eq:qcd-string-worldsheet-hagedorn-beta}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Set \(q=\ee^{-\varepsilon}\), with \(\varepsilon>0\).  The logarithm of the
oscillator generating function is
\[
  -c\sum_{n\ge1}\log(1-\ee^{-n\varepsilon})
  =
  c\sum_{m\ge1}\frac1m\frac{\ee^{-m\varepsilon}}{1-\ee^{-m\varepsilon}} .
\]
As \(\varepsilon\downarrow0\), comparison with the corresponding Riemann sum,
or equivalently the modular transformation of the Dedekind eta function, gives
\[
  \log\prod_{n=1}^{\infty}(1-\ee^{-n\varepsilon})^{-c}
  =
  \frac{\pi^2 c}{6\varepsilon}+O(\log\varepsilon).
  \label{eq:qcd-string-partition-small-epsilon}
\]
Cauchy's coefficient formula writes \(p_c(N)\) as the contour integral of
\(q^{-N-1}\prod_n(1-q^n)^{-c}\).  The exponential part of the integrand on the
positive saddle is
\[
  N\varepsilon+\frac{\pi^2 c}{6\varepsilon}.
\]
The stationary point is
\[
  \varepsilon_*=\pi\sqrt{\frac{c}{6N}},
\]
and the saddle exponent is
\[
  N\varepsilon_*+\frac{\pi^2 c}{6\varepsilon_*}
  =
  2\pi\sqrt{\frac{cN}{6}} .
\]
Gaussian fluctuations and the \(O(\log\varepsilon)\) term in
\eqref{eq:qcd-string-partition-small-epsilon} contribute only logarithmic
corrections to \(\log p_c(N)\), proving
\eqref{eq:qcd-string-colored-partition-asymptotic}.

For an open Nambu--Goto reference string at large excitation number,
\eqref{eq:qcd-string-ng-open-levels} gives
\[
  E^2=2\pi\sigma N+O(N^0)
\]
in the oscillator-dominated regime.  Substituting
\(N=E^2/(2\pi\sigma)+O(1)\) into
\eqref{eq:qcd-string-colored-partition-asymptotic} gives
\[
  \log\rho(E)
  =
  2\pi\sqrt{\frac{c_\perp}{6}\frac{E^2}{2\pi\sigma}}
  +O(\log E)
  =
  E\sqrt{\frac{\pi c_\perp}{3\sigma}}+O(\log E).
\]
For a closed string with level matching at zero longitudinal momentum,
\(N_L=N_R=N\).  The degeneracy is \(p_{c_\perp}(N)^2\), while
\eqref{eq:qcd-string-ng-closed-levels} gives
\[
  E^2=8\pi\sigma N+O(N^0).
\]
The doubled entropy and the doubled energy coefficient combine to the same
\(\beta_{\rm H}^{\rm ws}\).  This proves
\eqref{eq:qcd-string-worldsheet-hagedorn-beta}.
\end{proof}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Flux-tube Hagedorn scale]
\label{ca:qcd-string-hagedorn-interpretation}
Equation~\eqref{eq:qcd-string-worldsheet-hagedorn-beta} is a consequence of
three declared inputs: a stable long flux-tube sector, \(c_\perp\) massless
transverse fields with the oscillator generating function above, and the
Nambu--Goto high-level relation between excitation level and energy.  It is a
worldsheet-density statement.  A four-dimensional deconfinement temperature
requires the thermal gauge-theory path integral, center symmetry and
matter-content data, and the infinite-volume limit.  Equality between a
thermal transition scale and the worldsheet Hagedorn scale is an additional
dynamical statement whose proof would have to relate the thermal transfer
matrix to the long-string density
\eqref{eq:qcd-string-worldsheet-hagedorn-beta}.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\subsection{Static Observables, Lattice Extraction, and the Meaning of
String Tension}

The static potential and the effective string are nonperturbative objects.
Their definition does not use perturbative gluon states.  It uses the Hilbert
space obtained from the gauge theory with external static sources, or
equivalently the transfer matrix acting on gauge-invariant line-operator
states.  On a Euclidean lattice with spacing \(a_{\rm lat}\), a rectangular
Wilson loop is the trace of the ordered product of link variables around the
rectangle.  In the continuum notation used in this chapter it is written
\[
  W_R(C)=\operatorname{tr}_R\,
  \mathcal P\exp\left(i\oint_C A_\mu\,\dd x^\mu\right),
\]
where \(R\) is a representation of the gauge group and
\(\mathcal P\) denotes ordering along the contour.  The continuum expression
is a compact notation for the renormalized line operator obtained from a
chosen regulator; a Wilson loop with cusps or corners has additional local
renormalizations at those singular points.

The area-law statement relevant for the static flux tube is therefore a
statement after local perimeter and corner terms have been separated.  For
large rectangles \(C_{L,T}\), a pure gauge theory in a confining center sector
has
\begin{equation}
  -\log \langle W_R(C_{L,T})\rangle
  =
  \sigma_k LT+\rho_R(L+T)+\kappa_R
  +o(LT)
  \label{eq:qcd-string-rectangular-area-law}
\end{equation}
when both \(L\) and \(T\) are large in a regime where the lowest flux-tube
channel of \(N\)-ality \(k=k_R\) dominates.  The perimeter coefficient
\(\rho_R\) and the corner coefficient \(\kappa_R\) are not the string tension.
They depend on the definition of the line operator and on its ultraviolet
renormalization.  The coefficient \(\sigma_k\) is the asymptotic energy per
unit length of the lowest flux tube in the corresponding center-charge sector.

\begin{proposition}[Equivalence of rectangular area coefficient and static
potential slope]
\label{prop:qcd-string-area-static-equivalence}
Assume the static-source spectral expansion
\eqref{eq:qcd-string-static-source-spectral-expansion}, assume a nonzero
overlap with the lowest state for all sufficiently large \(L\), and assume
that the gap above \(E_0(L)\) is bounded below by a positive function whose
large-\(T\) suppression is uniform in the large-\(L\) window under
consideration.  If
\[
  E_0(L)=\sigma_k L+\mu_R+o(L)
  \qquad (L\to\infty),
\]
then the coefficient of \(LT\) in
\(-\log\langle W_R(C_{L,T})\rangle\), with \(T\to\infty\) taken before the
large-\(L\) slope, is \(\sigma_k\).  Conversely, if the rectangular Wilson
loop has the form \eqref{eq:qcd-string-rectangular-area-law} with a
controlled transfer-matrix limit at each fixed \(L\), then
\[
  \lim_{L\to\infty}\frac{E_0(L)}{L}=\sigma_k .
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Write the spectral expansion in the form
\[
  \langle W_R(C_{L,T})\rangle
  =
  c_0(L)\ee^{-E_0(L)T}
  \left[
    1+
    \sum_{\alpha>0}\frac{c_\alpha(L)}{c_0(L)}
    \ee^{-(E_\alpha(L)-E_0(L))T}
  \right],
\]
where \(c_0(L)\ne0\) by hypothesis.  The uniform gap assumption implies that
the logarithm of the bracket divided by \(T\) vanishes as \(T\to\infty\), so
\[
  -\lim_{T\to\infty}\frac1T
  \log \langle W_R(C_{L,T})\rangle
  =
  E_0(L).
\]
If \(E_0(L)=\sigma_kL+\mu_R+o(L)\), the coefficient multiplying \(LT\) in the
large-rectangle logarithm is \(\sigma_k\); the \(L\)-independent endpoint
energy \(\mu_R\), the overlap \(c_0(L)\), perimeter terms, and corner terms
do not contribute to the double slope
\(\lim_{L\to\infty}L^{-1}\lim_{T\to\infty}T^{-1}(-\log\langle W\rangle)\).
The converse is the same identity read in the opposite direction: the
transfer-matrix limit extracts \(E_0(L)\), and the assumed rectangular area
coefficient fixes the large-\(L\) slope of this extracted energy.
\end{proof}

On a Euclidean time circle of circumference \(\beta\), the corresponding
static observable is the Polyakov loop
\[
  P_R(\mathbf x)=
  \operatorname{tr}_R\,
  \mathcal P\exp\left(i\int_0^\beta A_0(\tau,\mathbf x)\,\dd\tau\right).
\]
The two-source free energy is defined by
\[
  F_R(L;\beta)
  =
  -\frac1\beta
  \log
  \langle P_R(\mathbf 0)^\dagger P_R(\mathbf L)\rangle_\beta .
\]
When the zero-temperature transfer-matrix limit is taken by sending
\(\beta\to\infty\), \(F_R(L;\beta)\) approaches the same static energy
extracted from a long rectangular Wilson loop, up to the vacuum-energy and
line-renormalization conventions used in defining the loop.  At finite
temperature in pure Yang--Mills theory, the expectation value of a single
fundamental Polyakov loop is charged under the temporal center symmetry and is
therefore an order parameter for that finite-temperature symmetry after the
infinite-volume limit is specified.  This is related to, but not identical
with, the zero-temperature string tension \(\sigma_k\).  The latter is a
property of the large-distance static-source spectrum.

In practical lattice calculations one does not measure
\(\sigma_k\) by fitting a bare Wilson loop alone.  One constructs a family of
gauge-invariant operators in the same static-source sector, computes their
Euclidean correlation matrix, and uses a variational transfer-matrix problem
to isolate the lowest and excited energies.  The effective string expansion
then describes the large-\(L\) behavior of these extracted energies.  This is
the operational reason that the QCD string is a nonperturbative observable:
it is a statement about the spectrum selected by gauge-invariant line
operators, not about perturbative gluons propagating between color charges.

\subsection{Baryonic Flux Networks}

Baryonic confinement is not a copy of the mesonic static potential with one
more endpoint.  In an \(SU(N_c)\) gauge theory a gauge-invariant static baryon
operator is made by joining \(N_c\) fundamental Wilson lines to a common color
junction and contracting their color indices with
\(\epsilon_{i_1\cdots i_{N_c}}\).  For paths
\(\Gamma_r\) running from a junction point \(y\) to source positions
\(\mathbf x_r\),
\[
  \mathcal B_{\Gamma_1,\ldots,\Gamma_{N_c}}
  =
  \epsilon_{i_1\cdots i_{N_c}}
  U(\Gamma_1)^{i_1}{}_{j_1}\cdots
  U(\Gamma_{N_c})^{i_{N_c}}{}_{j_{N_c}}
  Q^{j_1}(\mathbf x_1)\cdots Q^{j_{N_c}}(\mathbf x_{N_c}) .
\]
Here \(Q^j(\mathbf x_r)\) denotes a static fundamental source insertion; it
is not a dynamical asymptotic quark state.
The determinant-one property of \(SU(N_c)\) makes the contraction at the
junction gauge invariant.  For \(N_c=3\), and for source separations large
compared with the inverse mass gap, the leading string model predicts an
energy proportional to the length of the minimal three-pronged network, not
to a unique pairwise potential.  Endpoint and junction energies are local
terms and must be separated from the coefficient of the large lengths:
\begin{equation}
  V_{3Q}(\mathbf x_1,\mathbf x_2,\mathbf x_3)
  =
  \sigma\,L_Y(\mathbf x_1,\mathbf x_2,\mathbf x_3)
  +\mu_1+\mu_2+\mu_3+\mu_J+o(L_Y).
  \label{eq:qcd-string-baryon-y-potential}
\end{equation}

\begin{proposition}[Steiner length for a three-source baryonic string]
\label{prop:qcd-string-steiner-y-length}
Let \(a=|\mathbf x_2-\mathbf x_3|\),
\(b=|\mathbf x_3-\mathbf x_1|\), and
\(c=|\mathbf x_1-\mathbf x_2|\) be the side lengths of a Euclidean triangle,
and let \(\Delta\) be its area.  If every angle of the triangle is less than
\(2\pi/3\), the length minimizing
\(\sum_{r=1}^3|\mathbf y-\mathbf x_r|\) is realized by a point
\(\mathbf y_F\) from which the three segments meet at angles \(2\pi/3\), and
\begin{equation}
  L_Y^2
  =
  \frac12
  \left(
    a^2+b^2+c^2+4\sqrt3\,\Delta
  \right).
  \label{eq:qcd-string-steiner-length-formula}
\end{equation}
If one angle is at least \(2\pi/3\), the minimizing network collapses to the
two sides adjacent to that angle.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For an interior minimizer \(\mathbf y_F\), vary
\(\mathbf y\mapsto \mathbf y+\delta\mathbf y\).  The first variation of
\(\sum_r|\mathbf y-\mathbf x_r|\) is
\[
  \delta\mathbf y\cdot
  \sum_{r=1}^3
  \frac{\mathbf y_F-\mathbf x_r}
       {|\mathbf y_F-\mathbf x_r|}.
\]
It vanishes for all \(\delta\mathbf y\) precisely when the three unit vectors
from the sources to the junction sum to zero.  Three unit vectors sum to zero
only when their pairwise angles are \(2\pi/3\).

Set \(r_i=|\mathbf y_F-\mathbf x_i|\).  Because the angles at the junction are
\(2\pi/3\),
\[
  a^2=r_2^2+r_3^2+r_2r_3,\qquad
  b^2=r_3^2+r_1^2+r_3r_1,\qquad
  c^2=r_1^2+r_2^2+r_1r_2 .
\]
Also the total area is the sum of the three triangles with common vertex
\(\mathbf y_F\):
\[
  \Delta
  =
  \frac{\sqrt3}{4}
  (r_1r_2+r_2r_3+r_3r_1).
\]
Therefore
\[
  \frac12(a^2+b^2+c^2+4\sqrt3\,\Delta)
  =
  r_1^2+r_2^2+r_3^2
  +2(r_1r_2+r_2r_3+r_3r_1)
  =
  (r_1+r_2+r_3)^2 ,
\]
which proves \eqref{eq:qcd-string-steiner-length-formula}.  If an angle is
at least \(2\pi/3\), the stationarity condition cannot be realized by a point
inside the triangle with all three meeting angles \(2\pi/3\).  The convexity
of the sum of distances then places the minimum on the boundary; reducing the
same one-dimensional problem along the boundary gives the vertex at the large
angle, and the network is the union of the two adjacent sides.
\end{proof}

Figure~\ref{fig:qcd-string-baryonic-y-network} illustrates the Steiner-network
length entering the baryonic flux-string model: three strings meet at
\(2\pi/3\) when the Fermat point lies inside the source triangle, and otherwise
the minimum lies on the boundary.

\begin{figure}[H]
  \centering
  \begin{tikzpicture}[x=1cm,y=1cm,every node/.style={font=\scriptsize}]
    \coordinate (A) at (-2.2,-1.0);
    \coordinate (B) at (2.2,-1.0);
    \coordinate (C) at (0.35,1.65);
    \coordinate (F) at (0.05,-0.05);
    \draw[gray!70,thick] (A)--(B)--(C)--cycle;
    \draw[purple!75!black,very thick] (F)--(A);
    \draw[purple!75!black,very thick] (F)--(B);
    \draw[purple!75!black,very thick] (F)--(C);
    \fill[blue!75!black] (A) circle (2.6pt);
    \fill[blue!75!black] (B) circle (2.6pt);
    \fill[blue!75!black] (C) circle (2.6pt);
    \fill[purple!80!black] (F) circle (2.4pt);
    \node[below left] at (A) {\(\mathbf x_1\)};
    \node[below right] at (B) {\(\mathbf x_2\)};
    \node[above] at (C) {\(\mathbf x_3\)};
    \node[right,purple!80!black] at (F) {\(\mathbf y_F\)};
    \draw[->,gray!70] ($(F)+(0.45,-0.15)$) arc[start angle=-18,end angle=-138,radius=0.47];
    \draw[->,gray!70] ($(F)+(-0.25,0.39)$) arc[start angle=122,end angle=2,radius=0.47];
    \node[gray!80!black] at (-0.55,-0.48) {\(2\pi/3\)};
    \node[gray!80!black] at (0.58,0.42) {\(2\pi/3\)};
    \node[purple!75!black,align=center] at (0,-1.65)
      {\(L_Y=|\mathbf y_F-\mathbf x_1|+
      |\mathbf y_F-\mathbf x_2|+|\mathbf y_F-\mathbf x_3|\)};
  \end{tikzpicture}
  \caption{For three static fundamental sources in pure \(SU(3)\) Yang--Mills
  theory, the long-distance baryonic string model uses a gauge-invariant
  color junction.  When all triangle angles are below \(2\pi/3\), the leading
  network is the Steiner tree whose three segments meet at \(2\pi/3\).}
  \label{fig:qcd-string-baryonic-y-network}
\end{figure}

For an equilateral triangle of side \(a\),
\eqref{eq:qcd-string-steiner-length-formula} gives
\[
  L_Y=\sqrt3\,a .
\]
The frequently used pairwise comparison length
\[
  L_\Delta=\frac12(a+b+c)
\]
would give \(L_\Delta=3a/2\) in the same equilateral geometry.  These are
different large-distance hypotheses for the static baryon sector, not two
forms of the same formula.  The gauge-invariant object in the baryonic
Wilson-line construction contains a junction, and the effective string
description must decide, by matching to the gauge theory, whether the
long-distance energy is governed by a junction network, by an approximately
pairwise regime over the available distances, or by a crossover between the
two.

\subsection{Closed Flux Tubes, Glueball Channels, and Large-N String Coupling}

A closed flux tube is cleanly defined on a spatial torus by a spatial
Polyakov loop winding a noncontractible cycle,
\[
  \mathcal P_R(\tau)
  =
  \operatorname{tr}_R\,
  \mathcal P\exp\left(i\oint_{S^1_L}A_i(\tau,\mathbf x)\,\dd x^i\right).
\]
Its Euclidean time correlator has a transfer-matrix expansion
\[
  \langle \mathcal P_R(\tau)^\dagger\mathcal P_R(0)\rangle
  =
  \sum_n
  |\langle n;k,L|\mathcal P_R(0)\vac\rangle|^2
  \ee^{-E_n^{(k)}(L)\tau},
\]
where \(k\) is the center charge of \(R\).  The closed-string formulas
\eqref{eq:qcd-string-closed-luscher},
\eqref{eq:qcd-string-closed-gaussian-levels}, and
\eqref{eq:qcd-string-ng-closed-levels} apply to this winding sector under the
large-\(L\) effective-string hypotheses stated above.

This winding-sector statement is sharper than the phrase ``glueballs are
closed strings.''  A glueball is a state in the vacuum sector created by local
gauge-invariant operators such as
\(\operatorname{tr}(F_{\mu\nu}F^{\mu\nu})\) and
\(\operatorname{tr}(F_{\mu\nu}\widetilde F^{\mu\nu})\).  A noncontractible
winding flux tube belongs to a different finite-volume sector.  A
contractible closed flux loop, by contrast, can shrink to a size of order
\(\sigma^{-1/2}\), where the long-string derivative expansion is no longer
controlled.  Thus the closed-string picture of glueball spectra and Regge
trajectories is a dynamical large-\(N_c\) and effective-string hypothesis, not
a consequence of the Gaussian Luscher calculation.  What is nonperturbatively
well defined are the gauge-invariant correlators and their spectral
decomposition; the string interpretation is an additional infrared
organization whose range must be tested or derived.

Large \(N_c\) supplies the natural weak-coupling parameter for such a string
interpretation once a confining flux-tube spectrum exists.  The ribbon-graph
counting in the preceding section gives a connected contribution of order
\[
  N_c^{2-2h-b}
\]
for a surface of genus \(h\) with \(b\) color-trace boundaries before any
chosen normalization of the external loop operators.  A handle is therefore
suppressed by \(N_c^{-2}\).  Identifying the closed-string genus expansion as
\(g_s^{2h-2}\) gives the parametric relation
\[
  g_s\sim \frac1{N_c}.
\]
The same counting implies that splitting and joining processes of normalized
closed-string states carry the corresponding factors of \(N_c^{-1}\) fixed by
the number of topology-changing vertices.  This statement is a consequence of
color topology; it is not a derivation of the worldsheet action.  The
microscopic input still required is the existence of a
confining large-\(N_c\) gauge theory with isolated flux-tube and glueball
states in the relevant channels.

Three-dimensional confining gauge theories are especially clean testbeds for
the same logic.  In \(D=3\) there is a single transverse displacement field,
so the universal terms become
\[
  \Delta E_0^{\mathrm{open}}(L)=-\frac{\pi}{24L},
  \qquad
  \Delta E_0^{\mathrm{closed}}(L)=-\frac{\pi}{6L}.
\]
The reduced transverse symmetry makes the lattice spectral assignments less
crowded than in four dimensions, while the effective-string expansion has the
same conceptual structure: line operators define the sector, the transfer
matrix extracts energies, the free transverse field gives the universal
Casimir term, and later coefficients encode symmetry constraints and
microscopic matching.

With dynamical fundamental quarks the fundamental one-form symmetry is
explicitly broken.  The static-source Hilbert space then contains states made
from two color-singlet static-light mesons, and the ground-state energy at very
large \(L\) approaches the two-meson threshold rather than growing without
bound.  A flux tube can still be a well-defined long-lived state over a range
of \(L\), and its worldsheet effective theory can describe the corresponding
resonant or metastable channel, but the limiting string tension
\eqref{eq:qcd-string-tension-definition} is no longer an order parameter in the
same sense as in pure Yang--Mills theory.  This distinction is essential when
using string language in QCD: line operators, static-source sectors, and
calorimetric observables are physical, and asymptotic final states are
color-singlet hadrons.

\section{Heavy-Quark Effective Theory and the Wilson-Line Limit}
\label{sec:qcd-hqet-wilson-line-limit}

The static-source sector just described is also the first term in a
controlled expansion for a dynamical quark whose mass is much larger than the
hadronic scale.  This expansion is called heavy-quark effective theory
(HQET).  Its mathematical content is the regulator-dependent comparison of
gauge-invariant QCD matrix elements with gauge-invariant matrix elements of a
local expansion in inverse powers of the heavy mass.  The heavy quark is still
a colored field variable, so physical matrix elements are made gauge invariant
by the same Wilson-line and color-singlet constructions used elsewhere in this
chapter.

Throughout this section the spacetime metric is mostly plus,
\(\eta_{\mu\nu}=\operatorname{diag}(-,+,+,+)\).  A heavy-quark velocity is a
future-directed timelike unit vector \(v^\mu\) satisfying \(v^2=-1\).  The
orthogonal projector onto the three-plane transverse to \(v\) is
\begin{equation}
  \Pi_v{}^\mu{}_\nu=\delta^\mu{}_\nu+v^\mu v_\nu,
  \qquad
  D_\perp^\mu=\Pi_v{}^\mu{}_\nu D^\nu .
  \label{eq:hqet-transverse-projector}
\end{equation}
The identity \(v_\mu D_\perp^\mu=0\) follows immediately from \(v^2=-1\).  A
near-mass-shell heavy momentum is written
\begin{equation}
  p^\mu=m_Qv^\mu+k^\mu ,
  \label{eq:hqet-momentum-split}
\end{equation}
where \(m_Q\) is the heavy-quark mass coordinate in the chosen regulated QCD
Lagrangian and the residual momentum \(k^\mu\) is required to be small
compared with \(m_Q\) on the states or test functions under consideration.
The split is not unique: replacing \(v\) by \(v+\delta v\), with
\(v\cdot\delta v=0\) to first order, and replacing \(k\) by \(k-m_Q\delta v\)
leaves \(p\) fixed.  This elementary redundancy is the kinematic origin of
reparametrization constraints on the effective action.

Let \(\gamma_v=\gamma_\mu v^\mu\).  Since \(\gamma_v^2=-1\), the operator
\(\ii\gamma_v\) has eigenvalues \(\pm1\), and
\begin{equation}
  P_v^\pm=\frac12(1\pm\ii\gamma_v)
  \label{eq:hqet-spin-projectors}
\end{equation}
are complementary spinor projections.  The sign in
\eqref{eq:hqet-spin-projectors} is tied to the phase convention below.  Define
\(\tau_v(x)=-v\cdot x\); in the rest frame \(v=(1,0,0,0)\), this is the
ordinary time coordinate.  A heavy Dirac field \(Q\) is decomposed at fixed
velocity by
\begin{equation}
  Q(x)=\ee^{-\ii m_Q\tau_v(x)}\bigl(h_v(x)+H_v(x)\bigr),
  \qquad
  P_v^+h_v=h_v,\qquad P_v^-H_v=H_v .
  \label{eq:hqet-field-split}
\end{equation}
The phase removes the rest-energy oscillation associated with \(m_Qv^\mu\).
The field \(H_v\) carries the complementary Dirac components and is separated
from \(h_v\) by a gap of order \(m_Q\) in the free theory.

\begin{definition}[HQET regulator datum]
\label{def:hqet-regulator-datum}
A finite-cutoff HQET datum at velocity \(v\) consists of the following data.
\begin{enumerate}
  \item A gauge-covariant ultraviolet regulator for QCD with the heavy field
  \(Q\) and mass coordinate \(m_Q\), together with an infrared domain of states
  or test functions whose residual momenta obey \(|k|/m_Q\le\varepsilon\ll1\).
  \item The projected field \(h_v=P_v^+h_v\), transforming in the fundamental
  representation of the gauge group, and a Wilsonian procedure which
  integrates out \(H_v\) and modes whose virtuality is of order \(m_Q\).
  \item A local gauge-covariant action
  \begin{equation}
    S_{\rm HQET}^{(N)}[h_v,A]
    =
    \int \bar h_v\,\ii v\cdot D\,h_v\,\dd^4x
    +\sum_{r=1}^N\frac1{(2m_Q)^r}
      \sum_a C_{r,a}(\mu,m_Q)\int \mathcal O_{r,a}(x)\,\dd^4x ,
    \label{eq:hqet-local-action}
  \end{equation}
  where each \(\mathcal O_{r,a}\) is a local gauge-invariant density built
  from \(h_v,\bar h_v,F_{\mu\nu}\), and transverse covariant derivatives
  \(D_\perp\), modulo equations of motion and integration by parts in the
  chosen coordinate system on local functionals.
  \item Renormalized composite operators, for example
  \[
    \bar q\,\Gamma Q
    \longmapsto
    \sum_{r,a}\frac1{(2m_Q)^r}C_{\Gamma,r,a}(\mu,m_Q)\,
    \mathcal J_{\Gamma,r,a}^{\rm HQET}[q,h_v,A],
  \]
  with the same regulator and subtraction data.  A current matching statement
  is a statement about matrix elements of these renormalized operators, not an
  identity between classical monomials.
\end{enumerate}
The leading action is normalized so that the coefficient of
\(\bar h_v\ii v\cdot D h_v\) is one.  The first dimension-five operators may
be represented by
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal O_{\rm kin}=\bar h_vD_{\perp\mu}D_\perp^\mu h_v,
  \qquad
  \mathcal O_{\rm mag}=\bar h_v\sigma_{\mu\nu}F^{\mu\nu}h_v ,
  \label{eq:hqet-dimension-five-operators}
\end{equation}
with coefficients fixed by the chosen matching convention.  In a
reparametrization-compatible scheme the coefficient of the kinetic operator is
fixed relative to the leading term; the chromomagnetic coefficient is a
genuine short-distance matching coefficient.
\end{definition}

The leading HQET equation is the equation for parallel transport along the
heavy-quark worldline.  This is the precise sense in which an infinitely heavy
quark becomes a Wilson line.

\begin{proposition}[Static propagator as a Wilson line]
\label{prop:hqet-static-propagator-wilson-line}
Let \(x(s)=x_0+sv\), and let
\begin{equation}
  W_v(s_2,s_1)=\mathcal P\exp\left\{
    \ii\int_{s_1}^{s_2}v^\mu A_\mu^a(x(s))t_\square^a\,\dd s
  \right\}
  \label{eq:hqet-worldline-wilson-line}
\end{equation}
be the fundamental Wilson transporter along the heavy trajectory.  At finite
regulator and with background \(A_\mu\) smooth on the scale of the regulator,
the retarded Green kernel of the leading HQET operator on this trajectory is
\begin{equation}
  G_v(s_2,s_1)=\theta(s_2-s_1)\,W_v(s_2,s_1)\,P_v^+ ,
  \label{eq:hqet-static-green-kernel}
\end{equation}
up to the conventional overall factor fixed by the normalization of the
first-order inverse.  In particular, every gauge-invariant heavy-light or
heavy-heavy correlator at leading power contains the Wilson line carried by
the heavy source.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The transporter satisfies the initial-value problem
\[
  \frac{\dd}{\dd s_2}W_v(s_2,s_1)
  =
  \ii v^\mu A_\mu^a(x(s_2))t_\square^a W_v(s_2,s_1),
  \qquad W_v(s_1,s_1)=\mathbf 1 .
\]
Equivalently \(v\cdot D_{x(s_2)}W_v(s_2,s_1)=0\), using the chapter
convention \(D_\mu=\partial_\mu-\ii A_\mu\).  Applying the first-order operator
to \(\theta(s_2-s_1)W_v(s_2,s_1)P_v^+\) gives only the derivative of the step
function, because the covariant derivative annihilates the transporter for
\(s_2\ne s_1\).  This is the delta distribution on the oriented line.  The
projector \(P_v^+\) records the spinor components retained in the heavy field.
Gauge covariance follows from the endpoint transformation law of the same
Wilson transporter proven for light-ray operators in
Proposition~\ref{prop:qcd-light-ray-gauge-covariance}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Static spin and flavor symmetry]
\label{prop:hqet-static-spin-flavor}
Consider \(N_h\) heavy flavors whose masses have been removed by separate
phases and whose residual dynamics are described by the leading HQET action at
the same velocity \(v\).  The leading action
\[
  S_0=\sum_{A=1}^{N_h}\int \bar h_{v,A}\,\ii v\cdot D\,h_{v,A}\,\dd^4x
\]
is invariant under unitary rotations of the heavy-flavor labels and under
unitary rotations of the projected spin components commuting with \(P_v^+\).
These symmetries act on the heavy variables alone and leave the gauge and
light-quark fields fixed.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The operator \(\ii v\cdot D\) is scalar in the heavy-flavor labels and
contains no gamma matrix acting inside the projected spin space.  If
\(h_{v,A}\mapsto U_A{}^B Sh_{v,B}\), where \(U\) is a unitary matrix on flavor
labels and \(S\) is unitary on the image of \(P_v^+\), then
\(\bar h_{v,A}\ii v\cdot D h_{v,A}\) is unchanged after summing over \(A\).
The Wilson-line form of the propagator makes the same statement in correlator
language: at leading power the heavy source transports color, while its spin
and heavy-flavor labels are parallel spectators.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Free residual dispersion and the kinetic operator]
\label{prop:hqet-residual-dispersion}
For a free heavy particle with \(p^\mu=m_Qv^\mu+k^\mu\) and \(p^2+m_Q^2=0\),
the residual momentum obeys
\begin{equation}
  2m_Q\,v\cdot k+k^2=0 .
  \label{eq:hqet-onshell-residual}
\end{equation}
In the rest frame, writing \(k^\mu=(E_{\rm res},\mathbf k)\), this gives
\begin{equation}
  E_{\rm res}
  =
  \sqrt{m_Q^2+|\mathbf k|^2}-m_Q
  =
  \frac{|\mathbf k|^2}{2m_Q}
  -\frac{|\mathbf k|^4}{8m_Q^3}
  +O\!\left(\frac{|\mathbf k|^6}{m_Q^5}\right).
  \label{eq:hqet-free-dispersion}
\end{equation}
Thus the first correction to the static theory is the transverse kinetic
energy.  Gauge covariance promotes the transverse momentum to \(D_\perp\),
giving the operator \(\mathcal O_{\rm kin}\) in
\eqref{eq:hqet-dimension-five-operators}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Substituting \(p=m_Qv+k\) and \(v^2=-1\) into \(p^2+m_Q^2=0\) gives
\eqref{eq:hqet-onshell-residual}.  In the rest frame,
\(p=(m_Q+E_{\rm res},\mathbf k)\), so the positive-energy solution is
\(m_Q+E_{\rm res}=\sqrt{m_Q^2+|\mathbf k|^2}\).  Expanding the square root in
\(|\mathbf k|^2/m_Q^2\) gives \eqref{eq:hqet-free-dispersion}.  The covariant
operator statement follows from replacing the residual transverse momentum by
the transverse covariant derivative in the local Wilsonian expansion; the
coefficient is fixed by matching the free dispersion and, in an interacting
reparametrization-compatible scheme, by the invariance of the momentum split
\eqref{eq:hqet-momentum-split}.
\end{proof}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Meaning of the heavy-mass expansion]
\label{ca:hqet-heavy-mass-expansion}
Fix a regulator, a velocity \(v\), a renormalization scale \(\mu\ll m_Q\), and
a class of gauge-invariant external states and operator insertions whose
residual momenta and invariant hadronic scales are bounded by
\(\Lambda_{\rm had}\).  A truncation of HQET at order \(N\) asserts an
estimate of the form
\[
  \left|
  \langle \mathcal O\rangle_{\rm QCD}
  -
  \langle \mathcal O^{(N)}_{\rm HQET}\rangle_{\rm HQET}
  \right|
  \le
  C_{\mathcal O,N}
  \left(\frac{\Lambda_{\rm had}}{m_Q}\right)^{N+1}
\]
for the chosen smeared matrix elements, after the QCD operator and the HQET
operator have been matched in the same renormalization scheme.  The constant
\(C_{\mathcal O,N}\), the topology in which the estimate is meant, and the
range of \(\mu\) are part of the assertion.  The Wilson-line limit
Proposition~\ref{prop:hqet-static-propagator-wilson-line} supplies the
leading operator structure; the existence of a uniform heavy-mass expansion
for a specified family of hadronic matrix elements is additional dynamical and
renormalization information.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\section{Heavy-Light Currents and Heavy-Quark Symmetry}
\label{sec:qcd-hqet-heavy-light-currents}

The static Wilson-line limit becomes predictive only after composite currents
and hadron states are matched.  Let \(q\) be a light quark field and let
\(Q\) be a heavy quark field.  The mostly-plus spinor convention of
Definition~\ref{def:four-dimensional-mostly-plus-spinor-convention} fixes the
Hermitian vector and axial currents with an explicit factor of \(\ii\).  Thus
in this section
\[
  A^\mu_{qQ}=\ii[\bar q\gamma^\mu\gamma_5Q]_{\rm R},
  \qquad
  V^\mu_{qQ}=\ii[\bar q\gamma^\mu Q]_{\rm R}.
\]
More generally a renormalized heavy-light QCD current is a renormalized
gauge-invariant local operator
\[
  J_\Gamma^{\rm QCD}(x)=[\kappa_\Gamma\bar q(x)\Gamma Q(x)]_{\rm R},
\]
where \(\Gamma\) is a fixed spinor matrix, \(\kappa_\Gamma\in\{1,\ii\}\) is
part of the current convention, and the subscript records the regulator and
subtraction convention.  In HQET this current is represented by an expansion
\begin{equation}
  J_\Gamma^{\rm QCD}
  =
  C_\Gamma(m_Q,\mu)\,[\kappa_\Gamma\bar q\Gamma h_v]_{\rm R}
  +
  \sum_a\frac{B_{\Gamma,a}(m_Q,\mu)}{2m_Q}\,
  \mathcal J_{\Gamma,a}^{(1)}
  +O(m_Q^{-2})
  \label{eq:hqet-current-matching}
\end{equation}
inside the chosen class of matrix elements.  The operators
\(\mathcal J_{\Gamma,a}^{(1)}\) are local gauge-invariant HQET currents with
one additional transverse derivative, chromomagnetic insertion, or light-quark
mass insertion, modulo the leading equations of motion in the chosen operator
basis.  Equation \eqref{eq:hqet-current-matching} is a matching statement for
renormalized operator-valued distributions tested on low-residual-momentum
states.

Assume that for a heavy flavor \(Q\) there is an isolated stable pseudoscalar
meson \(P_Q\) and an isolated stable vector meson \(V_Q\) in the same
light-cloud channel.  Their decay constants are defined by
\begin{align}
  \langle 0|\,A^\mu_{qQ}\,|P_Q(p)\rangle
  &=
  f_{P_Q}\,p^\mu,
  \label{eq:hqet-pseudoscalar-decay-constant}\\
  \langle 0|\,V^\mu_{qQ}\,|V_Q(p,\varepsilon)\rangle
  &=
  f_{V_Q}\,M_{V_Q}\,\varepsilon^\mu,
  \label{eq:hqet-vector-decay-constant}
\end{align}
where \(p^2=-M^2\), \(p^0>0\), and the vector polarization satisfies
\(p\cdot\varepsilon=0\).  Momentum eigenstates in QCD are normalized by
\[
  \langle H(p')|H(p)\rangle
  =
  2p^0(2\pi)^3\delta^3(\mathbf p-\mathbf p').
\]
The corresponding HQET residual-momentum state is normalized by
\[
  {}_{\rm HQET}\langle H_v(k')|H_v(k)\rangle_{\rm HQET}
  =
  2v^0(2\pi)^3\delta^3(\mathbf k-\mathbf k'),
\]
with \(p^\mu=M_Hv^\mu+k^\mu\), and the leading state matching is
\begin{equation}
  |H_Q(p=M_Hv+k)\rangle_{\rm QCD}
  =
  \sqrt{M_H}\,|H_v(k)\rangle_{\rm HQET}
  +O(\Lambda_{\rm had}/m_Q)
  \label{eq:hqet-state-normalization-matching}
\end{equation}
for matrix elements in the stated residual-momentum domain.

\begin{proposition}[Heavy-light decay-constant scaling]
\label{prop:hqet-decay-constant-scaling}
Let
\[
  {}_{\rm HQET}\langle0|\,\ii[\bar q\gamma^\mu\gamma_5h_v]_{\rm R}
  |P_v(0)\rangle_{\rm HQET}
  =
  F_P(\mu)\,v^\mu .
\]
Then the leading HQET matching of the axial current gives
\begin{equation}
  f_{P_Q}\sqrt{M_{P_Q}}
  =
  C_A(m_Q,\mu)F_P(\mu)
  +O(\Lambda_{\rm had}/m_Q).
  \label{eq:hqet-decay-constant-scaling}
\end{equation}
The analogous vector-meson relation has the same static reduced matrix
element up to the spin rotation dictated by
Proposition~\ref{prop:hqet-static-spin-flavor}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
At \(p^\mu=M_{P_Q}v^\mu\), the QCD definition
\eqref{eq:hqet-pseudoscalar-decay-constant} gives
\[
  \langle0|A^\mu_{qQ}|P_Q(p)\rangle_{\rm QCD}
  =
  f_{P_Q}M_{P_Q}v^\mu .
\]
Using the leading current matching
\[
  A^\mu_{qQ}
  =
  C_A(m_Q,\mu)\,\ii[\bar q\gamma^\mu\gamma_5h_v]_{\rm R}
  +O(m_Q^{-1})
\]
and the state relation \eqref{eq:hqet-state-normalization-matching} gives
\[
  \langle0|A^\mu_{qQ}|P_Q(p)\rangle_{\rm QCD}
  =
  C_A\sqrt{M_{P_Q}}\,
  F_P(\mu)v^\mu
  +O(\Lambda_{\rm had}/m_Q).
\]
Equating the coefficients of \(v^\mu\) proves
\eqref{eq:hqet-decay-constant-scaling}.  The vector statement follows because
the leading static action transports color but contains no operator acting on
the projected heavy spin; pseudoscalar and vector states in the same light
cloud are related by the heavy-spin symmetry of the leading theory.
\end{proof}

Heavy-to-heavy currents compare two static sectors with velocities \(v\) and
\(v'\).  Define the recoil variable
\begin{equation}
  w=-v\cdot v'\ge1 .
  \label{eq:hqet-recoil-variable}
\end{equation}
For pseudoscalar ground-state mesons in the same light-cloud channel, the
leading HQET vector-current matrix element has the form
\begin{equation}
  {}_{\rm HQET}\langle H_{v'}|\,
  \mathcal V_{Q'Q}^\mu(v',v)\,|H_v\rangle_{\rm HQET}
  =
  \xi(w)(v+v')^\mu ,
  \label{eq:hqet-isgur-wise-definition}
\end{equation}
where
\[
  \mathcal V_{Q'Q}^\mu(v',v)
  =
  \ii[\bar h_{v'}^{(Q')}\gamma^\mu h_v^{(Q)}]_{\rm R}
\]
with the coefficient fixed by coupling the leading HQET action to a background
heavy-flavor gauge field.  The scalar function \(\xi\) is the leading
heavy-quark symmetry form factor.  For the full QCD states this corresponds to
\begin{equation}
  \begin{aligned}
  &\langle H_{Q'}(M_{Q'}v')|\,\ii[\bar Q'\gamma^\mu Q]_{\rm R}\,
  |H_Q(M_Qv)\rangle
  \\
  &\qquad =
  \sqrt{M_{Q'}M_Q}\,
  C_{Q'Q}(m_{Q'},m_Q,\mu)\,
  \xi(w)(v+v')^\mu
  +O(\Lambda_{\rm had}/m_Q,\Lambda_{\rm had}/m_{Q'}).
  \end{aligned}
  \label{eq:hqet-heavy-to-heavy-qcd-form-factor}
\end{equation}
More general spin states are obtained from the same light-cloud overlap by
inserting the appropriate heavy-spin trace factors.

\begin{proposition}[Zero-recoil normalization]
\label{prop:hqet-isgur-wise-normalization}
At zero recoil, \(v'=v\), the leading heavy-quark symmetry form factor obeys
\begin{equation}
  \xi(1)=1
  \label{eq:hqet-isgur-wise-normalization}
\end{equation}
when the current is normalized as the generator of the heavy-flavor symmetry
of the leading HQET action.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
At \(v'=v\), the leading HQET action has a unitary flavor symmetry rotating
the heavy labels \(Q\) and \(Q'\) while leaving the light fields and gauge
field fixed.  Couple this symmetry to a smooth background matrix-valued
connection \(B_\mu{}^A{}_B\) by replacing
\(D_\mu h_{v,A}\) with
\((D_\mu\delta_A{}^B-\ii B_\mu{}^B{}_A)h_{v,B}\).  Differentiation of the
action with respect to \(B_\mu{}^Q{}_{Q'}\) defines the current
\(\mathcal V^\mu_{Q'Q}(v,v)\), and the associated charge
\[
  Q_{Q'Q}
  =
  \int_{\Sigma_t}\dd^3x\,n_\mu\,\mathcal V^\mu_{Q'Q}(v,v)
\]
is the generator of the heavy-flavor rotation on the one-heavy-particle
sector.  Here \(n_\mu\) is the future unit normal covector to the quantization
slice, and the state normalization above fixes the matrix element of
\(Q_{Q'Q}\) between one-particle velocity states to be one.  Therefore
\(Q_{Q'Q}|H_v^{(Q)}\rangle=|H_v^{(Q')}\rangle\) after the same phase convention
for the two states is chosen.  Covariance in the fixed-velocity sector then
gives
\[
  {}_{\rm HQET}\langle H_v^{(Q')}|
  \mathcal V^\mu_{Q'Q}(v,v)
  |H_v^{(Q)}\rangle_{\rm HQET}
  =
  2v^\mu .
\]
Comparing with \eqref{eq:hqet-isgur-wise-definition} at \(v'=v\) gives
\(\xi(1)=1\).
\end{proof}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Heavy-light current expansion]
\label{ca:hqet-heavy-light-current-expansion}
A heavy-light or heavy-to-heavy form-factor prediction must specify the
renormalized QCD current, the HQET current basis, the state normalization, the
matching coefficients, and the spectral assumption that the meson states used
in the matrix element are isolated in the relevant channel.  The leading
relations \eqref{eq:hqet-decay-constant-scaling} and
\eqref{eq:hqet-isgur-wise-definition} are symmetry consequences of the static
theory after these data are fixed.  Corrections of order \(1/m_Q\) are matrix
elements of the subleading current operators and of insertions from the
subleading HQET action; their absence or suppression at special kinematic
points is an additional theorem only when the corresponding operator basis and
symmetry argument are displayed.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\section{Nonrelativistic Heavy Pairs and Potential Matching}
\label{sec:qcd-nrqcd-potential-matching}

Quarkonium requires a heavy-mass expansion with two heavy fields and a
specified time foliation.  Choose the rest frame of the heavy pair and write
\(t\) for its time coordinate.  A nonrelativistic heavy quark is represented by
a two-component Pauli field \(\psi(t,\mathbf x)\) in the fundamental
representation.  The corresponding antiquark is represented, after charge
conjugation, by another Pauli field \(\chi(t,\mathbf x)\) which also
transforms in the fundamental representation; its adjoint \(\chi^\dagger\)
creates an antiquark and transforms as a row antifundamental.  With
\[
  D_t=\partial_t-\ii A_0,\qquad
  \mathbf D=\nabla-\ii\mathbf A ,
\]
the leading nonrelativistic action is
\begin{equation}
  S_{\rm NR}^{(0)}
  =
  \int \dd t\,\dd^3\mathbf x\,
  \left[
    \psi^\dagger\left(\ii D_t+\frac{\mathbf D^2}{2m_Q}\right)\psi
    +
    \chi^\dagger\left(\ii D_t+\frac{\mathbf D^2}{2m_Q}\right)\chi
  \right].
  \label{eq:nrqcd-leading-action}
\end{equation}
The sign of the spatial Laplacian in \eqref{eq:nrqcd-leading-action} is fixed
by the convention \(D_i\ee^{\ii\mathbf p\cdot\mathbf x}=\ii p_i
\ee^{\ii\mathbf p\cdot\mathbf x}\) in the free theory.

\begin{definition}[NRQCD datum]
\label{def:nrqcd-datum}
An NRQCD datum for a heavy flavor of mass \(m_Q\) consists of the following
items.
\begin{enumerate}
  \item A gauge-covariant regulator for QCD and a matching scale below
  \(m_Q\), together with a class of states whose heavy-quark three-momenta
  obey \(|\mathbf p|/m_Q\ll1\).
  \item Pauli fields \(\psi,\chi\), the gauge fields, and a local action of
  the form
  \[
    S_{\rm NRQCD}^{(N)}
    =
    S_{\rm NR}^{(0)}
    +
    \sum_{a}\frac{c_a(\mu,m_Q)}{m_Q^{d_a-4}}
    \int \mathcal O_a^{\rm NR}(t,\mathbf x)\,\dd t\,\dd^3\mathbf x ,
  \]
  where \(\mathcal O_a^{\rm NR}\) ranges over gauge-invariant local operators
  built from \(\psi,\chi,F_{\mu\nu}\), covariant derivatives, Pauli matrices,
  and local four-heavy-field annihilation operators, ordered by the chosen
  velocity and \(1/m_Q\) power counting.
  \item Renormalized heavy-pair composite operators.  A quarkonium interpolator
  or current is part of the datum only after its Wilson-line dressing,
  regulator, and subtraction convention have been specified.
\end{enumerate}
The Pauli magnetic term
\[
  \frac{c_F}{2m_Q}\,
  \psi^\dagger\sigma^iB_i\psi
  -
  \frac{c_F}{2m_Q}\,
  \chi^\dagger\sigma^iB_i\chi,
  \qquad
  B_i=\frac12\epsilon_{ijk}F_{jk},
\]
is the first spin-dependent single-particle correction in a parity-invariant
coordinate system.  Its coefficient is a matching coefficient; it is not
deduced from the leading Schrödinger action alone.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Free NRQCD dispersion]
\label{prop:nrqcd-free-dispersion}
The free equation following from the leading quark term in
\eqref{eq:nrqcd-leading-action} has plane-wave solutions
\[
  \psi(t,\mathbf x)=u\,\ee^{-\ii Et+\ii\mathbf p\cdot\mathbf x}
\]
with
\[
  E=\frac{|\mathbf p|^2}{2m_Q}.
\]
Thus \eqref{eq:nrqcd-leading-action} realizes the leading term of the
relativistic residual-energy expansion
\eqref{eq:hqet-free-dispersion}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Substitution of the plane wave gives
\[
  \left(E-\frac{|\mathbf p|^2}{2m_Q}\right)u=0,
\]
because \(\nabla^2\ee^{\ii\mathbf p\cdot\mathbf x}
=-|\mathbf p|^2\ee^{\ii\mathbf p\cdot\mathbf x}\).  A nonzero spinor
amplitude \(u\) therefore requires the displayed dispersion relation.
\end{proof}

Gauge-invariant quarkonium operators are bilocal at nonzero separation.  Let
\[
  \mathbf x_1=\mathbf R+\frac{\mathbf r}{2},
  \qquad
  \mathbf x_2=\mathbf R-\frac{\mathbf r}{2},
\]
and let \(W(\mathbf x_2,\mathbf x_1;t)\) be the equal-time fundamental Wilson
transporter from \(\mathbf x_1\) to \(\mathbf x_2\).  Define the singlet
bilocal
\begin{equation}
  S(t,\mathbf R,\mathbf r)
  =
  \frac1{\sqrt{N_c}}\,
  \chi^\dagger(t,\mathbf x_2)
  W(\mathbf x_2,\mathbf x_1;t)
  \psi(t,\mathbf x_1).
  \label{eq:pnrqcd-singlet-bilocal}
\end{equation}
An octet bilocal with a color label based at \(\mathbf R\) is represented by
\begin{equation}
  O^a(t,\mathbf R,\mathbf r)
  =
  \chi^\dagger(t,\mathbf x_2)
  W(\mathbf x_2,\mathbf R;t)\,
  t^a\,
  W(\mathbf R,\mathbf x_1;t)
  \psi(t,\mathbf x_1).
  \label{eq:pnrqcd-octet-bilocal}
\end{equation}
The octet transforms in the adjoint representation at \(\mathbf R\); the
singlet is gauge invariant.

\begin{proof}[Gauge covariance of the bilocals]
Under a gauge transformation \(U(t,\mathbf x)\),
\[
  \psi(\mathbf x_1)\mapsto U(\mathbf x_1)\psi(\mathbf x_1),
  \qquad
  \chi^\dagger(\mathbf x_2)\mapsto
  \chi^\dagger(\mathbf x_2)U(\mathbf x_2)^{-1},
\]
and
\[
  W(\mathbf x_2,\mathbf x_1)
  \mapsto
  U(\mathbf x_2)W(\mathbf x_2,\mathbf x_1)U(\mathbf x_1)^{-1}.
\]
The endpoint matrices cancel in \eqref{eq:pnrqcd-singlet-bilocal}.  In
\eqref{eq:pnrqcd-octet-bilocal} the endpoint matrices again cancel, while the
generator at \(\mathbf R\) transforms by conjugation,
\(t^a\mapsto U(\mathbf R)t^aU(\mathbf R)^{-1}\), which is the adjoint action.
\end{proof}

Potential NRQCD is obtained by integrating out the relative-momentum scale
\(m_Qv_{\rm rel}\) while retaining the lower energy scale
\(m_Qv_{\rm rel}^2\).  The singlet part of the resulting bilocal action has
the form
\begin{equation}
  S_{\rm pNRQCD}^{S}
  =
  \int \dd t\,\dd^3\mathbf R\,\dd^3\mathbf r\,
  S^\dagger
  \left[
    \ii\partial_t
    +\frac{\nabla_{\mathbf r}^2}{m_Q}
    -V_S(r;\mu)
    +\cdots
  \right]S ,
  \label{eq:pnrqcd-singlet-action}
\end{equation}
where \(r=|\mathbf r|\).  The potential \(V_S(r;\mu)\) is a matching
coefficient for the bilocal singlet operator.  In a weak-coupling matching
regime, the tree-level Coulomb exchange gives
\begin{equation}
  V_S^{(0)}(r)=-\frac{g^2C_F}{4\pi r},
  \label{eq:pnrqcd-tree-coulomb-potential}
\end{equation}
with \(C_F=(N_c^2-1)/N_c\) and the same trace-delta coupling used throughout
this chapter.  This formula is invariant under conversion to the common
half-trace convention because \(g_{\rm ht}^2=2g^2\) and
\(C_F^{\rm ht}=C_F/2\).

\begin{proposition}[Tree-level singlet color factor]
\label{prop:pnrqcd-singlet-color-factor}
In the trace convention of \eqref{eq:qcd-casimir-definitions}, the color
factor for one-gluon exchange in a normalized quark-antiquark singlet is
\(-C_F\).  Hence the attractive Coulomb potential is
\eqref{eq:pnrqcd-tree-coulomb-potential}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The normalized singlet color tensor is
\(\delta^i{}_j/\sqrt{N_c}\).  The antiquark generator is the negative
transpose of the quark generator.  Acting with \(t^a\otimes(-t^{aT})\) on the
singlet gives
\[
  -\frac1{\sqrt{N_c}}(t^at^a)^i{}_j
  =
  -C_F\frac{\delta^i{}_j}{\sqrt{N_c}} .
\]
The spatial Fourier transform of the Coulomb kernel is
\[
  \int\frac{\dd^3\mathbf q}{(2\pi)^3}\,
  \frac{\ee^{\ii\mathbf q\cdot\mathbf r}}{|\mathbf q|^2}
  =
  \frac1{4\pi r},
\]
so the product of the exchange kernel \(g^2/|\mathbf q|^2\) with the singlet
color eigenvalue gives \eqref{eq:pnrqcd-tree-coulomb-potential}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Quarkonium fine and hyperfine spin algebra]
\label{prop:qcd-quarkonium-spin-centroid}
Fix a quarkonium radial level and orbital angular momentum \(L\) in a
pNRQCD datum.  Let
\[
  \mathbf S_Q=\frac12\boldsymbol\sigma_Q,\qquad
  \mathbf S_{\bar Q}=\frac12\boldsymbol\sigma_{\bar Q},\qquad
  \mathbf S=\mathbf S_Q+\mathbf S_{\bar Q},\qquad
  \mathbf J=\mathbf L+\mathbf S .
\]
Assume that, to first order in the spin-dependent part of the matched
Hamiltonian, the restriction to this radial-orbital subspace has the form
\begin{equation}
  H_{nL}^{\rm sd}
  =
  A_{nL}\,\mathbf S_Q\cdot\mathbf S_{\bar Q}
  +
  B_{nL}\,\mathbf L\cdot\mathbf S
  +
  C_{nL}\,\mathcal T_{LS},
  \label{eq:qcd-quarkonium-spin-dependent-hamiltonian}
\end{equation}
where \(A_{nL},B_{nL},C_{nL}\) are radial matrix elements or matching
coefficients in the chosen scheme, and \(\mathcal T_{LS}\) is the rotational
scalar obtained by coupling a traceless rank-two orbital tensor to a
traceless rank-two spin tensor.  Then
\[
  \mathbf S_Q\cdot\mathbf S_{\bar Q}
  =
  \begin{cases}
  -\frac34, & S=0,\\[2mm]
  \frac14, & S=1,
  \end{cases}
  \label{eq:qcd-quarkonium-spin-spin-eigenvalues}
\]
and, on the triplet \(S=1\) states,
\begin{equation}
  \mathbf L\cdot\mathbf S
  =
  \frac12\bigl(J(J+1)-L(L+1)-2\bigr)
  =
  \begin{cases}
  -(L+1), & J=L-1,\\
  -1, & J=L,\\
  L, & J=L+1 .
  \end{cases}
  \label{eq:qcd-quarkonium-spin-orbit-eigenvalues}
\end{equation}
If \(M(^1L_L)\) denotes the singlet mass and \(M(^3L_J)\) the triplet masses
computed to this first order from a common spin-independent radial level
\(E_{nL}^{(0)}\), then the triplet centroid obeys
\begin{equation}
  \overline M(^3L)
  :=
  \frac{\sum_{J=L-1}^{L+1}(2J+1)M(^3L_J)}{3(2L+1)}
  =
  E_{nL}^{(0)}+\frac14 A_{nL},
  \label{eq:qcd-quarkonium-triplet-centroid}
\end{equation}
with the obvious omission of the nonexistent \(J=L-1\) term when \(L=0\).
The centroid hyperfine difference is therefore
\begin{equation}
  \overline M(^3L)-M(^1L_L)=A_{nL}.
  \label{eq:qcd-quarkonium-hyperfine-centroid}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The two heavy spins are spin-\(\frac12\) representations.  Since
\[
  \mathbf S^2
  =
  \mathbf S_Q^2+\mathbf S_{\bar Q}^2
  +2\mathbf S_Q\cdot\mathbf S_{\bar Q},
  \qquad
  \mathbf S_Q^2=\mathbf S_{\bar Q}^2=\frac34,
\]
one has
\[
  \mathbf S_Q\cdot\mathbf S_{\bar Q}
  =
  \frac12\left(S(S+1)-\frac32\right),
\]
which gives \eqref{eq:qcd-quarkonium-spin-spin-eigenvalues} for
\(S=0,1\).  Similarly
\[
  \mathbf J^2
  =
  \mathbf L^2+\mathbf S^2+2\mathbf L\cdot\mathbf S
\]
gives the first equality in
\eqref{eq:qcd-quarkonium-spin-orbit-eigenvalues}; substituting
\(S=1\) and \(J=L-1,L,L+1\) gives the displayed three values.

It remains to check the centroid.  The trace of \(\mathbf L\cdot\mathbf S\)
on the tensor product of the orbital \(L\) space and the triplet spin space
vanishes:
\[
  \operatorname{Tr}_{L\otimes S=1}(\mathbf L\cdot\mathbf S)
  =
  \sum_i \operatorname{Tr}_{L}(L_i)\operatorname{Tr}_{S=1}(S_i)=0,
\]
because every generator of an irreducible \(SU(2)\) representation is
traceless.  The operator \(\mathcal T_{LS}\) is a contraction of traceless
rank-two tensors, so its trace on the same tensor product also vanishes.  The
weighted sum
\(\sum_J(2J+1)M(^3L_J)\) is precisely this trace after decomposition into
irreducible \(J\) summands.  Therefore only the spin-independent energy and
the triplet spin-spin eigenvalue \(\frac14A_{nL}\) survive in the centroid,
proving \eqref{eq:qcd-quarkonium-triplet-centroid}.  The singlet has
\(\mathbf L\cdot\mathbf S=0\), no rank-two spin tensor, and spin-spin
eigenvalue \(-\frac34\); subtracting its first-order mass from the triplet
centroid gives \eqref{eq:qcd-quarkonium-hyperfine-centroid}.
\end{proof}

Proposition~\ref{prop:qcd-quarkonium-spin-centroid} is the part of
quarkonium spectroscopy that follows from angular momentum and the matched
operator form alone.  The numerical values of
\(A_{nL},B_{nL},C_{nL}\) are QCD matching data.  In weak-coupling pNRQCD they
are computed from perturbative potentials and wavefunctions in a stated mass
scheme; in strong-coupling pNRQCD they are Wilson-loop and chromofield
insertion matrix elements.  In either case the symbols
``hyperfine splitting'' and ``fine structure'' refer to the spectral
differences defined by
\eqref{eq:qcd-quarkonium-spin-orbit-eigenvalues}--\eqref{eq:qcd-quarkonium-hyperfine-centroid},
rather than to a freestanding constituent-potential model.

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Quarkonium scale separation]
\label{ca:nrqcd-pnrqcd-scale-separation}
Let \(v_{\rm rel}\) be the velocity coordinate assigned to a family of
quarkonium states.  The weak-coupling potential expansion assumes
\[
  m_Q\gg m_Qv_{\rm rel}\gg m_Qv_{\rm rel}^2,
  \qquad
  m_Qv_{\rm rel}\gg \Lambda_{\rm QCD},
\]
so that the soft relative-momentum scale can be integrated out
perturbatively.  Strong-coupling pNRQCD instead treats the potential as a
nonperturbative matching coefficient defined by static Wilson-loop and
chromofield-insertion matrix elements.  In both regimes a claim of accuracy
requires a norm or class of smeared matrix elements and an explicit remainder
estimate in powers of \(v_{\rm rel}\), \(1/m_Q\), and
\(\Lambda_{\rm QCD}/(m_Qv_{\rm rel})\) when that ratio is used.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\section{Heavy-Quark Mass Coordinates and Static Energies}
\label{sec:qcd-heavy-mass-static-energy}

The mass \(m_Q\) appearing in HQET, NRQCD, and pNRQCD is a coordinate in a
regulated Lagrangian and in its matched effective descriptions.  In a confining
four-dimensional QCD theory an isolated colored quark is not an asymptotic
particle, so a quark pole mass is not a gauge-invariant spectral observable.
Perturbation theory in a fixed gauge nevertheless defines formal mass
coordinates, including an on-shell coordinate order by order.  Such
coordinates are useful only after their infrared sensitivity and their
relation to gauge-invariant quantities have been stated.

The gauge-invariant static quark-antiquark energy is extracted from Wilson
loops.  With a specified line-renormalization prescription, define
\begin{equation}
  E_{\rm stat}(r;\mu)
  =
  -\lim_{T\to\infty}\frac1T
  \log \langle W_{\square}(r,T)\rangle_{\rm ren,\mu},
  \label{eq:qcd-static-energy-renormalized}
\end{equation}
where \(W_{\square}(r,T)\) is the rectangular fundamental Wilson loop of
spatial size \(r\) and time extent \(T\).  The subscript records the
ultraviolet and line-renormalization convention.  Additive constants in
\(E_{\rm stat}\) are not absolute observables; energy differences and matched
hadron masses are.

At distances \(r\) in a weak-coupling matching range, the pNRQCD singlet
potential is a coordinate in the decomposition
\begin{equation}
  E_{\rm stat}(r;\mu)
  =
  2m_{\rm sd}(\mu_f)+V_{\rm sd}(r;\mu,\mu_f)+\Delta_{\rm us}(r;\mu,\mu_f),
  \label{eq:qcd-static-energy-sd-decomposition}
\end{equation}
where \(m_{\rm sd}\) is a short-distance heavy-quark mass coordinate,
\(V_{\rm sd}\) is the corresponding singlet potential coordinate, and
\(\Delta_{\rm us}\) denotes lower-energy contributions retained in pNRQCD.
The auxiliary scale \(\mu_f\) separates contributions assigned to the mass
coordinate from contributions assigned to the potential coordinate.

\begin{proposition}[Constant mass-coordinate transformations]
\label{prop:qcd-heavy-mass-potential-shift}
Let \(\delta m\) be a finite scheme change independent of \(r\).  The
coordinate transformation
\begin{equation}
  m_{\rm sd}'=m_{\rm sd}+\delta m,
  \qquad
  V_{\rm sd}'(r)=V_{\rm sd}(r)-2\delta m
  \label{eq:qcd-heavy-mass-potential-shift}
\end{equation}
leaves the static energy \eqref{eq:qcd-static-energy-sd-decomposition}
unchanged when \(\Delta_{\rm us}\) is held fixed.  If a pNRQCD Hamiltonian is
shifted by \(V_{\rm sd}\mapsto V_{\rm sd}-2\delta m\), every singlet
eigenvalue \(E_n\) is shifted by \(-2\delta m\), and
\(2m_{\rm sd}+E_n\) is unchanged.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Substitution into \eqref{eq:qcd-static-energy-sd-decomposition} gives
\[
  2(m_{\rm sd}+\delta m)+(V_{\rm sd}-2\delta m)+\Delta_{\rm us}
  =
  2m_{\rm sd}+V_{\rm sd}+\Delta_{\rm us}.
\]
For a Hamiltonian \(H_{\rm sd}=T+V_{\rm sd}\), the transformed Hamiltonian is
\(H_{\rm sd}'=H_{\rm sd}-2\delta m\).  If
\(H_{\rm sd}\psi_n=E_n\psi_n\), then
\(H_{\rm sd}'\psi_n=(E_n-2\delta m)\psi_n\).  Therefore
\[
  2(m_{\rm sd}+\delta m)+(E_n-2\delta m)=2m_{\rm sd}+E_n .
\]
The statement is finite-dimensional spectral algebra applied to the
regularized Hamiltonian, and then to any limit in which the relevant
eigenvalue exists.
\end{proof}

One useful short-distance coordinate is the potential-subtracted mass.  Start
from a formal perturbative pole coordinate \(m_{\rm pole}\) and define
\begin{equation}
  m_{\rm PS}(\mu_f)
  =
  m_{\rm pole}-\delta m_{\rm PS}(\mu_f),
  \qquad
  \delta m_{\rm PS}(\mu_f)
  =
  -\frac12
  \int_{|\mathbf q|<\mu_f}
  \frac{\dd^3\mathbf q}{(2\pi)^3}\,
  \widetilde V(\mathbf q),
  \label{eq:qcd-ps-mass-definition}
\end{equation}
where \(\widetilde V(\mathbf q)\) is the perturbative momentum-space singlet
potential in the same convention.  At tree level
\[
  \widetilde V^{(0)}(\mathbf q)=-\frac{g^2C_F}{|\mathbf q|^2}.
\]
Consequently
\begin{equation}
  \delta m_{\rm PS}^{(0)}(\mu_f)
  =
  \frac{g^2C_F}{4\pi^2}\,\mu_f .
  \label{eq:qcd-ps-leading-subtraction}
\end{equation}
In the common half-trace convention this is the same expression because
\(g_{\rm ht}^2C_F^{\rm ht}=g^2C_F\).

\begin{proof}
Using spherical coordinates in momentum space,
\[
  \int_{|\mathbf q|<\mu_f}
  \frac{\dd^3\mathbf q}{(2\pi)^3}\,\frac1{|\mathbf q|^2}
  =
  \frac{4\pi}{(2\pi)^3}\int_0^{\mu_f}\dd q
  =
  \frac{\mu_f}{2\pi^2}.
\]
Multiplying by \(g^2C_F/2\), as dictated by
\eqref{eq:qcd-ps-mass-definition} and
\(\widetilde V^{(0)}=-g^2C_F/|\mathbf q|^2\), gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-ps-leading-subtraction}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Renormalon language in the heavy-quark sector]
\label{rem:qcd-heavy-renormalon-status}
The leading infrared sensitivity of the formal perturbative pole coordinate
and the additive constant in the perturbative static potential are tied to the
same long-distance momentum region.  In perturbative large-order language this
is described as a cancellation of the leading static-energy renormalon between
\(2m_{\rm pole}\) and \(V_{\rm pole}(r)\).  The mathematically precise
statement used here is the finite coordinate transformation
\eqref{eq:qcd-heavy-mass-potential-shift} and the definition of
short-distance coordinates such as \eqref{eq:qcd-ps-mass-definition}.  A claim
about a Borel singularity, its residue, or its cancellation is a claim about a
specified perturbative expansion and summation prescription, not a
nonperturbative definition of the quark mass.
\end{remark}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Mass schemes in quarkonium predictions]
\label{ca:qcd-heavy-mass-scheme-control}
A quarkonium prediction based on pNRQCD must state the mass coordinate, the
potential coordinate, the subtraction scale \(\mu_f\) when one is used, and the
class of matrix elements or energy levels being approximated.  Replacing
\((m,V)\) by a short-distance pair \((m',V')\) is exact at the level of the
matched Hamiltonian if \eqref{eq:qcd-heavy-mass-potential-shift} is imposed.
Truncating perturbative series introduces residual \(\mu_f\)- and
scheme-dependence; the size of that dependence is an error diagnostic only
after the truncation order, velocity counting, and ultrasoft treatment have
been fixed.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\section{Color and Physical External States}

The gauge-fixed quark and gluon fields are useful local variables in
perturbation theory.  Physical states are BRST cohomology classes, and local
physical operators are represented by gauge-invariant or BRST-closed
operators.  This has an immediate consequence for scattering: LSZ reduction
applied to the elementary quark or gluon fields does not by itself define a
physical hadron \(S\)-matrix.  Physical external states in QCD are created by
color-singlet operators, such as
\[
  \bar q_I q_J,\qquad
  \bar q_I\gamma^\mu q_J,\qquad
  \epsilon_{i_1\cdots i_{N_c}}
  q^{i_1}_{I_1}\cdots q^{i_{N_c}}_{I_{N_c}},
  \qquad
  \operatorname{tr}(F_{\mu\nu}F^{\mu\nu}).
\]
The first three are mesonic current, vector-current, and baryonic examples;
the last is a gluonic example.

Confinement, in the spectral sense used here, is the assertion that isolated
finite-energy asymptotic particles carry no color.  In four-dimensional QCD
this assertion is a nonperturbative physical input, supported by the observed
hadron spectrum and by lattice evidence, rather than a theorem presently
derived from the continuum Lagrangian.  The monograph uses this precise
spectral hypothesis when discussing QCD phenomenology: the asymptotic states
are hadrons, while the short-distance operator expansion is expressed in terms
of quark and gluon fields because those are the local variables of the
renormalized gauge theory.

\begin{openproblem}[Asymptotic completeness of physical QCD]
\label{op:qcd-asymptotic-completeness}
Starting from a nonperturbative four-dimensional QCD Hilbert space
\(\mathcal H_{\rm phys}\), its unitary translation representation, and its
gauge-invariant local observable algebra, construct the physical incoming and
outgoing scattering theory.  The required asymptotic space
\[
  \mathcal H_{\rm as}^{\rm QCD}
\]
should be built from stable color-singlet Wigner particles in the relevant
superselection sectors: mesons, baryons, glueballs in pure Yang--Mills
subsectors, and, in chiral limits, the massless Goldstone modes with their
long-distance scattering structure.  Unstable hadronic resonances should enter
through the analytic structure of the color-singlet scattering operator rather
than as ordinary external vectors.  The wave operators
\[
  \Omega_{\rm in/out}^{\rm QCD}:
  \mathcal H_{\rm as}^{\rm QCD}\longrightarrow \mathcal H_{\rm phys}
\]
should be isometric, should intertwine translations, and should have common
closed range equal to the finite-energy physical sector under consideration:
\[
  \overline{\operatorname{Ran}\Omega_{\rm in}^{\rm QCD}}
  =
  \overline{\operatorname{Ran}\Omega_{\rm out}^{\rm QCD}}
  =
  \mathcal H_{\rm phys}^{\rm sector}.
\]
One must also construct the detector limits, such as the energy-flow
operators below, on the same scattering domain and prove that the inclusive
calorimetric observables used in high-energy QCD are obtained from this
Hilbert-space scattering theory.

This problem is logically stronger than asymptotic freedom, factorization, a
mass gap in pure Yang--Mills theory, or the spectral confinement hypothesis
used above.  Asymptotic freedom controls short-distance operator products and
partonic coefficient functions.  Factorization gives a perturbative expansion
for selected inclusive observables after the relevant operator matrix elements
have been defined.  Asymptotic completeness is a large-time statement about
the range of physical wave operators in the gauge-invariant Hilbert space.
\end{openproblem}

\section{Hadron Spectroscopy as an Ab Initio QCD Datum}
\label{sec:qcd-hadron-spectroscopy-ab-initio}

Hadron spectroscopy is not a list of model names assigned to observed peaks.
It is a collection of spectral and scattering statements about the
gauge-invariant Hilbert space of QCD.  A spectroscopic claim must therefore
state which Hilbert-space object is being computed.  Stable hadrons are
isolated eigenvalues of the mass operator \(M^2=P_\mu P^\mu\) in color-singlet
superselection sectors.  Resonances are poles of color-singlet scattering
amplitudes on specified nonphysical sheets, as in
Chapter~\ref{ch:volume-ii-resonances-dressed-propagators}; they are not
additional vectors in the asymptotic Hilbert space.  Finite-volume energy
levels are regulator observables whose infinite-volume interpretation requires
a quantization map, not a direct equality between a box eigenvalue and a
resonance mass.

Let \(I,J\) denote flavor labels and let \(i,j\) be color labels.  Typical
local color-singlet sources are
\begin{align}
  M_{\Gamma,IJ}(x)
  &=
  \bar q_I(x)\Gamma q_J(x),
  \label{eq:qcd-meson-local-source}\\
  B_{\alpha_1\cdots\alpha_{N_c};I_1\cdots I_{N_c}}(x)
  &=
  \epsilon_{i_1\cdots i_{N_c}}\,
  q^{i_1}_{\alpha_1 I_1}(x)\cdots
  q^{i_{N_c}}_{\alpha_{N_c} I_{N_c}}(x),
  \label{eq:qcd-baryon-local-source}\\
  G_{\mathcal P}(x)
  &=
  \operatorname{tr}\mathcal P(F_{\mu\nu},D_\rho)(x).
  \label{eq:qcd-glueball-local-source}
\end{align}
Here \(\Gamma\) is a Dirac matrix, possibly with covariant derivatives
inserted and with Lorentz indices projected to a definite spin channel, and
\(\mathcal P\) is a gauge-covariant polynomial whose color indices are traced
using the convention fixed in \eqref{eq:qcd-casimir-definitions}.  Nonlocal
sources are allowed, but their Wilson lines, smearing kernels, and endpoint
renormalizations are part of the operator definition.  For example, a hybrid
meson source may be represented by
\[
  \bar q_I(x)\Gamma^{\mu\nu} F_{\mu\nu}(x) q_J(x),
\]
or by a point-split bilinear with a Wilson-line path and a field-strength
insertion on that path.  These are different regulator coordinates unless a
continuum matching relation has been supplied.

\begin{definition}[Hadron spectral extraction datum]
\label{def:qcd-hadron-spectral-extraction-datum}
A QCD hadron spectral extraction datum consists of:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the quark masses, gauge group, global form, spacetime volume, boundary
  conditions, and regulator action;
  \item a list of gauge-invariant interpolating operators, including their
  flavor, parity, charge conjugation, spin or cubic-group channel, smearing,
  and renormalization prescriptions;
  \item the Euclidean correlation matrix
  \[
    C_{AB}(t)=
    \langle \mathcal O_A(t)\mathcal O_B^\dagger(0)\rangle
    -\langle \mathcal O_A\rangle\langle\mathcal O_B^\dagger\rangle ;
  \]
  \item a finite-volume spectral extraction method, usually a generalized
  eigenvalue problem for \(C(t)\);
  \item a map from finite-volume energies to infinite-volume observables:
  isolated stable masses for one-particle states, and scattering amplitudes or
  pole positions for resonances;
  \item continuum, chiral, heavy-quark, and infinite-volume extrapolations,
  with the systematics stated separately.
\end{enumerate}
The datum is called \emph{ab initio} only when the matrix elements are defined
from the QCD path integral or Hilbert space itself.  A constituent model may
be useful as a coordinate chart or mnemonic, but it is not an ab initio
definition of the spectrum.
\end{definition}

For a finite spatial torus and a reflection-positive lattice regulator, the
spectral decomposition has the same form as
\eqref{eq:lattice-glueball-spectral-matrix}:
\[
  C_{AB}(t)=
  \sum_{n\ge0}Z_A^{(n)}\overline{Z_B^{(n)}}\ee^{-E_n t},
  \qquad
  Z_A^{(n)}=\bra{\Omega}\mathcal O_A\ket{n,L}.
\]
The vectors \(\ket{n,L}\) are finite-volume color-singlet eigenvectors.  If
an eigenvalue converges, after removing the center-of-mass motion and taking
the regulator limits, to an isolated one-particle mass below all relevant
thresholds, the resulting number is a stable-hadron mass.  Above threshold the
finite-volume levels instead sample the scattering operator.  In a single
elastic two-particle channel with total momentum zero, particle masses
\(m_1,m_2\), relative momentum \(k\), and energy
\[
  E=\sqrt{m_1^2+k^2}+\sqrt{m_2^2+k^2},
\]
the simplest unmixed partial-wave quantization condition is
\begin{equation}
  \delta_\ell(k)+\phi_{\ell}(q)=n\pi,
  \qquad
  q=\frac{kL}{2\pi},
  \label{eq:qcd-luscher-single-channel-condition}
\end{equation}
where \(\delta_\ell\) is the infinite-volume elastic phase shift and
\(\phi_\ell\) is a known geometric function built from the finite-volume zeta
function.  Equation~\eqref{eq:qcd-luscher-single-channel-condition} is not a
model of a resonance.  It is a finite-volume reconstruction theorem under
elasticity, locality, and regulator hypotheses.  In realistic QCD channels
one must use the coupled-channel determinant version, because cubic symmetry
mixes partial waves and inelastic thresholds are often nearby.

\begin{proposition}[Single-channel finite-volume pole reconstruction]
\label{prop:qcd-single-channel-luscher-kmatrix-pole}
Assume that, on an open real energy interval \(I\), a QCD channel is
elastic, has two stable color-singlet particles of masses \(m_1,m_2\), and
has been reduced, by a stated cubic-irrep analysis, to a single partial wave
\(\ell\).  Put \(J=\{E^2:E\in I\}\) and
\[
  \rho_{12}(s)=\frac{2k(s)}{\sqrt s},
  \qquad
  E=\sqrt{m_1^2+k(s)^2}+\sqrt{m_2^2+k(s)^2},
\]
for \(s=E^2\in J\), and use the partial-wave normalization
\[
  S_\ell(s)=1+2\ii \rho_{12}(s)t_\ell^{(I)}(s)
  =\ee^{2\ii\delta_\ell(s)} .
\]
Then the physical-sheet elastic amplitude is equivalently written
\begin{equation}
  t_\ell^{(I)}(s)=
  \frac{1}{K_\ell^{-1}(s)-\ii\rho_{12}(s)},
  \qquad
  K_\ell^{-1}(s)=\rho_{12}(s)\cot\delta_\ell(s),
  \label{eq:qcd-single-channel-kmatrix-definition}
\end{equation}
where \(K_\ell^{-1}(s)\) is real on \(J\).  Each finite-volume energy
\(E_n\in I\) satisfying
\eqref{eq:qcd-luscher-single-channel-condition} determines the real-axis
coordinate
\begin{equation}
  K_\ell^{-1}(E_n^2)
  =
  -\rho_{12}(E_n^2)\cot\phi_\ell(q_n),
  \qquad
  q_n=\frac{k(E_n)L}{2\pi}.
  \label{eq:qcd-luscher-kmatrix-sample}
\end{equation}
If \(K_\ell^{-1}\) and \(\rho_{12}\) have the chosen analytic continuations
to a simply connected neighborhood of a candidate resonance pole and no
additional channel threshold crosses that neighborhood, the corresponding
second-sheet pole \(s_\ast\) is a zero of
\begin{equation}
  K_\ell^{-1}(s_\ast)+\ii\rho_{12}(s_\ast)=0 .
  \label{eq:qcd-single-channel-second-sheet-pole}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Elastic unitarity in the normalization of the proposition says
\(S_\ell^\ast S_\ell=1\) on \(I\).  Hence
\[
  t_\ell^{(I)}(s)
  =
  \frac{\ee^{2\ii\delta_\ell(s)}-1}{2\ii\rho_{12}(s)}
  =
  \frac{\ee^{\ii\delta_\ell(s)}\sin\delta_\ell(s)}
       {\rho_{12}(s)}
\]
and therefore
\[
  \bigl(t_\ell^{(I)}(s)\bigr)^{-1}
  =
  \rho_{12}(s)\bigl(\cot\delta_\ell(s)-\ii\bigr).
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:qcd-single-channel-kmatrix-definition} and identifies
the real coordinate \(K_\ell^{-1}=\rho_{12}\cot\delta_\ell\).  At a
finite-volume level satisfying
\(\delta_\ell(k_n)+\phi_\ell(q_n)=n\pi\),
\[
  \cot\delta_\ell(k_n)
  =
  \cot\bigl(n\pi-\phi_\ell(q_n)\bigr)
  =
  -\cot\phi_\ell(q_n),
\]
which gives \eqref{eq:qcd-luscher-kmatrix-sample}.  Across the elastic
unitarity cut the chosen branch of the two-body momentum changes sign, so
\(\rho_{12}\) changes sign while \(K_\ell^{-1}\), being the real analytic
coordinate fixed on the cut, continues through the same germ.  Thus the
amplitude on the adjacent sheet is
\[
  t_\ell^{(II)}(s)=
  \frac{1}{K_\ell^{-1}(s)+\ii\rho_{12}(s)} ,
\]
and its isolated poles are precisely the zeros of the denominator, giving
\eqref{eq:qcd-single-channel-second-sheet-pole}.
\end{proof}

This proposition gives the exact algebraic target of a one-channel
finite-volume resonance extraction.  A concrete determination of
\(s_\ast\) also contains an analytic representation or parametrization of
\(K_\ell^{-1}\), regulator and volume limits for the input energies, and
separate bounds for neglected partial waves and inelastic channels.

\begin{proposition}[Coupled-channel determinant and sheet bookkeeping]
\label{prop:qcd-coupled-channel-kmatrix-sheet}
Let \(a,b=1,\ldots,N\) label finitely many stable two-particle
color-singlet channels in a fixed set of conserved quantum numbers, and let
\(\alpha,\beta\) label the partial waves and cubic-irrep components retained
in a finite-volume analysis.  On a real interval below the next omitted
threshold, let \(\rho(s)\) be the positive diagonal matrix with entries
\(\rho_a(s)=2k_a(s)/\sqrt s\), repeated on the retained angular-momentum
indices.  With the normalization
\[
  S=1+2\ii\,\rho^{1/2}t^{(I)}\rho^{1/2},
\]
elastic coupled-channel unitarity is equivalent, on the interval, to
\begin{equation}
  t^{(I)}(s)=\bigl(K^{-1}(s)-\ii\rho(s)\bigr)^{-1},
  \qquad
  K^{-1}(s)^\dagger=K^{-1}(s).
  \label{eq:qcd-coupled-channel-kmatrix}
\end{equation}
Suppose, in addition, that the coupled-channel finite-volume reconstruction
theorem has been established for this channel and written in the same
normalization, so that the finite-volume energies in a cubic irrep
\(\Gamma\) obey
\begin{equation}
  \det\!\bigl(K^{-1}(E^2)+F^\Gamma(E,L)\bigr)=0,
  \label{eq:qcd-coupled-channel-luscher-determinant}
\end{equation}
where \(F^\Gamma(E,L)\) is the real geometric matrix determined by the box,
total momentum, masses, and irrep projection.  In the one-channel unmixed
limit \(F^\Gamma=\rho_{12}\cot\phi_\ell\), so
\eqref{eq:qcd-coupled-channel-luscher-determinant} reduces to
\eqref{eq:qcd-luscher-kmatrix-sample}.  If \(\Sigma\) is the diagonal matrix
whose entry is \(+1\) on a channel kept on the physical branch and \(-1\) on
a channel analytically continued through its unitary cut, the corresponding
sheet amplitude is
\begin{equation}
  t^{(\Sigma)}(s)=
  \bigl(K^{-1}(s)-\ii\,\Sigma\rho(s)\bigr)^{-1},
  \qquad
  \det\!\bigl(K^{-1}(s_\ast)-\ii\,\Sigma\rho(s_\ast)\bigr)=0 .
  \label{eq:qcd-coupled-channel-sheet-pole}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
From \(S^\dagger S=1\) and
\(S=1+2\ii\rho^{1/2}t^{(I)}\rho^{1/2}\), one obtains
\[
  t^{(I)}-t^{(I)\dagger}
  =
  2\ii\,t^{(I)\dagger}\rho\,t^{(I)}.
\]
Multiplying by \(\bigl(t^{(I)\dagger}\bigr)^{-1}\) on the left and by
\(\bigl(t^{(I)}\bigr)^{-1}\) on the right gives
\[
  \bigl(t^{(I)\dagger}\bigr)^{-1}
  -
  \bigl(t^{(I)}\bigr)^{-1}
  =
  2\ii\rho,
  \qquad
  \bigl(t^{(I)}\bigr)^{-1}
  -
  \bigl(t^{(I)\dagger}\bigr)^{-1}
  =
  -2\ii\rho .
\]
Thus \(K^{-1}:=\bigl(t^{(I)}\bigr)^{-1}+\ii\rho\) is Hermitian on the
physical interval, and \eqref{eq:qcd-coupled-channel-kmatrix} follows.  The
finite-volume determinant relation is the stated reconstruction input
