expressed in this \(K\)-matrix coordinate.  In the one-channel unmixed
reduction, its zero condition is
\[
  K_\ell^{-1}(E^2)+\rho_{12}(E^2)\cot\phi_\ell(q)=0,
  \qquad
  K_\ell^{-1}(E^2)
  =
  -\rho_{12}(E^2)\cot\phi_\ell(q),
\]
which is exactly \eqref{eq:qcd-luscher-kmatrix-sample}.  Finally, analytic
continuation through a chosen channel cut changes the sign of that channel's
two-body momentum, hence of the corresponding diagonal entry of \(\rho\),
while the \(K^{-1}\) germ is held fixed.  Repeating this sign choice for all
channels gives the matrix \(\Sigma\), the sheet amplitude in
\eqref{eq:qcd-coupled-channel-sheet-pole}, and the determinant pole
condition.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[QCD resonance pole datum]
\label{def:qcd-resonance-pole-datum}
A hadronic resonance datum consists of a channel space of stable
color-singlet asymptotic states, a physical-region scattering matrix
\(S_{ab}(s)\), a specified analytic continuation across specified unitary
cuts, and an isolated pole \(s_\ast\) of the continued matrix or of an
equivalent partial-wave amplitude.  The mass and width coordinates
\[
  \sqrt{s_\ast}=M_\ast-\frac{\ii}{2}\Gamma_\ast
\]
are pole coordinates after a branch of the square root has been declared.
For a broad or overlapping resonance, line-shape parameters on the real axis
are not invariant substitutes for \(s_\ast\).
\end{definition}

This definition is the correct language for the \(\rho\), the light scalar
isoscalar pole usually denoted \(f_0(500)\), many excited baryons, and
near-threshold exotic candidates.  The notation ``tetraquark'', ``molecule'',
``hybrid'', or ``glueball component'' is then a statement about operator
overlaps, pole motion under controlled deformations, large-\(N_c\) scaling,
or residue factorization.  It is not a separate definition of the state.

The light pseudoscalar sector has additional structure because chiral symmetry
and the anomaly constrain the low-energy coordinates.  Chapter~\ref{ch:volume-ii-21}
derives the pion effective theory, the Gell-Mann--Oakes--Renner relation, and
the Witten--Veneziano large-\(N_c\) formula for the singlet mass.  The vector
and scalar resonances require the scattering-amplitude language above.  For
\(\pi\pi\) scattering, write the isospin partial waves as \(t_\ell^I(s)\)
with physical-region elastic unitarity
\[
  \operatorname{Im}t_\ell^I(s)
  =
  \rho_{\pi\pi}(s)|t_\ell^I(s)|^2,
  \qquad
  \rho_{\pi\pi}(s)=\sqrt{1-\frac{4m_\pi^2}{s}},
\]
below the first inelastic threshold in the chosen normalization.  Roy-type
representations are twice-subtracted fixed-\(t\) dispersion relations
projected to partial waves:
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname{Re}t_\ell^I(s)
  =
  k_\ell^I(s;a_0^0,a_0^2)
  +
  \sum_{I',\ell'}\int_{4m_\pi^2}^{\infty}\dd s'\,
  K_{\ell\ell'}^{II'}(s,s')\,\operatorname{Im}t_{\ell'}^{I'}(s').
  \label{eq:qcd-roy-equation-projected}
\end{equation}
The subtraction constants are the \(S\)-wave scattering lengths.  The kernels
are fixed by crossing, analyticity, and partial-wave projection.  A pole
extraction from \eqref{eq:qcd-roy-equation-projected} is therefore a
controlled dispersive determination only after the high-energy input,
inelastic channels, subtraction constants, and error correlations have been
specified.  The same principle governs Roy--Steiner equations for
\(\pi K\), \(\pi N\), and related channels.

Heavy quarkonium uses a different controlled coordinate system.  If
\[
  m_Q\gg m_Qv\gg m_Qv^2
\]
is a useful hierarchy, the pNRQCD Hamiltonian of the preceding sections
predicts the charmonium and bottomonium level spacings through a potential
coordinate, spin-dependent \(1/m_Q\) operators, and ultrasoft corrections.
The spin-averaged levels, hyperfine splittings, and fine structure are then
matrix elements in a stated effective Hamiltonian.  They are not predictions
of a nonrelativistic potential unless the matching coefficients, mass scheme,
and ultrasoft treatment have been fixed as part of the datum.  The angular
momentum algebra that turns these matched operators into centroid, fine, and
hyperfine coordinates is the finite-dimensional statement of
Proposition~\ref{prop:qcd-quarkonium-spin-centroid}.

Baryon spectroscopy is likewise a QCD spectral problem, not a three-body
mechanics problem imposed from outside.  For \(N_f=3\) light flavors, the
lowest baryons organize approximately into flavor \(SU(3)\) octet and
decuplet representations when the quark masses are close.  To first order in
an octet symmetry-breaking Hamiltonian, the octet masses may be written as
\[
  M(Y,I)=M_0+aY
  +b\left(I(I+1)-\frac{Y^2}{4}\right),
  \label{eq:qcd-baryon-octet-gmo-chart}
\]
where \(Y\) is hypercharge and \(I\) is isospin.  This coordinate chart gives
the Gell-Mann--Okubo relation
\begin{equation}
  2(M_N+M_\Xi)=3M_\Lambda+M_\Sigma .
  \label{eq:qcd-baryon-gell-mann-okubo}
\end{equation}
For the decuplet, first-order octet breaking gives equal spacing along the
hypercharge ladder.  These relations are symmetry consequences of a stated
approximation; the actual QCD masses require lattice, dispersive, and chiral
extrapolation inputs.

\begin{proposition}[Octet and decuplet first-order mass relations]
\label{prop:qcd-baryon-first-order-mass-relations}
Assume that first-order \(SU(3)\)-breaking baryon masses are described by
\eqref{eq:qcd-baryon-octet-gmo-chart} in the octet and by
\(M_{10}(Y)=M_{10,0}+cY\) in the decuplet.  Then
\eqref{eq:qcd-baryon-gell-mann-okubo} holds and
\[
  M_{\Sigma^\ast}-M_\Delta
  =
  M_{\Xi^\ast}-M_{\Sigma^\ast}
  =
  M_\Omega-M_{\Xi^\ast}.
  \label{eq:qcd-decuplet-equal-spacing}
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For the octet,
\[
  (Y,I)_N=(1,\tfrac12),\quad
  (Y,I)_\Lambda=(0,0),\quad
  (Y,I)_\Sigma=(0,1),\quad
  (Y,I)_\Xi=(-1,\tfrac12).
\]
Substitution in \eqref{eq:qcd-baryon-octet-gmo-chart} gives
\[
  M_N=M_0+a+\frac b2,\quad
  M_\Xi=M_0-a+\frac b2,\quad
  M_\Lambda=M_0,\quad
  M_\Sigma=M_0+2b,
\]
which implies \eqref{eq:qcd-baryon-gell-mann-okubo}.  For the decuplet the
hypercharges are \(1,0,-1,-2\).  A linear function of \(Y\) has equal
successive differences, giving \eqref{eq:qcd-decuplet-equal-spacing}.
\end{proof}

In the large-\(N_c\) limit with \(N_f\) fixed, the baryon operator
\eqref{eq:qcd-baryon-local-source} contains \(N_c\) quark fields.  The
pair-counting argument around \eqref{eq:qcd-large-n-baryon-pair-counting}
gives a mass of order \(N_c\), while collective spin-flavor splittings are
typically \(O(1/N_c)\) in the rotor regime.  This is a controlled limit of QCD
under its own hypotheses, and it explains why baryons require a separate
large-\(N_c\) analysis from mesons.  It does not license importing
constituent-quark spectra as QCD predictions.

\begin{definition}[Nucleon current-matrix-element datum]
\label{def:qcd-nucleon-current-matrix-element-datum}
Let \(|N(p,s)\rangle\) be an isolated one-nucleon state in the color-singlet
QCD Hilbert space, with \(p^2=-M_N^2\), \(p^0>0\), and spin label \(s\).  In
the mostly-plus spinor convention of Section~\ref{sec:spinor-conventions},
use the same Dirac--Pauli basis as in
Definition~\ref{def:qed-electron-electromagnetic-form-factors}.  For the Hermitian
electromagnetic current \(J_{\rm em}^\mu\), normalized by the flavor charges
of the quarks, define the nucleon Dirac and Pauli form factors by
\begin{equation}
  \langle N(p',s')|J_{\rm em}^\mu(0)|N(p,s)\rangle
  =
  \frac{\ii e}{(2\pi)^3}\,
  \bar u_{s'}(p')
  \left[
    \gamma^\mu F_1^N(k^2)
    +
    \frac1{M_N}S^{\mu\nu}k_\nu F_2^N(k^2)
  \right]
  u_s(p),
  \qquad k:=p-p',
  \label{eq:qcd-nucleon-dirac-pauli-form-factors}
\end{equation}
where \(e>0\) is the elementary charge and
\(S^{\mu\nu}=-\ii[\gamma^\mu,\gamma^\nu]/4\).  The charge normalization is
\[
  F_1^p(0)=1,\qquad F_1^n(0)=0.
\]
The anomalous magnetic moment coordinate is \(F_2^N(0)\), and the magnetic
moment in nuclear magnetons is \(F_1^N(0)+F_2^N(0)\) after the conventional
normalization by \(e/(2M_N)\).

For spacelike transfer set
\[
  Q^2:=-k^2>0,\qquad
  \tau:=\frac{Q^2}{4M_N^2}.
\]
The Sachs coordinates are the linear combinations
\begin{equation}
  G_E^N(Q^2)=F_1^N(-Q^2)-\tau F_2^N(-Q^2),
  \qquad
  G_M^N(Q^2)=F_1^N(-Q^2)+F_2^N(-Q^2).
  \label{eq:qcd-nucleon-sachs-form-factors}
\end{equation}
They are useful Breit-frame coordinates for elastic electron--nucleon
scattering, but the nonperturbative definition is the current matrix element
\eqref{eq:qcd-nucleon-dirac-pauli-form-factors}.  A lattice, dispersive, or
experimental extraction must state the current renormalization, finite-volume
matrix-element method, excited-state removal, and analytic continuation or
fit ansatz used to obtain the functions of \(Q^2\).
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Sachs and Dirac--Pauli coordinates]
\label{prop:qcd-nucleon-sachs-coordinate-transform}
For \(\tau\ne -1\), the coordinate change
\eqref{eq:qcd-nucleon-sachs-form-factors} is invertible:
\begin{equation}
  F_1^N(-Q^2)
  =
  \frac{G_E^N(Q^2)+\tau G_M^N(Q^2)}{1+\tau},
  \qquad
  F_2^N(-Q^2)
  =
  \frac{G_M^N(Q^2)-G_E^N(Q^2)}{1+\tau}.
  \label{eq:qcd-nucleon-sachs-inverse}
\end{equation}
At \(Q^2=0\),
\[
  G_E^N(0)=F_1^N(0),\qquad
  G_M^N(0)=F_1^N(0)+F_2^N(0).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The two equations in \eqref{eq:qcd-nucleon-sachs-form-factors} form the
linear system
\[
  \begin{pmatrix}G_E\\G_M\end{pmatrix}
  =
  \begin{pmatrix}1&-\tau\\ 1&1\end{pmatrix}
  \begin{pmatrix}F_1\\F_2\end{pmatrix}.
\]
The determinant is \(1+\tau\).  Inverting the matrix gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-nucleon-sachs-inverse}.  Setting \(Q^2=0\), hence \(\tau=0\),
gives the stated zero-transfer normalizations.  No model of nucleon
substructure enters this argument; it is only a change of coordinates on the
same current matrix element.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Isovector axial form factors]
\label{def:qcd-nucleon-axial-form-factors}
Let \(A_a^\mu\) be the renormalized isovector axial current, with
\(a=1,2,3\) and flavor generator \(\tau_a/2\).  Between one-nucleon states,
parity, Lorentz covariance, and isospin give the decomposition
\begin{equation}
  \langle N(p',s')|A_a^\mu(0)|N(p,s)\rangle
  =
  \frac{\ii}{(2\pi)^3}\,
  \bar u_{s'}(p')
  \left[
    \gamma^\mu\gamma_5\,G_A(Q^2)
    +
    \frac{k^\mu}{2M_N}\gamma_5\,G_P(Q^2)
  \right]
  \frac{\tau_a}{2}\,
  u_s(p),
  \label{eq:qcd-nucleon-axial-form-factors}
\end{equation}
again with \(Q^2=-k^2\).  The number \(g_A:=G_A(0)\) is the axial charge in
this current normalization.  The induced pseudoscalar form factor \(G_P\)
contains the pion-pole contribution dictated by the chiral Ward identity and
the pion effective theory of Chapter~\ref{ch:volume-ii-21}; beyond that pole,
its regular part is another QCD matrix element.  Thus nucleon axial data are
part of the same ab initio program as the mass spectrum: they are not
defined by a quark-model wave function but by renormalized current insertions
between color-singlet Hilbert-space states.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Stable-current three-point extraction]
\label{prop:qcd-stable-current-three-point-extraction}
Let a reflection-positive finite-volume regulator of QCD on a spatial torus
\(\mathbb T_L^3\) be fixed, with Hilbert space \(\mathcal H_L\), vacuum
\(\Omega_L\), self-adjoint Hamiltonian \(H_L\ge0\), and momentum operators
\(\mathbf P_L\).  Let \(J_{\mathcal R}\) be a renormalized, gauge-invariant
current in a specified operator-renormalization scheme \(\mathcal R\), and let
\(J_{\mathcal R,\mathbf q}\) denote its spatial Fourier component carrying
momentum \(\mathbf q\).  Choose momenta
\(\mathbf p,\mathbf p'\in(2\pi/L)\mathbb Z^3\) with
\(\mathbf p'=\mathbf p+\mathbf q\).  Suppose that in the two relevant
baryon-number-one momentum sectors there are normalized one-nucleon eigenvectors
\[
  H_L|N,L;\mathbf p,r\rangle=E_L(\mathbf p)|N,L;\mathbf p,r\rangle,\qquad
  H_L|N,L;\mathbf p',r'\rangle=E_L(\mathbf p')|N,L;\mathbf p',r'\rangle,
\]
isolated from the rest of the spectrum in the same quantum-number channels by
positive gaps \(\Delta_L(\mathbf p)\) and \(\Delta_L(\mathbf p')\).  Here
\(r,r'\) label chosen rows in the relevant finite-volume symmetry irreducible
representations; after the \(L\to\infty\) limit these rows are matched to the
usual spin labels.  Let \(\mathcal O_{\mathbf p,r}^\dagger\) and
\(\mathcal O_{\mathbf p',r'}^\dagger\) be gauge-invariant baryon sources,
projected to the indicated momentum and row, and set
\[
  \psi_{\mathbf p,r}:=\mathcal O_{\mathbf p,r}^\dagger\Omega_L,\qquad
  \psi_{\mathbf p',r'}:=\mathcal O_{\mathbf p',r'}^\dagger\Omega_L.
\]
Assume their one-particle overlaps
\[
  Z_{\mathbf p,r}:=\langle N,L;\mathbf p,r|\psi_{\mathbf p,r}\rangle,\qquad
  Z_{\mathbf p',r'}:=
  \langle N,L;\mathbf p',r'|\psi_{\mathbf p',r'}\rangle
\]
are nonzero.  At fixed regulator, assume \(J_{\mathcal R,\mathbf q}\) is
bounded on the finite-energy subspace generated by these sources; on a lattice
with compact gauge variables and local fermion bilinears this is the ordinary
boundedness statement for the regulated local insertion.

Define the Euclidean two- and three-point functions
\begin{align}
  C_2(t;\mathbf p,r)
  &:=
  \langle\psi_{\mathbf p,r},e^{-H_Lt}\psi_{\mathbf p,r}\rangle,
  \label{eq:qcd-two-point-transfer-matrix-form}\\
  C_3^{J_{\mathcal R}}(t,\tau;\mathbf p',r';\mathbf p,r)
  &:=
  \langle
    \psi_{\mathbf p',r'},
    e^{-H_L(t-\tau)}J_{\mathcal R,\mathbf q}e^{-H_L\tau}
    \psi_{\mathbf p,r}
  \rangle,
  \qquad 0<\tau<t .
  \label{eq:qcd-three-point-transfer-matrix-form}
\end{align}
Then
\begin{equation}
  C_2(t;\mathbf p,r)
  =
  |Z_{\mathbf p,r}|^2e^{-E_L(\mathbf p)t}
  +R_2(t;\mathbf p,r),
  \qquad
  |R_2(t;\mathbf p,r)|
  \le
  \|\eta_{\mathbf p,r}\|^2
  e^{-(E_L(\mathbf p)+\Delta_L(\mathbf p))t},
  \label{eq:qcd-two-point-gap-estimate}
\end{equation}
where
\(\eta_{\mathbf p,r}:=(1-P_{\mathbf p,r})\psi_{\mathbf p,r}\) and
\(P_{\mathbf p,r}\) is the spectral projection onto
\(|N,L;\mathbf p,r\rangle\).  Moreover
\begin{align}
  C_3^{J_{\mathcal R}}(t,\tau;\mathbf p',r';\mathbf p,r)
  &=
  \overline{Z_{\mathbf p',r'}}Z_{\mathbf p,r}\,
  e^{-E_L(\mathbf p')(t-\tau)}e^{-E_L(\mathbf p)\tau}
  \langle N,L;\mathbf p',r'|
    J_{\mathcal R,\mathbf q}
  |N,L;\mathbf p,r\rangle
  \nonumber\\
  &\hspace{1cm}
  +R_3(t,\tau;\mathbf p',r';\mathbf p,r),
  \label{eq:qcd-three-point-gap-expansion}
\end{align}
with the explicit bound
\begin{align}
  |R_3|
  \le
  \|J_{\mathcal R,\mathbf q}\|
  \Big(&
    \|\eta_{\mathbf p',r'}\|\,|Z_{\mathbf p,r}|\,
    e^{-(E_L(\mathbf p')+\Delta_L(\mathbf p'))(t-\tau)}
    e^{-E_L(\mathbf p)\tau}
  \nonumber\\
  &+
    |Z_{\mathbf p',r'}|\,\|\eta_{\mathbf p,r}\|\,
    e^{-E_L(\mathbf p')(t-\tau)}
    e^{-(E_L(\mathbf p)+\Delta_L(\mathbf p))\tau}
  \nonumber\\
  &+
    \|\eta_{\mathbf p',r'}\|\,\|\eta_{\mathbf p,r}\|\,
    e^{-(E_L(\mathbf p')+\Delta_L(\mathbf p'))(t-\tau)}
    e^{-(E_L(\mathbf p)+\Delta_L(\mathbf p))\tau}
  \Big).
  \label{eq:qcd-three-point-gap-bound}
\end{align}
Consequently the ratio
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal R_{J_{\mathcal R}}(t,\tau)
  :=
  \frac{
    C_3^{J_{\mathcal R}}(t,\tau;\mathbf p',r';\mathbf p,r)}
  {
    \overline{Z_{\mathbf p',r'}}Z_{\mathbf p,r}\,
    e^{-E_L(\mathbf p')(t-\tau)}e^{-E_L(\mathbf p)\tau}}
  \label{eq:qcd-three-point-matrix-element-ratio}
\end{equation}
satisfies
\[
  \mathcal R_{J_{\mathcal R}}(t,\tau)
  =
  \langle N,L;\mathbf p',r'|
    J_{\mathcal R,\mathbf q}
  |N,L;\mathbf p,r\rangle
  +O(e^{-\Delta_L(\mathbf p')(t-\tau)})
  +O(e^{-\Delta_L(\mathbf p)\tau})
\]
as \(\tau\to\infty\) and \(t-\tau\to\infty\), with constants fixed by the
source norms, overlaps, and regulated-current norm above.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The proof is the spectral theorem for the finite-volume transfer-matrix
Hamiltonian.  We give the details because this is the mathematical content
behind the phrase ``extracting a form factor''.  Decompose the source vectors
into their one-particle components and orthogonal remainders,
\[
  \psi_{\mathbf p,r}
  =
  Z_{\mathbf p,r}|N,L;\mathbf p,r\rangle+\eta_{\mathbf p,r},
  \qquad
  \psi_{\mathbf p',r'}
  =
  Z_{\mathbf p',r'}|N,L;\mathbf p',r'\rangle+\eta_{\mathbf p',r'}.
\]
By the assumed spectral gaps, the spectral support of
\(\eta_{\mathbf p,r}\) lies in
\([E_L(\mathbf p)+\Delta_L(\mathbf p),\infty)\), and similarly for
\(\eta_{\mathbf p',r'}\).  Hence
\[
  \|e^{-H_Ls}\eta_{\mathbf p,r}\|
  \le
  e^{-(E_L(\mathbf p)+\Delta_L(\mathbf p))s}\|\eta_{\mathbf p,r}\|,
  \qquad s\ge0,
\]
and the corresponding estimate holds in the primed channel.  Substituting the
decomposition of \(\psi_{\mathbf p,r}\) into
\eqref{eq:qcd-two-point-transfer-matrix-form} gives the leading term
\(|Z_{\mathbf p,r}|^2e^{-E_L(\mathbf p)t}\).  The cross terms vanish because
\(\eta_{\mathbf p,r}\) is orthogonal to the one-particle eigenspace and
\(e^{-H_Lt}\) preserves the spectral decomposition.  The remaining
\(\eta\)-term is bounded by the preceding estimate, proving
\eqref{eq:qcd-two-point-gap-estimate}.

For the three-point function, insert the same decompositions on the sink and
source sides of \eqref{eq:qcd-three-point-transfer-matrix-form}.  The term in
which both spectral projections are one-particle projections is exactly the
first line of \eqref{eq:qcd-three-point-gap-expansion}.  The three remaining
terms contain an excited component on the sink side, on the source side, or on
both sides.  Applying the gap estimate to the side on which the excited
component propagates, and applying Cauchy's inequality together with the
regulated operator norm of \(J_{\mathcal R,\mathbf q}\), gives the three
terms in \eqref{eq:qcd-three-point-gap-bound}.  Division by the nonzero
leading overlap factor gives \eqref{eq:qcd-three-point-matrix-element-ratio}
and the stated asymptotic error.  Nothing in the argument assumes a constituent
description of the nucleon; the only inputs are reflection positivity,
spectral isolation, a renormalized gauge-invariant current insertion, and
nonzero overlap of the chosen source with the state.
\end{proof}

The continuum nucleon form factors of
Definition~\ref{def:qcd-nucleon-current-matrix-element-datum} are obtained
from the finite-volume matrix element in
Proposition~\ref{prop:qcd-stable-current-three-point-extraction} only after
the current-renormalization scheme has been fixed and the regulator and
volume limits have been taken with the chosen state normalization.  A plateau
in a ratio of Euclidean correlators is therefore evidence for the hypotheses
of the proposition in a numerical calculation; it is not itself the definition
of the form factor.

\begin{definition}[Forward Compton and polarizability datum]
\label{def:qcd-forward-compton-polarizability-datum}
Let \(N\) be a stable proton or neutron state of mass \(M_N\) and spin
\(\frac12\).  Work in the nucleon rest frame and let a real photon have energy
\(\omega>0\), direction \(\mathbf n\in S^2\), and transverse polarization
representatives \(\boldsymbol\epsilon,\boldsymbol\epsilon'\) satisfying
\(\mathbf n\cdot\boldsymbol\epsilon
=\mathbf n\cdot\boldsymbol\epsilon'=0\).  The forward real-Compton amplitude
is the on-shell, connected, LSZ-reduced matrix element of two insertions of
the renormalized electromagnetic current \(J_{\rm em}^\mu\), with the photon
coupling and the one-nucleon state normalization fixed by the scattering
chapters.  For a spin state with unit spin vector \(\mathbf s\), define the
scalar forward amplitudes \(f_N(\omega)\) and \(g_N(\omega)\) by
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal A_{\gamma N\to\gamma N}^{\rm fwd}
  =
  \boldsymbol\epsilon'^{\,*}\!\cdot\boldsymbol\epsilon\, f_N(\omega)
  +
  \ii\,\mathbf s\cdot
  \bigl(\boldsymbol\epsilon'^{\,*}\times\boldsymbol\epsilon\bigr)\,
  g_N(\omega).
  \label{eq:qcd-forward-compton-fg-definition}
\end{equation}
This equation is a definition of the normalization of \(f_N,g_N\).  Let
\[
  f_N^{\rm nb}(\omega):=f_N(\omega)-f_N^{\rm Born}(\omega)
\]
denote the non-Born amplitude after subtracting the one-nucleon pole
contribution, whose normalization is specified in the low-energy expansion
below.  With this normalization the optical-theorem convention for the
absorptive non-Born amplitude is
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname{Im}f_N^{\rm nb}(\omega+\ii0)
  =
  \frac{\omega}{4\pi}\,
  \sigma_{\gamma N}^{\rm abs}(\omega),
  \qquad
  \omega\ge\omega_{\rm th},
  \label{eq:qcd-forward-compton-optical-theorem}
\end{equation}
where \(\omega_{\rm th}\) is the first inelastic threshold and
\(\sigma_{\gamma N}^{\rm abs}\) is the total real-photon absorption cross
section in the same convention, not the elastic Compton cross section.  The
spin-dependent optical theorem similarly uses the helicity-difference
absorption cross section
\(\Delta\sigma_{\gamma N}:=\sigma_{1/2}-\sigma_{3/2}\):
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname{Im}g_N(\omega+\ii0)
  =
  \frac{\omega}{8\pi}\,
  \Delta\sigma_{\gamma N}(\omega).
  \label{eq:qcd-forward-spin-compton-optical-theorem}
\end{equation}

The spin-independent electric-plus-magnetic polarizability is the coefficient
of the first non-Born term in the low-energy expansion
\begin{equation}
  f_N(\omega)
  =
  f_N^{\rm Born}(\omega)
  +
  \bigl(\alpha_E^N+\beta_M^N\bigr)\omega^2
  +O(\omega^4).
  \label{eq:qcd-forward-polarizability-definition}
\end{equation}
The Born amplitude is the one-nucleon pole contribution determined by the
charge \(F_1^N(0)\), magnetic moment \(F_1^N(0)+F_2^N(0)\), and the same
Compton Ward identity used in the QED external-state chapter.  Equation
\eqref{eq:qcd-forward-polarizability-definition} defines only the sum
\(\alpha_E^N+\beta_M^N\).  Separating \(\alpha_E^N\) from \(\beta_M^N\)
requires either non-forward Compton amplitudes or a background-field
definition with separately specified electric and magnetic external fields.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Baldin sum rule as a forward-dispersion theorem]
\label{prop:qcd-baldin-forward-dispersion}
Assume that the spin-independent forward Compton amplitude
\(f_N^{\rm nb}(\omega)\) is an even function of \(\omega\) analytic in the
complex \(\omega\)-plane cut along
\((-\infty,-\omega_{\rm th}]\cup[\omega_{\rm th},\infty)\), real on the
real interval \(|\omega|<\omega_{\rm th}\), and sufficiently bounded at
infinity so that the once-subtracted Cauchy formula below has no boundary
term.  Then
\begin{equation}
  f_N^{\rm nb}(\omega)-f_N^{\rm nb}(0)
  =
  \frac{2\omega^2}{\pi}
  \int_{\omega_{\rm th}}^\infty
  \frac{\operatorname{Im}f_N^{\rm nb}(\omega'+\ii0)}
       {\omega'(\omega'^2-\omega^2)}
  \,\dd\omega',
  \qquad |\omega|<\omega_{\rm th}.
  \label{eq:qcd-forward-compton-subtracted-dispersion}
\end{equation}
If the small-\(\omega\) expansion
\eqref{eq:qcd-forward-polarizability-definition} exists and the integral may
be expanded at \(\omega=0\), then
\begin{equation}
  \alpha_E^N+\beta_M^N
  =
  \frac{1}{2\pi^2}
  \int_{\omega_{\rm th}}^\infty
  \frac{\sigma_{\gamma N}^{\rm abs}(\omega')}{\omega'^2}\,\dd\omega' .
  \label{eq:qcd-baldin-sum-rule}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Set \(F(\omega):=f_N^{\rm nb}(\omega)-f_N^{\rm nb}(0)\).  By crossing in the
forward channel \(F\) is even.  Apply Cauchy's theorem to
\(F(z)/(z^2-\omega^2)\) on a contour surrounding the two cuts and use the
assumed large-\(|z|\) bound to drop the circle at infinity.  The discontinuity
on the positive cut is
\[
  F(\omega'+\ii0)-F(\omega'-\ii0)
  =
  2\ii\,\operatorname{Im}f_N^{\rm nb}(\omega'+\ii0).
\]
The negative cut gives the same contribution after the change
\(\omega'\mapsto-\omega'\), because \(F\) is even.  The residues at
\(z=\pm\omega\) then give
\eqref{eq:qcd-forward-compton-subtracted-dispersion}.  For
\(|\omega|<\omega_{\rm th}\),
\[
  \frac{1}{\omega'^2-\omega^2}
  =
  \frac{1}{\omega'^2}
  +O(\omega^2),
\]
under the stated integrability assumption.  Therefore the coefficient of
\(\omega^2\) in \(F(\omega)\) is
\[
  \frac{2}{\pi}
  \int_{\omega_{\rm th}}^\infty
  \frac{\operatorname{Im}f_N^{\rm nb}(\omega'+\ii0)}{\omega'^3}\,\dd\omega' .
\]
Using the optical theorem
\eqref{eq:qcd-forward-compton-optical-theorem} gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-baldin-sum-rule}.  The proof shows precisely where the analytic
and high-energy hypotheses enter; QCD supplies the current matrix elements,
while the dispersion relation is an additional analyticity statement about the
real-photon forward amplitude.
\end{proof}

The spin-dependent amplitude \(g_N\) is handled in the same way after the
elastic pole term has been fixed by \(F_1^N(0)\) and \(F_2^N(0)\).  Its
low-energy coefficients define forward spin polarizabilities, and its
dispersion relations involve
\(\Delta\sigma_{\gamma N}=\sigma_{1/2}-\sigma_{3/2}\).  The monograph keeps
this as a statement about current-current matrix elements and their analytic
continuation; it is not a model of the nucleon as a polarizable medium.

The practical hierarchy of spectroscopic control is therefore:
\begin{itemize}
  \item Stable mesons and baryons are isolated color-singlet mass eigenvalues;
  their controlled extraction uses the finite-volume transfer matrix and
  continuum extrapolation.
  \item Elastic resonances are second-sheet poles of partial waves; their
  controlled extraction uses Luscher, Roy, or Roy--Steiner reconstruction.
  \item Heavy quarkonium is a color-singlet \(Q\bar Q\) spectrum; its
  controlled extraction uses a matched NRQCD or pNRQCD Hamiltonian and
  lattice checks.
  \item Hybrids and glueballs are operator-overlap sectors and pole data; their
  controlled extraction uses lattice GEVP, large-\(N_c\), and mixing analysis.
  \item Exotic near-threshold states are poles plus residues in coupled
  channels; their controlled extraction uses finite-volume coupled-channel
  amplitudes.
\end{itemize}
Every entry in this list is a statement about QCD observables.  The words
``quark model'', ``molecule'', ``diquark'', and ``flux-tube excitation'' may
summarize patterns in a chosen coordinate system, but the monograph treats
them as derived interpretations only after the corresponding spectral or pole
datum has been defined.

\section{Detector Observables and Energy Correlators}

A nonperturbative formulation of high-energy QCD final states begins with
detector measurements in the physical Hilbert space.  The calorimetric
observable is built from the renormalized, gauge-invariant stress tensor
\(T^{\mu\nu}\), whose normalization is fixed by the translation generators:
\[
  P^\nu=\int_{\R^3}\dd^3x\,T^{0\nu}(t,\mathbf x)
\]
on the common domain of finite-energy states where the integral is defined as
a quadratic form.

\begin{construction}[Energy-flow detector from the stress tensor]
\label{cons:qcd-energy-flow-detector}
For a real test function \(f\in C^\infty(S^2)\), define the formal
null-infinity flux quadratic form by
\begin{equation}
  \widehat{\mathcal E}(f)
  =
  \mathrm{w}\!-\!\lim_{R\to\infty}
  R^2
  \int_{-\infty}^{\infty}\dd t
  \int_{S^2}\dd\Omega(\mathbf n)\,
  f(\mathbf n)\,
  n_i\,\widehat T^{0i}(t,R\mathbf n).
  \label{eq:energy-flow-operator-smeared}
\end{equation}
The notation means that the limit is first tested between finite-energy
physical states.  The operation is part of the detector definition only after
the domain and closure properties below have been supplied.
\end{construction}

\begin{hypothesis}[Detector existence and self-adjointness]
\label{hyp:qcd-energy-flow-detector}
There is a dense scattering domain
\(\mathcal D_{\rm det}\subset\Hilb_{\rm phys}\), stable under finite products
of the smeared detector forms used below, such that for every real
\(f\in C^\infty(S^2)\) the weak limit
\eqref{eq:energy-flow-operator-smeared} exists on
\(\mathcal D_{\rm det}\), is symmetric there, and has a unique self-adjoint
closure.  For each pair \(\Psi,\Phi\in\mathcal D_{\rm det}\), the map
\[
  f\longmapsto
  \bra{\Psi}\widehat{\mathcal E}(f)\ket{\Phi}
\]
is a distribution of finite order on \(S^2\).  The constant test function
satisfies
\[
  \widehat{\mathcal E}(1)=H_{\mathrm{out}}
\]
on outgoing scattering states, where \(H_{\mathrm{out}}\) is the outgoing
Hamiltonian restricted to the physical scattering Hilbert space.
\end{hypothesis}

\begin{theorem}[Detector positivity from ANEC]
\label{thm:qcd-energy-detector-positivity-from-anec}
Assume Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:qcd-energy-flow-detector}.  Assume in addition
that the stress tensor satisfies the averaged null energy condition as a
quadratic-form statement on the same scattering domain: for every future null
direction \(n^\mu\), every nonnegative transverse smearing
\(\varphi\), and every \(\Psi\in\mathcal D_{\rm det}\),
\[
  \int\dd^2x_\perp\,\varphi(x_\perp)
  \int_{-\infty}^{\infty}\dd\lambda\,
  \bra{\Psi}T_{\mu\nu}(x_\perp+\lambda n)n^\mu n^\nu\ket{\Psi}
  \geq0 .
\]
Then the self-adjoint closure of \(\widehat{\mathcal E}(f)\) is positive for
every \(f\geq0\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Write a nonnegative smooth angular test function as a finite sum of functions
supported in coordinate patches on \(S^2\), using a partition of unity.  In
each patch, the large-\(R\) detector limit is the conformal or asymptotic
image of a null-energy integral along the complete generator labelled by
\(\mathbf n\), with transverse smearing determined by the angular support of
\(f\).  The Jacobian relating the angular measure to transverse measure is
positive.  The ANEC inequality therefore gives nonnegative quadratic form
values for each patch.  Summing the patch contributions gives
\[
  \bra{\Psi}\widehat{\mathcal E}(f)\ket{\Psi}\geq0
  \qquad (\Psi\in\mathcal D_{\rm det},\ f\geq0).
\]
Since the operator has a unique self-adjoint closure by
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:qcd-energy-flow-detector}, positivity of the quadratic
form on a core implies positivity of the closure by the spectral theorem.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Status in QCD and in conformal theories]
\label{rem:qcd-energy-flow-status}
For free massless fields, the limit in
\eqref{eq:energy-flow-operator-smeared} is obtained by inserting the mode
expansion and applying stationary phase at null infinity.  For conformal
field theories satisfying the light-transform hypotheses of
Chapter~\ref{ch:cft-light-ray-energy-correlators}, the detector is the
stress-tensor light-ray operator and positivity is supplied by the ANEC
theorem stated there.  In four-dimensional QCD, the detector is the expected
physical calorimeter observable, but its nonperturbative construction depends
on the existence of the continuum theory, the physical scattering space, and
the hadronic asymptotic completeness problem stated in
Open Problem~\ref{op:qcd-asymptotic-completeness}.  Perturbative KLN
cancellation proves finiteness of regulator-expanded coefficients for
IRC-continuous measurements after the relevant sums over degenerate states
and the required factorization steps have been made; it does not construct
the self-adjoint detector operator on the exact physical Hilbert space.
\end{remark}

\begin{openproblem}[Energy-flow operators in four-dimensional QCD]
\label{op:qcd-energy-flow-operator-construction}
Construct the operators \(\widehat{\mathcal E}(f)\) of
Construction~\ref{cons:qcd-energy-flow-detector} in continuum
four-dimensional QCD.  The construction should start from a nonperturbative
definition of the physical Hilbert space, identify a dense finite-energy
scattering domain, prove the null-infinity weak limits, prove essential
self-adjointness or specify the self-adjoint extension selected by detector
physics, prove positivity from an ANEC theorem in the same framework, and
show that \(\widehat{\mathcal E}(1)\) agrees with the outgoing Hamiltonian on
the hadronic scattering subspace.
\end{openproblem}

Here \(\mathbf n\in S^2\) is a unit spatial direction and \(\dd\Omega\) is the
rotation-invariant measure on \(S^2\).  The distribution
\(\widehat{\mathcal E}(\mathbf n)\) is defined by
\(\widehat{\mathcal E}(f)=\int_{S^2}\dd\Omega(\mathbf n)
f(\mathbf n)\widehat{\mathcal E}(\mathbf n)\).  On an outgoing state of
stable hadrons with momenta \(p_r\), species labels \(a_r\), and the
normalization conventions of scattering theory,
\begin{equation}
  \widehat{\mathcal E}(f)
  \ket{p_1,a_1;\ldots;p_N,a_N}_{\mathrm{out}}
  =
  \left(\sum_{r=1}^N p_r^0\,f(\widehat{\mathbf p}_r)\right)
  \ket{p_1,a_1;\ldots;p_N,a_N}_{\mathrm{out}},
  \qquad
  \widehat{\mathbf p}_r:=\frac{\mathbf p_r}{|\mathbf p_r|}.
  \label{eq:energy-flow-on-hadron-state}
\end{equation}
Equation~\eqref{eq:energy-flow-on-hadron-state} is the spectral action of the
detector limit on physical hadronic asymptotic states.  The corresponding
classical calorimetric measure of the final state \(X\) is
\[
  \mu_X
  =
  \sum_{r\in X}p_r^0\,\delta_{\widehat{\mathbf p}_r},
  \qquad
  \widehat{\mathcal E}_X(f)=\int_{S^2}f\,\dd\mu_X .
\]
The detector observable depends on \(X\) only through the positive measure
\(\mu_X\).

Given a normalized incoming physical state \(\Psi_{\mathrm{in}}\), or a state
prepared by a local color-singlet current and then evolved to future infinity,
the \(k\)-point energy correlator is the distribution on \((S^2)^k\)
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal G_k(f_1,\ldots,f_k;\Psi)
  =
  {}_{\mathrm{out}}\!\bra{\Psi}
  \widehat{\mathcal E}(f_1)\cdots
  \widehat{\mathcal E}(f_k)
  \ket{\Psi}_{\mathrm{out}} .
  \label{eq:energy-correlator-definition}
\end{equation}
After inserting a complete set of physical hadronic out-states, this becomes
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal G_k(f_1,\ldots,f_k;\Psi)
  =
  \sum_X
  |\braket{X,\mathrm{out}}{\Psi,\mathrm{out}}|^2
  \prod_{\ell=1}^k
  \left(
    \sum_{r\in X} p_r^0\,f_\ell(\widehat{\mathbf p}_r)
  \right),
  \label{eq:energy-correlator-hadron-sum}
\end{equation}
with the usual replacement of the displayed sum by direct integrals over
continuous multiparticle phase space.  This formula is nonperturbative: all
states in \(X\) are physical hadronic states, and the operator being measured
is built from \(T^{\mu\nu}\).

\begin{lemma}[Soft and collinear continuity of smeared energy flow]
\label{lem:energy-flow-irc-continuity}
Let \(f\in C^1(S^2)\).  Suppose a final-state calorimetric measure
\(\mu_X\) is changed either by adding one particle of energy \(\varepsilon\) at
direction \(\mathbf m\), or by replacing two particles of energies \(E_a,E_b\)
and directions \(\mathbf n_a,\mathbf n_b\) by one particle of energy
\(E_a+E_b\) in the direction
\[
  \mathbf n_{ab}
  =
  \frac{E_a\mathbf n_a+E_b\mathbf n_b}
       {|E_a\mathbf n_a+E_b\mathbf n_b|}.
\]
Then
\[
  \left|\Delta\widehat{\mathcal E}_X(f)\right|
  \leq
  \varepsilon \|f\|_\infty
\]
in the soft case, and
\[
  \left|\Delta\widehat{\mathcal E}_X(f)\right|
  \leq
  (E_a+E_b)\operatorname{Lip}(f)\,
  \operatorname{diam}\{\mathbf n_a,\mathbf n_b,\mathbf n_{ab}\}
\]
in the collinear case.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
For a soft particle, the measure changes by
\(\varepsilon\delta_{\mathbf m}\), so the change of the detector value is
\(\varepsilon f(\mathbf m)\).  For a collinear recombination, the change is
\[
  E_a f(\mathbf n_a)+E_b f(\mathbf n_b)
  -(E_a+E_b)f(\mathbf n_{ab}).
\]
Adding and subtracting
\((E_a+E_b)f(\mathbf n_{ab})\) gives the displayed bound from the Lipschitz
constant of \(f\).  The bound tends to zero uniformly for bounded total energy
when the opening angle tends to zero.
\end{proof}

The same estimate applies to products
\(\prod_{\ell=1}^k\widehat{\mathcal E}_X(f_\ell)\) on any fixed
finite-energy sector by the elementary telescoping identity
\[
  \prod_{\ell=1}^k A_\ell-\prod_{\ell=1}^k B_\ell
  =
  \sum_{j=1}^k
  \left(\prod_{\ell<j}A_\ell\right)
  (A_j-B_j)
  \left(\prod_{\ell>j}B_\ell\right),
\]
with \(A_\ell=\widehat{\mathcal E}_{X'}(f_\ell)\) and
\(B_\ell=\widehat{\mathcal E}_X(f_\ell)\).  Thus smeared energy correlators
are continuous functions of the calorimetric measure for soft and collinear
degenerations.  Perturbative finiteness then has a precise theorem boundary:
at each fixed order in a regulator for which the Kinoshita--Lee--Nauenberg
cancellation and QCD factorization hold for the chosen inclusive channel,
measurement functions with the above continuity produce finite coefficients
after summing over degenerate final states and virtual corrections.  The
operator definition \eqref{eq:energy-correlator-definition} is the
nonperturbative observable; perturbation theory computes its short-distance
expansion in the regime where asymptotic freedom supplies a controlled small
coupling.

The unsmeared product
\(\widehat{\mathcal E}(\mathbf n_1)\cdots
\widehat{\mathcal E}(\mathbf n_k)\) is a distribution.  Coincident directions
carry contact singularities because several detector insertions can act on the
same hadron.  The separated-angle correlator is obtained by testing against
functions supported away from the coincidence diagonals in \((S^2)^k\); fully
smeared correlators include the contact terms determined by the detector
operator product itself.

\subsection{Energy-Energy Correlation in Electron-Positron Annihilation}

Let a color-singlet current create a state of total center-of-mass energy
\(Q\).  For each physical hadronic final state \(X\), write
\[
  z_r=\frac{p_r^0}{Q},
  \qquad
  \cos\chi_{rs}=
  \widehat{\mathbf p}_r\cdot\widehat{\mathbf p}_s .
\]
The normalized two-point energy-energy correlator is the distribution
\begin{equation}
  \mathrm{EEC}(\chi)
  =
  \frac{1}{\sigma_{\mathrm{tot}}}
  \sum_X
  \int \dd\sigma_X\,
  \sum_{r,s\in X}
  z_r z_s\,
  \delta(\cos\chi-\cos\chi_{rs}),
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-definition}
\end{equation}
where \(\dd\sigma_X\) is the differential cross-section measure for the
exclusive hadronic channel \(X\), and the sum is a direct integral over
continuous phase space.  The terms \(r=s\) are the coincident-detector contact
part at \(\chi=0\).  A convention that removes this contact part defines a
different distribution at \(\chi=0\) and the same separated-angle function for
\(0<\chi<\pi\).

Equation~\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-definition} is the detector form of the
Basham--Brown--Ellis--Love observable.  Its perturbative expansion in
asymptotically free QCD is a calculation of the current-created state and of
the detector insertions in the short-distance region.  The back-to-back limit
\(\chi\to\pi\) is controlled by soft and collinear radiation constrained by
transverse momentum conservation; the small-angle limit is controlled by a
collinear operator product of energy-flow insertions.  Both limits require
resummation because the separated-angle distribution contains large logarithms
of \(1+\cos\chi\) or \(1-\cos\chi\), respectively.

\begin{proposition}[EEC sum rules and the contact term]
\label{prop:qcd-eec-sum-rules}
Let \(X\) be a physical final state in the center-of-mass frame of a
color-singlet source, with total energy \(Q\) and total spatial momentum zero.
Set
\[
  z_r=\frac{p_r^0}{Q},
  \qquad
  \mathbf n_r=\frac{\mathbf p_r}{|\mathbf p_r|},
  \qquad
  \zeta_{rs}=\mathbf n_r\cdot\mathbf n_s .
\]
Define the eventwise two-point calorimetric distribution in
\(\zeta=\cos\chi\) by
\[
  E_{2,X}(\zeta)
  =
  \sum_{r,s\in X}z_r z_s\,\delta(\zeta-\zeta_{rs}) .
  \label{eq:eventwise-eec-zeta-distribution}
\]
Then, as distributional moments on \([-1,1]\),
\[
  \int_{-1}^{1} E_{2,X}(\zeta)\,\dd\zeta=1,
  \qquad
  \int_{-1}^{1}\zeta\,E_{2,X}(\zeta)\,\dd\zeta=0 .
  \label{eq:eventwise-eec-first-sum-rules}
\]
The coincident-detector contact part at \(\zeta=1\) has weight
\[
  E_{2,X}^{\rm contact}(\zeta)
  =
  \left(\sum_{r\in X}z_r^2\right)\delta(\zeta-1).
  \label{eq:eventwise-eec-contact-weight}
\]
Consequently the cross-section averaged EEC of
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-definition}, including the \(r=s\) terms, satisfies the same
zeroth and first moment sum rules after division by \(\sigma_{\rm tot}\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The total-energy condition gives
\[
  \sum_{r\in X}z_r=1.
\]
Testing \eqref{eq:eventwise-eec-zeta-distribution} against the constant
function \(1\) gives
\[
  \sum_{r,s}z_rz_s
  =
  \left(\sum_r z_r\right)^2
  =
  1.
\]
Testing against \(\zeta\) gives
\[
  \sum_{r,s}z_rz_s\,\mathbf n_r\cdot\mathbf n_s
  =
  \left|\sum_r z_r\mathbf n_r\right|^2.
\]
Since the source is in its center-of-mass frame,
\[
  \sum_r p_r^0\mathbf n_r=\sum_r\mathbf p_r=0,
\]
and the first moment vanishes.  The contact contribution is exactly the
subsum with \(r=s\), for which \(\zeta_{rr}=1\).  Averaging the eventwise
identities with the positive cross-section measure and dividing by
\(\sigma_{\rm tot}\) preserves the two moment identities.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Use of the sum rules]
\label{rem:eec-sum-rules-use}
The sum rules in Proposition~\ref{prop:qcd-eec-sum-rules} are statements about
the nonperturbative detector observable, not about partons.  A fixed-order
calculation, a resummed endpoint formula, a lattice-inspired approximation, or
a parton shower that claims to represent the normalized EEC must specify how
the \(\zeta=1\) contact term is treated and must satisfy the moment identities
after the same convention is applied.  If the contact term is removed, the
remaining separated-angle distribution no longer has unit integral by itself;
the missing weight is \(\langle\sum_r z_r^2\rangle\).
\end{remark}

\subsection{Light-Ray Interpretation and Endpoint Regimes}

The detector density \(\widehat{\mathcal E}(\mathbf n)\) is the QCD analogue
of the stress-tensor light transform developed in
Chapter~\ref{ch:cft-light-ray-energy-correlators}.  In a conformal theory the
light transform is an operator-valued distribution controlled by Lorentzian
conformal representation theory.  In QCD the coupling runs, so the same
formula is not a conformal operator identity.  It remains an asymptotic
detector definition in the physical Hilbert space, and the short-distance
limits are computed by matching the detector product onto operators whose
renormalization group evolution is controlled by QCD anomalous dimensions.

For \(0<\chi<\pi\), the EEC is a separated-angle distribution.  Two endpoint
regions have different expansions.  In the small-angle region set
\[
  \theta^2:=2(1-\cos\chi)\ll1 .
\]
The product of two nearby detector insertions is matched onto a sum of
collinear light-ray operators:
\begin{equation}
  \widehat{\mathcal E}(\mathbf n_1)\widehat{\mathcal E}(\mathbf n_2)
  \sim
  \sum_A C_A(\theta,Q,\mu)\,
  \mathbb O_A(\mathbf n,\mu),
  \qquad
  \mathbf n_1,\mathbf n_2\to\mathbf n .
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-ope-form}
\end{equation}
Here \(\mathbb O_A\) are light-ray operators in the collinear direction,
including twist-two energy-flow moments and their descendants in the
appropriate channel.  The symbol \(\sim\) denotes an asymptotic expansion
after smearing against angular test functions supported at
\(\theta\ll1\).  The coefficient functions \(C_A\) are perturbatively
computable at large transverse scale \(Q\theta\), and the evolution of
\(\mathbb O_A\) resums logarithms of \(\theta\).

In the back-to-back region set
\[
  q_T^2:=Q^2(1+\cos\chi)\ll Q^2 .
\]
Momentum conservation forces the two measured energy deposits to recoil
against soft and collinear radiation of small total transverse momentum.  The
factorized form is the transverse-momentum resummation analogue
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\dd\sigma}{\dd q_T^2}
  =
  H(Q,\mu)
  \int \frac{\dd^2 b}{(2\pi)^2}\,
  \ee^{\ii b\cdot q_T}\,
  J_n(b,\mu,\nu)\,
  J_{\bar n}(b,\mu,\nu)\,
  S(b,\mu,\nu)
  +
  O(q_T/Q),
  \label{eq:qcd-eec-back-to-back-factorization}
\end{equation}
for a color-singlet source and in a rapidity-renormalization scheme with
rapidity scale \(\nu\).  The hard, jet, and soft functions have coupled
\(\mu\)- and \(\nu\)-evolution equations; solving them resums Sudakov
logarithms of \(q_T/Q\).  The power remainder and the absence or treatment of
Glauber exchanges are part of the factorization datum.

Here and below \(\alpha_s(\mu):=g^2(\mu)/(4\pi)\) in the trace-delta gauge
coordinate of this chapter.  Whenever a coefficient is proportional to
\(\alpha_s C_F\), it is invariant under conversion to the common half-trace
generator convention because \(g_{\rm ht}^2C_F^{\rm ht}=g^2C_F\), as in
\eqref{eq:pnrqcd-tree-coulomb-potential}.

\begin{proposition}[Tree-level collinear coefficient for the separated EEC]
\label{prop:qcd-eec-tree-collinear-coefficient}
Use the standard four-dimensional, azimuth-integrated, final-state collinear
splitting convention
\begin{equation}
  \dd P_{a\to bc}
  =
  \frac{\alpha_s}{2\pi}\,
  P_{a\to bc}(x)\,\dd x\,\frac{\dd\theta^2}{\theta^2},
  \qquad 0<x<1,
  \label{eq:final-state-collinear-splitting-convention}
\end{equation}
where \(x\) and \(1-x\) are the daughter energy fractions and \(\theta\) is
their small opening angle.  The real-emission contribution of this resolved
splitting to the ordered separated-angle EEC is weighted by
\begin{equation}
  w_{\rm EEC}(x)=2x(1-x).
  \label{eq:eec-ordered-collinear-weight}
\end{equation}
Consequently, for \(\zeta=\cos\chi\) and
\(\theta^2=2(1-\zeta)+O((1-\zeta)^2)\), the leading-power separated-angle
collinear density generated by a parent of type \(a\) has the form
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\dd P_a^{\rm EEC}}{\dd\zeta}
  =
  \frac{\alpha_s}{2\pi}\,
  \frac{\Gamma_a^{\rm EEC}}{1-\zeta}
  +
  \text{terms less singular as }\zeta\to1,
  \label{eq:eec-tree-collinear-density}
\end{equation}
with resolved real-kernel coefficients
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
  \Gamma_q^{\rm EEC}
  &=
  \int_0^1 2x(1-x)\,
  C_F\frac{1+x^2}{1-x}\,\dd x
  =
  \frac32\,C_F,                                      \\
  \Gamma_{g\to gg}^{\rm EEC}
  &=
  \int_0^1 2x(1-x)\,
  2C_A\left[
    \frac{x}{1-x}+\frac{1-x}{x}+x(1-x)
  \right]\dd x
  =
  \frac{14}{5}\,C_A,                                 \\
  \Gamma_{g\to q\bar q}^{\rm EEC}
  &=
  \int_0^1 2x(1-x)\,
  T_F\bigl(x^2+(1-x)^2\bigr)\dd x
  =
  \frac15\,T_F
\end{aligned}
\label{eq:eec-real-collinear-coefficients}
\end{equation}
per quark flavor in the last line.  The endpoint singularities of the real
splitting kernels are integrable in these coefficients because the detector
weight \(2x(1-x)\) vanishes when either daughter carries zero energy.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For one parent of energy \(E\) splitting into two collinear daughters of
energies \(xE\) and \((1-x)E\), the ordered two-detector contribution at the
nonzero opening angle consists of the two ordered pairs \((b,c)\) and
\((c,b)\).  Its energy weight divided by \(E^2\) is therefore
\[
  x(1-x)+(1-x)x=2x(1-x),
\]
which proves \eqref{eq:eec-ordered-collinear-weight}.  The coincident
daughter terms have contact weight
\[
  x^2+(1-x)^2,
\]
and the identity
\[
  x^2+(1-x)^2+2x(1-x)=1
\]
is the local version of the zeroth-moment sum rule in
Proposition~\ref{prop:qcd-eec-sum-rules}: a collinear splitting redistributes
the parent's detector weight between the contact point and the separated
small angle without changing the total two-detector weight.

At leading collinear power the probability measure for the resolved splitting
is \eqref{eq:final-state-collinear-splitting-convention}.  Since
\[
  1-\zeta=1-\cos\theta=\frac{\theta^2}{2}+O(\theta^4),
\]
the positive measure \(\dd\theta^2/\theta^2\), pulled back to the
\(\zeta\)-line near \(\zeta=1\), is
\[
  \frac{\dd\theta^2}{\theta^2}
  =
  \frac{\dd\zeta}{1-\zeta}+O(1)\,\dd\zeta ,
\]
where the equality is an equality of positive densities on intervals
\(\zeta<1\), not an oriented one-form identity.
Multiplying the splitting probability by the ordered EEC weight and retaining
only the leading distribution as \(\zeta\to1\) gives
\eqref{eq:eec-tree-collinear-density} with
\[
  \Gamma_a^{\rm EEC}
  =
  \sum_{a\to bc}
  \int_0^1 2x(1-x)P_{a\to bc}(x)\,\dd x .
\]
Substituting the real tree-level kernels displayed in
\eqref{eq:eec-real-collinear-coefficients} reduces the three coefficients to
elementary polynomial integrals:
\[
  2C_F\int_0^1 x(1+x^2)\,\dd x=\frac32C_F,
\]
\[
  4C_A\int_0^1
  \bigl[x^2+(1-x)^2+x^2(1-x)^2\bigr]\dd x
  =
  \frac{14}{5}C_A,
\]
and
\[
  2T_F\int_0^1
  x(1-x)\bigl(x^2+(1-x)^2\bigr)\dd x
  =
  \frac15T_F .
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:eec-real-collinear-coefficients}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[What the tree coefficient does and does not prove]
\label{rem:eec-tree-collinear-coefficient-status}
Proposition~\ref{prop:qcd-eec-tree-collinear-coefficient} is a derivation of
the first resolved real-emission coefficient in the small-angle expansion
under the stated collinear splitting convention.  It is not the full
small-angle EEC theorem.  Beyond this leading coefficient, one must define the
renormalized light-ray operator basis, include virtual terms and contact
conventions, solve the mixing problem, and match the endpoint expansion to
the separated-angle distribution in a fixed regulator and subtraction scheme.
The exact observable remains the detector distribution
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-definition}.
\end{remark}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Perturbative EEC endpoint calculations]
\label{ca:qcd-eec-endpoint-calculations}
A perturbative endpoint calculation of the EEC consists of a declared
endpoint variable, a factorization or light-ray OPE formula such as
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-light-ray-ope-form} or
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-back-to-back-factorization}, anomalous dimensions and
matching coefficients through specified orders, a prescription for matching
the endpoint expansion to the separated-angle fixed-order distribution, and a
power correction estimate in \(\theta\) or \(q_T/Q\).  The exact observable
remains the hadronic detector distribution
\eqref{eq:qcd-eec-definition}.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\subsection{Multipoint Correlators and Energy-Flow Polynomials}

For a jet or event with a chosen positive energy scale \(E_{\mathrm{ref}}\),
define \(z_i=E_i/E_{\mathrm{ref}}\) and
\(\theta_{ij}\) to be the angular distance between directions \(i\) and \(j\).
For \(\beta>0\), the \(N\)-point energy correlation function used in jet
substructure has the form
\begin{equation}
  e_N^{(\beta)}
  =
  \sum_{i_1<\cdots<i_N}
  z_{i_1}\cdots z_{i_N}
  \prod_{a<b}
  \theta_{i_a i_b}^{\beta}.
  \label{eq:qcd-energy-correlation-function-jet}
\end{equation}
The strict positivity of \(\beta\) makes the observable collinear continuous:
when two labels become collinear, every factor distinguishing the split
vanishes or recombines into the total energy weight.  The soft behavior is
linear in the soft energy weight.  Thus \eqref{eq:qcd-energy-correlation-function-jet}
is infrared and collinear safe in the sense of
Lemma~\ref{lem:energy-flow-irc-continuity}.

More generally, a finite graph \(G\) with vertices
\(\{1,\ldots,N\}\) defines an energy-flow polynomial
\begin{equation}
  \mathrm{EFP}_G^{(\beta)}
  =
  \sum_{i_1,\ldots,i_N}
  z_{i_1}\cdots z_{i_N}
  \prod_{(a,b)\in E(G)}
  \theta_{i_a i_b}^{\beta}.
  \label{eq:qcd-energy-flow-polynomial}
\end{equation}
This is again a polynomial functional of the calorimetric measure and angular
kernel.  It is a useful coordinate system on infrared-collinear safe event
information because it is built from the same positive detector measure
\(\mu_X\) rather than from colored partonic labels.  In an exact QCD
calculation the final states are hadrons; in a short-distance approximation,
quark and gluon variables enter through factorized coefficient functions,
evolution kernels, and power corrections for this color-singlet observable.

\section{Current Correlators and the Hadronic Tensor}

Deep inelastic scattering probes a hadron by a local current.  The process is
inclusive:
\[
  e^-(k,\sigma)+N(P,s)\longrightarrow e^-(k',\sigma')+X,
  \qquad
  q:=k-k',
\]
where \(N\) is the target hadron and \(X\) runs over all hadronic final states
with total momentum \(P_X=P+q\).  The exchange momentum is spacelike,
\[
  Q^2:=-q^2>0,
  \qquad
  x_B:=\frac{Q^2}{2P\cdot q}.
\]
The variable \(x_B\) is the Bjorken scaling variable.

Figure~\ref{fig:qcd-dis-inclusive-kinematics} fixes the inclusive DIS
kinematics used below: the current transfers spacelike momentum \(q\), the
hadronic final state is summed over \(X\), and \(x_B=Q^2/(2P\cdot q)\).

\begin{figure}[H]
  \centering
  \resizebox{0.86\textwidth}{!}{%
  \begin{tikzpicture}[x=1cm,y=1cm,every node/.style={font=\scriptsize},
    photon/.style={decorate,decoration={snake,amplitude=1.35pt,segment length=6pt},
      line width=0.8pt,blue!70!black},
    fermion/.style={line width=0.85pt},
    hadron/.style={line width=0.9pt}]
    \coordinate (eIn) at (-4.3,1.45);
    \coordinate (eV) at (-0.8,1.05);
    \coordinate (eOut) at (3.0,1.72);
    \coordinate (hIn) at (-4.3,-1.2);
    \coordinate (hV) at (-0.8,-0.95);
    \coordinate (hOut) at (3.0,-0.55);

    \draw[fermion,-{Latex[length=2mm]}] (eIn)--(eV);
    \draw[fermion,-{Latex[length=2mm]}] (eV)--(eOut);
    \draw[photon,-{Latex[length=2mm]}] (eV)--(hV);
    \draw[hadron,-{Latex[length=2mm]}] (hIn)--(hV);
    \draw[hadron,-{Latex[length=2mm]}] (hV)--(hOut);
    \fill (eV) circle (2pt);
    \fill (hV) circle (2pt);

    \node[above] at (-3.1,1.45) {\(k,\sigma\)};
    \node[above] at (1.42,1.55) {\(k',\sigma'\)};
    \node[right,blue!70!black] at (-0.63,0.05) {\(q=k-k'\)};
    \node[below] at (-3.1,-1.22) {\(P,s\)};
    \node[below] at (1.40,-0.72) {\(X\)};
    \node[left] at (-4.35,1.45) {electron};
    \node[left] at (-4.35,-1.2) {hadron \(N\)};
    \node[right,align=left] at (3.08,-0.55) {summed hadronic\\final state};
  \end{tikzpicture}
  }
  \caption{Inclusive deep inelastic scattering.  The lepton line is treated
  perturbatively in the electromagnetic coupling, while the hadronic part is
  the current-current matrix element in QCD.}
  \label{fig:qcd-dis-inclusive-kinematics}
\end{figure}

Let the electromagnetic current be
\[
  J^\mu(x)=\sum_I e_I\,\bar q_I(x)\gamma^\mu q_I(x),
\]
where \(e_I\) is the electric charge of flavor \(I\).  At leading order in the
electromagnetic coupling, the amplitude for a fixed hadronic final state has
the form
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal A_{\sigma'\!,X;\sigma,s}
  =
  \bar u_{\sigma'}(k')\,e\gamma_\mu\,u_{\sigma}(k)\,
  \frac{-\ii}{q^2-\ii\epsilon}\,
  \bra{X}J^\mu(0)\ket{P,s}.
  \label{eq:qcd-dis-leading-amplitude}
\end{equation}
After summing over all hadronic final states \(X\) with the fixed transferred
momentum \(q\), the QCD part of the differential cross section is the
spin-averaged positive tensor
\begin{equation}
  W^{\mu\nu}(P,q)
  =
  \frac12\sum_s
  \sum_X (2\pi)^4\delta^{(4)}(P_X-P-q)\,
  \bra{P,s}J^\nu(0)\ket{X}
  \bra{X}J^\mu(0)\ket{P,s}.
  \label{eq:hadronic-tensor-definition}
\end{equation}
where \(\sum_X\) denotes the sum over species and the invariant phase-space
integrals for a complete set of hadronic states, using the same state
normalization as in the scattering chapters.  Completeness and translation
covariance give the equivalent form
\begin{equation}
  W^{\mu\nu}(P,q)
  =
  \frac12\sum_s
  \int\dd^4x\,\ee^{-\ii q\cdot x}
  \bra{P,s}J^\nu(x)J^\mu(0)\ket{P,s},
  \label{eq:hadronic-tensor-current-product}
\end{equation}
in those conventions.  Thus \(W^{\mu\nu}\) is a Wightman matrix element
between hadron states.  Its positivity follows directly from the sum over
\(X\) in
\eqref{eq:hadronic-tensor-definition}.

Current conservation gives
\[
  q_\mu W^{\mu\nu}=q_\nu W^{\mu\nu}=0 .
\]
For an unpolarized target, Lorentz covariance, current conservation, and
parity give two scalar structure functions.  Define
\[
  \Pi^\mu(P,q)
  :=
  P^\mu-\frac{P\cdot q}{q^2}q^\mu .
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
  W^{\mu\nu}(P,q)
  =
  \left(\eta^{\mu\nu}-\frac{q^\mu q^\nu}{q^2}\right)W_1(\nu,Q^2)
  +
  \Pi^\mu(P,q)\Pi^\nu(P,q)\,W_2(\nu,Q^2),
  \qquad
  \nu:=\frac{P\cdot q}{M},
  \label{eq:qcd-dis-tensor-decomposition}
\end{equation}
where \(M^2=P^2\).  Other common normalizations absorb powers of \(M\) and
\(P\cdot q\) into \(W_1,W_2\).

The support condition is kinematic.  If \(N\) is the lightest hadron with the
chosen conserved quantum numbers, then
\[
  (P+q)^2=P_X^2\ge M^2 .
\]
Since \(q^2=-Q^2\), this implies
\[
  2P\cdot q\ge Q^2,
  \qquad
  0<x_B\le1
\]
for the physical inclusive region.

The time-ordered forward Compton amplitude is
\begin{equation}
  T^{\mu\nu}(P,q)
  =
  \frac{\ii}{2}\sum_s
  \int\dd^4x\,\ee^{-\ii q\cdot x}
  \bra{P,s}\operatorname T\,J^\nu(x)J^\mu(0)\ket{P,s}.
  \label{eq:qcd-forward-compton-amplitude}
\end{equation}
Its discontinuity in the energy variable is determined by the same Wightman
matrix elements:
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname{Disc}\,T^{\mu\nu}(P,q)
  =
  2\pi
  \left[
    W^{\mu\nu}(P,q)
    +W^{\nu\mu}(P,-q)
  \right],
  \label{eq:qcd-dis-discontinuity}
\end{equation}
with the second term absent in the physical region \(P\cdot q>0\) for the
spacelike process.  Thus the inclusive cross section is controlled by the
absorptive part of a time-ordered current-current amplitude, and the
observable tensor is the Wightman object
\eqref{eq:hadronic-tensor-definition}.

The Bjorken limit is
\[
  Q^2\to\infty,
  \qquad
  x_B\ \text{fixed}.
\]
The short-distance region \(x\to0\) in
\eqref{eq:qcd-forward-compton-amplitude} is then controlled by the operator
product expansion of the two currents:
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname T\,J^\mu(x)J^\nu(0)
  \sim
  \sum_a C_a^{\mu\nu}(x,\mu)\,\mathcal O_a(0,\mu).
  \label{eq:dis-current-ope}
\end{equation}
The Wilson coefficients \(C_a^{\mu\nu}\) are determined by short-distance
renormalization and can be computed in perturbation theory at large \(Q\).  The
matrix elements
\(\bra{P}\mathcal O_a(0,\mu)\ket{P}\) are long-distance hadronic data.

\section{Twist, Parton Distributions, and Factorization}
\label{sec:qcd-twist-parton-distributions-factorization}

For a local symmetric traceless operator of Lorentz spin \(s\) and scaling
dimension \(\Delta\), its twist is
\[
  \tau:=\Delta-s .
\]
In an interacting theory \(\Delta\) is a renormalized scaling exponent of the
chosen operator basis.  The word ``twist'' in this section is therefore a
statement about the renormalized leading-power expansion, not only about the
engineering dimension of a classical monomial.  In the Bjorken limit, the
leading terms in the OPE are the smallest-twist operators compatible with the
quantum numbers of the currents.  A convenient way to collect the tower of
leading-twist matrix elements is by light-ray operators.

Let \(n^\mu\) be a future-directed lightlike vector, \(n^2=0\), and choose the
normalization \(P\cdot n>0\) for the target momentum.  For a representation
\(R\) of the gauge group, define the straight Wilson transporter
\[
  W_R(\lambda n,0)
  =
  \mathcal P
  \exp\left\{\ii\int_0^\lambda
  n^\mu A_\mu^a(sn)t_R^a\,\dd s\right\}.
\]
Here \(A_\mu=A_\mu^at^a\) is the same connection coordinate used throughout the
chapter, with \(D_\mu=\partial_\mu-\ii A_\mu\) and
\(-\frac1{4g^2}\operatorname{tr}F_{\mu\nu}F^{\mu\nu}\).  The symbol
\(\mathcal P\) orders factors with larger parameter \(s\) to the left.

\begin{proposition}[Gauge covariance of the open light-ray operator]
\label{prop:qcd-light-ray-gauge-covariance}
Let \(U(x)\) be a smooth gauge transformation in the fundamental
representation, and let \(U_R(x)\) be its image in a representation \(R\).
With the transformation law
\[
  A_\mu\longmapsto U A_\mu U^{-1}-\ii(\partial_\mu U)U^{-1},
  \qquad
  q(x)\longmapsto U(x)q(x),
\]
the transporter satisfies
\[
  W_R(\lambda n,0)
  \longmapsto
  U_R(\lambda n)W_R(\lambda n,0)U_R(0)^{-1}.
\]
Consequently
\[
  \bar q(\lambda n)W_{\square}(\lambda n,0)\gamma\cdot n\,q(0)
\]
is a color-singlet bilocal operator before renormalization, and its
renormalized descendants remain gauge invariant if the regularization and
subtraction scheme preserve background gauge covariance.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Let \(W_R(s,0)\) denote the partial transporter from \(0\) to \(sn\).  It is the
solution of
\[
  \frac{\dd}{\dd s}W_R(s,0)
  =
  \ii n^\mu A_\mu^a(sn)t_R^a W_R(s,0),
  \qquad
  W_R(0,0)=\mathbf 1 .
\]
After the gauge transformation, the product
\(U_R(sn)W_R(s,0)U_R(0)^{-1}\) obeys the same differential equation with the
transformed connection and has the same initial value at \(s=0\).  Uniqueness of
solutions to this finite-dimensional linear ordinary differential equation
gives the stated transformation law.  The endpoint factors cancel against the
transformations of \(\bar q(\lambda n)\) and \(q(0)\), because the gamma matrix
acts on spinor indices and is the identity in color space.
\end{proof}

For an unpolarized target, write
\[
  \langle \mathcal X\rangle_{P,H}
  :=
  \frac12\sum_s\bra{P,s}\mathcal X\ket{P,s},
\]
with the one-particle normalization fixed in the scattering chapters.  The
renormalized quark light-ray operator and its parton distribution are
\begin{align}
  \mathbb O_q(\lambda n;\mu)
  &:=
  \left[
    \bar q(\lambda n)W_{\square}(\lambda n,0)\gamma\cdot n\,q(0)
  \right]_{\mu},
  \label{eq:qcd-quark-light-ray-operator}\\
  f_{q/H}(x,\mu)
  &:=
  \frac1{2P\cdot n}
  \int\frac{\dd\lambda}{2\pi}\,
  \ee^{-\ii x\lambda P\cdot n}
  \langle\mathbb O_q(\lambda n;\mu)\rangle_{P,H}.
  \label{eq:pdf-light-ray-definition}
\end{align}
The factor \(2P\cdot n\) fixes the convention so that a free quark target has
\(f_{q/q}(x)=\delta(1-x)\).  The antiquark distribution is defined by the
charge-conjugate bilocal with the fields interchanged and the transporter
running between the same endpoints.  The gluon distribution is defined from
the adjoint light-ray operator
\begin{align}
  \mathbb O_g(\lambda n;\mu)
  &:=
  \left[
    F^a_{n\rho}(\lambda n)
    W_{\rm ad}^{ab}(\lambda n,0)
    F_n^{b\rho}(0)
  \right]_{\mu},
  \qquad
  F_{n\rho}:=n^\mu F_{\mu\rho},
  \label{eq:qcd-gluon-light-ray-operator}\\
  f_{g/H}(x,\mu)
  &:=
  \frac1{2x(P\cdot n)^2}
  \int\frac{\dd\lambda}{2\pi}\,
  \ee^{-\ii x\lambda P\cdot n}
  \langle\mathbb O_g(\lambda n;\mu)\rangle_{P,H},
  \qquad 0<x<1 .
  \label{eq:qcd-gluon-pdf-definition}
\end{align}
The factor \(1/x\) is part of the conventional normalization of the gluon
light-ray distribution; it is what makes the \(N\)-th Mellin moment correspond
to the spin-\(N\) local gluon operator below.  Possible singular behavior at
\(x=0\) belongs to the small-\(x\) problem and is not hidden inside the
definition.

The preceding equations are nonperturbative operator definitions once the
underlying quantum field theory supplies the renormalized light-ray operators
\(\mathbb O_a(\lambda n;\mu)\) as operator-valued distributions, or at least as
matrix-element distributions between the hadron states under consideration.
They are not definitions in terms of on-shell quarks or gluons, and they do not
presuppose a colored particle interpretation.  In four-dimensional continuum
QCD this existence statement is tied to the still-open problem of constructing
the theory and to the additional ultraviolet problem of renormalizing lightlike
Wilson-line composites.  A gauge-invariant regulator can define finite
approximants, but the continuum lightcone limit, the operator-renormalization
limit, and the factorization theorem are separate assertions.  Equal-time
Euclidean bilocals used in lattice quasi-PDF or pseudo-PDF methods are therefore
matching observables for the light-ray definition, not the definition itself.

The subscript \(\mu\) in
\eqref{eq:qcd-quark-light-ray-operator}--\eqref{eq:qcd-gluon-pdf-definition}
means that the singular lightlike bilocal has been defined in a specified
regularization and factorization scheme.  For integrated collinear PDFs, the
renormalization is a convolution in the light-cone momentum fraction:
\begin{equation}
  \mathbb O^{\rm bare}_{a}(x)
  =
  \sum_b
  \int_x^1\frac{\dd z}{z}\,
  Z_{ab}\!\left(\frac{x}{z},\mu,\Lambda_{\rm UV}\right)
  \mathbb O_b(z;\mu),
  \label{eq:qcd-light-ray-renormalization-convolution}
\end{equation}
where \(a,b\) range over quarks, antiquarks, and gluons.  This equation is a
definition of the renormalized light-ray coordinates; the anomalous-dimension
kernel obtained from \(Z\) is the splitting kernel in DGLAP evolution.  For
TMDs or other observables with unresolved transverse momentum, an additional
rapidity renormalization is required; it is not part of the integrated PDF
definition used in inclusive DIS.

Figure~\ref{fig:qcd-dis-ope-light-ray-factorization} records the operator
factorization used for inclusive DIS: the short-distance current product is
matched to renormalized light-ray operators whose convolutional
renormalization gives DGLAP evolution.

\begin{figure}[H]
  \centering
  \resizebox{0.96\textwidth}{!}{%
  \begin{tikzpicture}[x=1cm,y=1cm,every node/.style={font=\scriptsize}]
    \begin{scope}
      \node[font=\small] at (0,2.35) {current product};
      \fill[blue!70!black] (-1.05,0.55) circle (2.4pt);
      \fill[blue!70!black] (1.05,0.55) circle (2.4pt);
      \draw[blue!70!black,thick] (-1.05,0.55)--(1.05,0.55);
      \node[above] at (-1.05,0.65) {\(J^\mu(x)\)};
      \node[above] at (1.05,0.65) {\(J^\nu(0)\)};
      \draw[<->,orange!85!black,thick] (-1.05,0.16)--(1.05,0.16);
      \node[orange!85!black,below] at (0,0.16) {\(|x|\sim Q^{-1}\)};
      \node[align=center] at (0,-0.8)
        {short-distance coefficients\\\(C_a^{\mu\nu}(x,\mu)\)};
    \end{scope}

    \draw[-{Latex[length=2mm]},thick] (2.25,0.45)--(3.75,0.45);
    \node[align=center] at (3.0,0.88) {OPE};

    \begin{scope}[shift={(5.35,0)}]
      \node[font=\small] at (0,2.35) {local tower};
      \draw[thick] (-1.4,0.85)--(1.4,0.85);
      \foreach \x in {-1.05,-0.55,-0.05,0.45,0.95} {
        \draw[blue!65!black,thick,-{Latex[length=1.6mm]}] (\x,0.15)--(\x,0.78);
      }
      \node[align=center] at (0,-0.68)
        {\(\bar q\,\gamma^{(\mu_1}\ii D^{\mu_2}\cdots \ii D^{\mu_N)}q\),\\
        \(F^{(\mu_1}{}_{\rho}\ii D^{\mu_2}\cdots F^{\mu_N)\rho}\)};
    \end{scope}

    \draw[-{Latex[length=2mm]},thick] (7.85,0.45)--(9.25,0.45);
    \node[align=center] at (8.55,0.88) {resum\\on light ray};

    \begin{scope}[shift={(11.0,0)}]
      \node[font=\small] at (0,2.35) {renormalized light-ray operator};
      \draw[purple!70!black,thick,decorate,
        decoration={snake,amplitude=0.85pt,segment length=7pt}]
        (-1.75,0.52)--(1.75,0.52);
      \fill[blue!70!black] (-1.75,0.52) circle (2.3pt);
      \fill[red!70!black] (1.75,0.52) circle (2.3pt);
      \node[below] at (-1.75,0.35) {\(\bar q(\lambda n)\)};
      \node[below] at (1.75,0.35) {\(q(0)\)};
      \node[purple!70!black,above] at (0,0.78) {\(W_{\square}(\lambda n,0)\)};
      \node[align=center] at (0,-0.72)
        {matrix element in \(\ket P\)\\defines \(f_{a/H}(x,\mu)\)};
    \end{scope}
  \end{tikzpicture}
  }
  \caption{The short-distance current product is first expanded into local
  renormalized operators.  The leading-twist tower can then be packaged into
  gauge-invariant light-ray operators whose hadron matrix elements define
  parton distributions.}
  \label{fig:qcd-dis-ope-light-ray-factorization}
\end{figure}

The factorization assertion has two logically separate parts.  The first is
the exact definition of the hadronic tensor as the current-current Wightman
matrix element \eqref{eq:hadronic-tensor-current-product}.  The second is the
leading-power short-distance statement that, after the current OPE and
light-ray renormalization have been performed, the same observable can be
coordinatized by universal hadronic light-ray matrix elements and perturbative
coefficient functions.

\begin{hypothesis}[Leading-twist DIS factorization datum]
\label{hyp:qcd-dis-leading-twist-factorization}
Fix a factorization scheme and a compact interval
\(K\Subset(0,1)\) of Bjorken \(x\).  A leading-twist factorization datum for an
inclusive structure function \(F_i\) consists of coefficient distributions
\(C_{i,a}\), renormalized integrated PDFs \(f_{a/H}\), and constants
\(C_{K,\varphi}\), \(\Lambda_{\rm HT}\), and \(p>0\), such that for every test
function \(\varphi\in C_c^\infty(K)\) the difference between the exact
structure function and the factorized expression obeys
\[
  \left|
  \left\langle
  F_i-\sum_a C_{i,a}\otimes f_{a/H},\varphi
  \right\rangle
  \right|
  \le
  C_{K,\varphi}
  \left(\frac{\Lambda_{\rm HT}}{Q}\right)^p
\]
for all sufficiently large \(Q\).  The convolution is the one displayed in
\eqref{eq:dis-factorization}.  The compact-\(x\) restriction excludes the
separate threshold \(x\to1\) and small-\(x\) limits, whose large logarithms
require additional factorization data.
\end{hypothesis}

Under this hypothesis, factorization expresses a structure function \(F_i\) in
the form
\begin{equation}
  F_i(x_B,Q)
  =
  \sum_{a}
  \int_{x_B}^{1}\frac{\dd z}{z}\,
  C_{i,a}\!\left(\frac{x_B}{z},\frac{Q}{\mu},g(\mu)\right)
  f_{a/H}(z,\mu)
  +
  R_i(x_B,Q),
  \label{eq:dis-factorization}
\end{equation}
where \(a\) runs over quark, antiquark, and gluon parton species, and the
remainder \(R_i\) satisfies the distributional power bound in
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:qcd-dis-leading-twist-factorization}.  The coefficients
\(C_{i,a}\) are short-distance kernels; the distributions \(f_{a/H}\) are
universal hadronic matrix elements for the chosen factorization scheme.  This
paragraph is not a statement about colored asymptotic particles.  The
``parton'' label \(a\) is a label in the light-ray operator basis and in the
coefficient algebra.

The role of the parton distributions in
\eqref{eq:dis-factorization} is also the point at which the nonabelian theory
departs from the abelian Bloch--Nordsieck construction of
Remark~\ref{rem:abelian-scope-bloch-nordsieck}.  A quark or gluon entering a
short-distance hard subprocess is a colored partonic variable, not a physical
asymptotic state.  Its collinear gluon cloud is tied to a color generator and
to the Wilson line in \eqref{eq:pdf-light-ray-definition}.  Summing over
unresolved final-state gluons gives the final-state part of an
infrared-collinear safe observable, but the singularities associated with a
massless incoming colored parton are absorbed into the renormalized light-ray
operator defining \(f_{a/H}\).  Equivalently, the collinear subtraction that
renormalizes the PDF is part of the definition of the factorized hadronic
observable.  The residual \(\mu\)-dependence of this subtraction is the
DGLAP evolution below.

The independence of \(F_i\) from the auxiliary scale \(\mu\) gives the
evolution equation
\begin{equation}
  \mu\frac{\dd}{\dd\mu} f_{a/H}(x,\mu)
  =
  \sum_b\int_x^1\frac{\dd z}{z}\,
  P_{ab}\!\left(\frac{x}{z},g(\mu)\right)f_{b/H}(z,\mu),
  \label{eq:dglap-evolution}
\end{equation}
where \(P_{ab}\) are splitting kernels, equivalently anomalous dimensions of
the light-ray operators.  This is the precise sense in which short-distance
quark and gluon variables control high-energy hadronic observables while
physical asymptotic states remain color singlets.
More explicitly, differentiating
\eqref{eq:qcd-light-ray-renormalization-convolution} at fixed bare operator
gives a convolution anomalous dimension.  With the sign convention used in
\eqref{eq:dglap-evolution}, that anomalous dimension is denoted \(P_{ab}\).
The coefficient functions obey the dual equation, so the \(\mu\)-dependence of
the convolution in \eqref{eq:dis-factorization} cancels.
At leading order, in the same convention as \eqref{eq:dglap-evolution},
\[
  P_{ab}(x,g)
  =
  \frac{g^2}{8\pi^2}P_{ab}^{(0)}(x)+O(g^4).
\]
For unpolarized distributions in the \(\overline{\mathrm{MS}}\) scheme,
\[
  C_F=\frac{N_c^2-1}{N_c},
  \qquad
  C_A=2N_c,
  \qquad
  T_R=1,
\]
in the trace normalization of \eqref{eq:qcd-casimir-definitions}.  These are
twice the standard half-trace numbers, while the overall perturbative
coefficient in \eqref{eq:dglap-evolution} is written in the corresponding
coupling coordinate.  Let
\begin{equation}
  D_0(x):=\left(\frac1{1-x}\right)_+
  \label{eq:qcd-d0-plus-distribution}
\end{equation}
be the plus distribution defined by
\[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,D_0(x)\,\varphi(x)
  =
  \int_0^1\dd x\,\frac{\varphi(x)-\varphi(1)}{1-x}
\]
for every smooth test function \(\varphi\).  Products such as \(xD_0(x)\) are
defined by multiplication of this distribution by the smooth function \(x\).
With this unambiguous convention, the nonzero leading kernels are
\begin{align}
  P_{q_iq_j}^{(0)}(x)
  &=
  \delta_{ij}\,
  C_F\left[
    2D_0(x)-1-x
    +\frac32\delta(1-x)
  \right],
  \notag\\
  P_{\bar q_i\bar q_j}^{(0)}(x)
  &=
  P_{q_iq_j}^{(0)}(x),
  \notag\\
  P_{q_i g}^{(0)}(x)
  &=
  P_{\bar q_i g}^{(0)}(x)
  =
  T_R\bigl[x^2+(1-x)^2\bigr],
  \notag\\
  P_{gq_i}^{(0)}(x)
  &=
  P_{g\bar q_i}^{(0)}(x)
  =
  C_F\,\frac{1+(1-x)^2}{x},
  \notag\\
  P_{gg}^{(0)}(x)
  &=
  2C_A\left[
    xD_0(x)
    +\frac{1-x}{x}
    +x(1-x)
  \right]
  +
  \frac{11C_A-4T_RN_f}{6}\delta(1-x).
  \label{eq:lo-dglap-splitting-kernels}
\end{align}
This notation avoids the common ambiguity between plus-prescribing the whole
rational function and plus-prescribing only the pole at \(x=1\).  For example,
\(2D_0-1-x\) is the distribution often abbreviated as
\((1+x^2)/(1-x)_+\) in particle-physics notation.  Equivalently, for the flavor
singlet quark distribution
\(\Sigma=\sum_{i=1}^{N_f}(q_i+\bar q_i)\),
\[
  \mu\frac{\dd}{\dd\mu}
  \begin{pmatrix}\Sigma\\ f_g\end{pmatrix}
  =
  \frac{g^2}{8\pi^2}
  \begin{pmatrix}
    P_{qq}^{(0)} & 2N_fP_{qg}^{(0)}\\
    P_{gq}^{(0)} & P_{gg}^{(0)}
  \end{pmatrix}
  \otimes
  \begin{pmatrix}\Sigma\\ f_g\end{pmatrix}
  +O(g^4),
\]
where \(\otimes\) denotes the convolution appearing in
\eqref{eq:dglap-evolution}.  Nonsinglet quark combinations evolve with the
same \(P_{qq}^{(0)}\) and do not mix with the gluon at this order.

\begin{proposition}[Number and momentum sum rules at one loop]
\label{prop:qcd-lo-dglap-sum-rules}
The kernels in \eqref{eq:lo-dglap-splitting-kernels} satisfy
\[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,P_{qq}^{(0)}(x)=0,
\]
and the two momentum-column identities
\[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,x
  \bigl(P_{qq}^{(0)}(x)+P_{gq}^{(0)}(x)\bigr)=0,
  \qquad
  \int_0^1\dd x\,x
  \bigl(2N_fP_{qg}^{(0)}(x)+P_{gg}^{(0)}(x)\bigr)=0 .
\]
Thus nonsinglet quark number and the total light-cone momentum fraction are
preserved by the leading-order evolution.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For \(m\ge0\),
\[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,x^mD_0(x)
  =
  \int_0^1\dd x\,\frac{x^m-1}{1-x}
  =
  -H_m,
  \qquad
  H_m:=\sum_{r=1}^m\frac1r ,
\]
with \(H_0=0\).  The number sum rule is
\[
  C_F\left(2H_0-\int_0^1(1+x)\,\dd x+\frac32\right)=0.
\]
For a quark parent,
\[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,xP_{qq}^{(0)}(x)
  =
  C_F\left(-2-\frac12-\frac13+\frac32\right)
  =
  -\frac43C_F,
\]
while
\[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,xP_{gq}^{(0)}(x)
  =
  C_F\int_0^1\dd x\,\bigl[1+(1-x)^2\bigr]
  =
  \frac43C_F .
\]
For a gluon parent,
\[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,xP_{qg}^{(0)}(x)
  =
  T_R\int_0^1\dd x\,x\bigl[x^2+(1-x)^2\bigr]
  =
  \frac13T_R ,
\]
and
\[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,xP_{gg}^{(0)}(x)
  =
  2C_A\left(-H_2+\frac12+\frac1{12}\right)
  +\frac{11C_A-4T_RN_f}{6}
  =
  -\frac23T_RN_f .
\]
The two column sums therefore vanish.
\end{proof}

\section{Transverse-Momentum Dependent Distributions and Rapidity Renormalization}
\label{sec:qcd-tmd-rapidity-renormalization}

Integrated PDFs are obtained after summing over all transverse momentum in the
collinear sector.  Observables differential in a transverse momentum, for
example color-singlet production with \(q_\perp^2\ll Q^2\), require a different
operator coordinate.  The relevant nonperturbative input is not the integrated
light-ray operator \eqref{eq:qcd-quark-light-ray-operator}; it is a
transverse-separated light-ray matrix element with Wilson lines whose geometry
creates rapidity divergences.  Rapidity subtraction is therefore part of the
definition, in the same sense that ultraviolet subtraction is part of the
definition of a renormalized local operator.

Let \(n,\bar n\) be future-directed lightlike vectors with
\(n\cdot\bar n=2\), and let \(b_\perp\) be transverse:
\[
  b_\perp\cdot n=b_\perp\cdot\bar n=0 .
\]
For a real parameter \(\lambda\), set
\[
  z^\mu=\lambda n^\mu+b_\perp^\mu .
\]
A finite rapidity regulator may be implemented by replacing lightlike Wilson
lines by Wilson lines along non-lightlike directions \(v,\bar v\), by an
analytic rapidity regulator, by a delta regulator, or by an equivalent
gauge-covariant subtraction.  The monograph denotes the regulator data
collectively by \(\rho\).  At finite \(\rho\) and finite ultraviolet cutoff
\(\Lambda\), let
\(\mathcal U^{[\eta]}_{v}(z,0;\rho,\Lambda)\) be a staple transporter from
\(0\) to \(z\), with longitudinal direction \(v\), transverse bridge
\(b_\perp\), and orientation \(\eta=+1\) for future-pointing and
\(\eta=-1\) for past-pointing staples.

\begin{definition}[TMD operator datum]
\label{def:qcd-tmd-operator-datum}
A quark TMD datum for a hadron \(H\) with momentum \(P\) consists of:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the vectors \(n,\bar n\), a transverse separation \(b_\perp\), and an
  orientation \(\eta\) of the staple Wilson line;
  \item a finite rapidity regulator \(\rho\) and ultraviolet regulator
  \(\Lambda\), both chosen in a gauge-covariant way;
  \item the unsubtracted beam matrix element
  \[
    B^{\rm unsub}_{q/H}(x,b_\perp;\rho,\Lambda,\eta)
    =
    \frac1{2P\cdot n}
    \int\frac{\dd\lambda}{2\pi}\,
    \ee^{-\ii x\lambda P\cdot n}
    \Bigl\langle
    \bar q(z)\,
    \mathcal U^{[\eta]}_{v}(z,0;\rho,\Lambda)\,
    \gamma\cdot n\,q(0)
    \Bigr\rangle_{P,H};
  \]
  \item the vacuum soft factor
  \(S(b_\perp;\rho,\Lambda,\eta)\), defined by the trace of the closed Wilson
  geometry obtained by multiplying the corresponding \(v\)- and
  \(\bar v\)-staples in the vacuum;
  \item a finite-part prescription, denoted
  \(\operatorname{FP}_{\rho,\Lambda}\), which removes ultraviolet and rapidity
  regulator dependence and introduces the scales \(\mu\) and \(\zeta\).
\end{enumerate}
The renormalized TMD in this scheme is
\begin{equation}
  F_{q/H}^{[\eta]}(x,b_\perp;\mu,\zeta)
  =
  \operatorname{FP}_{\rho,\Lambda}
  \left[
    Z_q(\mu,\zeta;\rho,\Lambda)\,
    \frac{
      B^{\rm unsub}_{q/H}(x,b_\perp;\rho,\Lambda,\eta)
    }{
      S(b_\perp;\rho,\Lambda,\eta)^{1/2}
    }
  \right].
  \label{eq:qcd-renormalized-tmd-definition}
\end{equation}
The square root is a convention for assigning half of the soft subtraction to
each collinear sector.  A different finite assignment is a different TMD
scheme, related by a finite multiplicative transformation.  The variables
\(\mu\) and \(\zeta\) record, respectively, ultraviolet and rapidity
renormalization.  The orientation \(\eta\) is part of the operator definition;
time-reversal odd TMDs may change sign between future- and past-pointing
staples, as in semi-inclusive DIS versus Drell--Yan kinematics.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Gauge invariance of the subtracted TMD datum]
\label{prop:qcd-tmd-gauge-invariance}
At finite regulator, the numerator and soft factor in
\eqref{eq:qcd-renormalized-tmd-definition} are gauge invariant after taking
the color trace and endpoint fields into account.  Hence a background
gauge-covariant finite-part prescription produces a gauge-invariant
renormalized TMD matrix element.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Every Wilson segment transforms by multiplication with the gauge
transformation at its endpoints, as in
Proposition~\ref{prop:qcd-light-ray-gauge-covariance}.  Along a staple, the
factors at internal junctions cancel between adjacent segments.  The remaining
endpoint factors at \(0\) and \(z\) cancel the gauge transformations of
\(q(0)\) and \(\bar q(z)\).  In the soft factor all Wilson lines are multiplied
inside a trace, so the residual base-point factor is removed by cyclicity of
the trace.  The finite-part map changes only regulator and scale coordinates;
if it is background gauge covariant, it cannot introduce an uncanceled color
index.
\end{proof}

Rapidity evolution is the statement that changing the auxiliary rapidity
scale changes the coordinate description of the same physical transverse
momentum distribution.  It is most transparent in impact-parameter space,
where convolutions in transverse momentum become products.  Put
\[
  \ell_\mu:=\log\mu,
  \qquad
  \ell_\zeta:=\log\sqrt{\zeta}.
\]
For a fixed \(x\)-test function and fixed \(b_\perp\), suppose the paired TMD
