matrix element is nonzero and obeys
\begin{align}
  \frac{\partial}{\partial\ell_\zeta}
  \log F_{q/H}^{[\eta]}(x,b_\perp;\mu,\zeta)
  &=
  \mathcal D_q(b_\perp;\mu),
  \label{eq:qcd-collins-soper-equation}\\
  \frac{\partial}{\partial\ell_\mu}
  \log F_{q/H}^{[\eta]}(x,b_\perp;\mu,\zeta)
  &=
  \gamma_F^q(g(\mu),\ell_\zeta-\ell_\mu).
  \label{eq:qcd-tmd-mu-evolution}
\end{align}
The first equation defines the Collins--Soper kernel
\(\mathcal D_q\) in the chosen convention.

\begin{proposition}[Collins--Soper consistency]
\label{prop:qcd-collins-soper-consistency}
If the derivatives in
\eqref{eq:qcd-collins-soper-equation}--\eqref{eq:qcd-tmd-mu-evolution}
commute on the renormalized TMD distribution, then
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\partial}{\partial\ell_\mu}\mathcal D_q(b_\perp;\mu)
  =
  \frac{\partial}{\partial\ell_\zeta}
  \gamma_F^q(g(\mu),\ell_\zeta-\ell_\mu).
  \label{eq:qcd-collins-soper-integrability}
\end{equation}
In the convention
\[
  \gamma_F^q(g,\ell_\zeta-\ell_\mu)
  =
  \gamma_F^{q,0}(g)
  -2\Gamma_{\rm cusp}^q(g)(\ell_\zeta-\ell_\mu),
\]
this gives
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\partial}{\partial\log\mu}\mathcal D_q(b_\perp;\mu)
  =
  -2\Gamma_{\rm cusp}^q(g(\mu)).
  \label{eq:qcd-collins-soper-cusp}
\end{equation}
At small \(b_\perp\), the one-loop solution compatible with the cusp
normalization of \eqref{eq:qcd-nonsinglet-large-n} is
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal D_q(b_\perp;\mu)
  =
  -\frac{g^2(\mu)C_F}{4\pi^2}
  \log\frac{\mu^2 b_\perp^2\ee^{2\gamma_{\rm E}}}{4}
  +O(g^4),
  \label{eq:qcd-collins-soper-kernel-one-loop}
\end{equation}
up to a finite \(b_\perp\)-dependent scheme term independent of \(\mu\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Apply
\(\partial_{\ell_\mu}\partial_{\ell_\zeta}
=\partial_{\ell_\zeta}\partial_{\ell_\mu}\)
to \(\log F_{q/H}^{[\eta]}\).  The left order differentiates
\eqref{eq:qcd-collins-soper-equation}; the right order differentiates
\eqref{eq:qcd-tmd-mu-evolution}.  This proves
\eqref{eq:qcd-collins-soper-integrability}.  Substituting the displayed form
of \(\gamma_F^q\) gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-collins-soper-cusp}.  Finally,
\(\partial_{\log\mu}\log(\mu^2b_\perp^2\ee^{2\gamma_{\rm E}}/4)=2\), so the
derivative of \eqref{eq:qcd-collins-soper-kernel-one-loop} is
\(-g^2C_F/(2\pi^2)+O(g^4)\), equal to
\(-2\Gamma_{\rm cusp}^q(g)+O(g^4)\) with
\(\Gamma_{\rm cusp}^q(g)=g^2C_F/(4\pi^2)+O(g^4)\) in the trace-delta
normalization.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Finite TMD scheme changes]
\label{prop:qcd-tmd-finite-scheme-change}
Let \(R(b_\perp;\mu,\zeta)\) be a finite scalar function and set
\(F'=\ee^R F\).  Then
\[
  \mathcal D'=\mathcal D+\frac{\partial R}{\partial\ell_\zeta},
  \qquad
  \gamma_F'=\gamma_F+\frac{\partial R}{\partial\ell_\mu}.
\]
The consistency relation
\eqref{eq:qcd-collins-soper-integrability} is preserved.  Therefore the
separation of a rapidity-sensitive cross section into hard, TMD, and soft
coordinates is scheme dependent, whereas the final cross section is not.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Take logarithms of \(F'=\ee^R F\) and differentiate with respect to
\(\ell_\zeta\) and \(\ell_\mu\).  The displayed transformations follow.  Taking
\(\partial_{\ell_\mu}\) of the first transformation and
\(\partial_{\ell_\zeta}\) of the second gives the same extra term
\(\partial_{\ell_\mu}\partial_{\ell_\zeta}R\).  Hence the difference between
the two sides of
\eqref{eq:qcd-collins-soper-integrability} is unchanged.
\end{proof}

\begin{hypothesis}[Small-\(q_\perp\) color-singlet TMD factorization datum]
\label{hyp:qcd-tmd-factorization-datum}
For a color-singlet final state of invariant mass \(Q\) produced in
hadron--hadron scattering, a leading-power small-\(q_\perp\) TMD
factorization datum consists of TMD schemes for the two incoming hadrons, a
hard function \(H_{ij}(Q,\mu)\), rapidity scales satisfying
\(\zeta_A\zeta_B=Q^4\), a \(Y\)-term that matches the region
\(|q_\perp|\sim Q\), a statement about Glauber exchange, and a distributional
remainder estimate.  In the region
\(\Lambda_{\rm QCD}\lesssim |q_\perp|\ll Q\) the singular part has the
impact-parameter form
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\dd\sigma_{\rm sing}}{\dd Q^2\dd^2q_\perp}
  =
  \sum_{i,j}
  H_{ij}(Q,\mu)
  \int\frac{\dd^2 b_\perp}{(2\pi)^2}\,
  \ee^{\ii b_\perp\cdot q_\perp}
  F_{i/A}(x_A,b_\perp;\mu,\zeta_A)
  F_{j/B}(x_B,b_\perp;\mu,\zeta_B).
  \label{eq:qcd-tmd-factorization}
\end{equation}
The formula is a theorem only when the regulator construction, cancellation or
operator representation of Glauber exchange, and the topology of the
power-remainder estimate have all been supplied.
\end{hypothesis}

\section{Drell--Yan Factorization and Glauber Status}
\label{sec:qcd-drell-yan-glauber-status}

Drell--Yan production is the timelike current analogue of DIS:
\[
  h_A(P_A)+h_B(P_B)\longrightarrow \ell^+\ell^-+X,
  \qquad q=p_{\ell^+}+p_{\ell^-},
  \qquad q^2=Q^2>0 .
\]
The QCD object is again a Wightman current matrix element, now between a
two-hadron incoming state.  For unpolarized hadrons define
\begin{equation}
  W_{AB}^{\mu\nu}(P_A,P_B,q)
  =
  \frac1{N_{\rm spin}}
  \sum_{\sigma_A,\sigma_B}
  \sum_X
  (2\pi)^4\delta^{(4)}(P_A+P_B-q-P_X)
  \bra{P_A,P_B}J^\mu(0)\ket{X}
  \bra{X}J^\nu(0)\ket{P_A,P_B}.
  \label{eq:qcd-drell-yan-hadronic-tensor}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, by translation covariance and completeness,
\begin{equation}
  W_{AB}^{\mu\nu}(P_A,P_B,q)
  =
  \frac1{N_{\rm spin}}
  \sum_{\sigma_A,\sigma_B}
  \int\dd^4x\,\ee^{\ii q\cdot x}
  \bra{P_A,P_B}J^\mu(x)J^\nu(0)\ket{P_A,P_B},
  \label{eq:qcd-drell-yan-current-product}
\end{equation}
with the same state-normalization convention as in the scattering chapters.
The partonic formulae below are short-distance coordinates for this tensor;
they are not definitions of a cross section with colored asymptotic states.

\begin{proposition}[Drell--Yan leading-power kinematics]
\label{prop:qcd-drell-yan-leading-kinematics}
Let
\[
  s:=(P_A+P_B)^2,
  \qquad
  \tau:=\frac{Q^2}{s},
\]
and choose the hadron center-of-mass frame with the \(A\)-hadron moving in the
positive longitudinal direction.  At leading power in hadron masses and
transverse momentum, the longitudinal momentum fractions entering the
short-distance hard collision are
\begin{equation}
  x_A=\sqrt{\tau}\,\ee^y,
  \qquad
  x_B=\sqrt{\tau}\,\ee^{-y},
  \label{eq:qcd-drell-yan-xa-xb}
\end{equation}
where
\[
  y:=\frac12\log\frac{q^0+q^3}{q^0-q^3}
\]
is the lepton-pair rapidity.  Hence
\[
  x_Ax_B=\tau,
  \qquad
  y=\frac12\log\frac{x_A}{x_B}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
In light-cone coordinates adapted to the beam directions, write the leading
hadron momenta as
\[
  P_A^+=\sqrt{s},\quad P_A^-=0,
  \qquad
  P_B^-= \sqrt{s},\quad P_B^+=0,
\]
and neglect transverse components in the leading-power kinematic identity.
The active partons carry
\[
  q^+=x_AP_A^+,\qquad q^-=x_BP_B^-.
\]
Therefore \(Q^2=q^+q^-+O(q_\perp^2,M_{A,B}^2)=x_Ax_Bs+O(q_\perp^2,M_{A,B}^2)\),
which gives \(x_Ax_B=\tau\) at leading power.  The rapidity satisfies
\[
  y=\frac12\log\frac{q^+}{q^-}
  =
  \frac12\log\frac{x_A}{x_B}.
\]
Solving the two equations gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-drell-yan-xa-xb}.
\end{proof}

\begin{hypothesis}[Drell--Yan small-\(q_\perp\) TMD datum]
\label{hyp:qcd-drell-yan-tmd-datum}
A leading-power Drell--Yan TMD factorization datum consists of:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item the renormalized current hard function \(H_{ij}(Q,\mu)\);
  \item past-pointing TMD operator data
  \(F_{i/A}^{[-]}(x_A,b_\perp;\mu,\zeta_A)\) and
  \(F_{j/B}^{[-]}(x_B,b_\perp;\mu,\zeta_B)\), in the notation of
  Definition~\ref{def:qcd-tmd-operator-datum};
  \item rapidity scales constrained by \(\zeta_A\zeta_B=Q^4\);
  \item a \(Y\)-term matching to the region \(|q_\perp|\sim Q\);
  \item a proof or controlled hypothesis for Glauber exchange;
  \item a distributional power-remainder estimate in \(q_\perp/Q\) and in the
  hadron-mass corrections.
\end{enumerate}
The singular small-\(q_\perp\) term is then represented as
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\dd\sigma_{\rm sing}}{\dd Q^2\dd y\,\dd^2q_\perp}
  =
  \sum_{i,j}
  H_{ij}(Q,\mu)
  \int\frac{\dd^2b_\perp}{(2\pi)^2}\,
  \ee^{\ii b_\perp\cdot q_\perp}
  F_{i/A}^{[-]}(x_A,b_\perp;\mu,\zeta_A)
  F_{j/B}^{[-]}(x_B,b_\perp;\mu,\zeta_B),
  \label{eq:qcd-drell-yan-tmd-factorization}
\end{equation}
plus the stated \(Y\)-term and power remainder.  The past-pointing staple
orientation is part of the operator definition.  It is the operator-level
source of the sign reversal of time-reversal-odd TMD coordinates between
semi-inclusive DIS and Drell--Yan, once the relevant antiunitary
transformation and spin conventions are specified.
\end{hypothesis}

\begin{proposition}[Finite unitarity model for Glauber cancellation]
\label{prop:qcd-finite-glauber-cancellation-model}
Let \(\mathcal H_{\rm obs}\) be a finite-dimensional observed Hilbert space,
let \(\mathcal H_{\rm un}\) be an unobserved Hilbert space, let
\(\rho\) be a trace-class density matrix on
\(\mathcal H_{\rm obs}\otimes\mathcal H_{\rm un}\), and let \(M\) be an
observable acting only on \(\mathcal H_{\rm obs}\).  If the effect of a
Glauber exchange on the unobserved degrees of freedom is represented by a
unitary \(U_G\) acting only on \(\mathcal H_{\rm un}\), then
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname{Tr}_{\rm obs,un}
  \left[
    (M\otimes\mathbf1)
    (\mathbf1\otimes U_G)\rho(\mathbf1\otimes U_G^\dagger)
  \right]
  =
  \operatorname{Tr}_{\rm obs,un}
  \left[
    (M\otimes\mathbf1)\rho
  \right].
  \label{eq:qcd-finite-glauber-unitarity-identity}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Use cyclicity of the full trace and
\((\mathbf1\otimes U_G^\dagger)(M\otimes\mathbf1)(\mathbf1\otimes U_G)
=M\otimes\mathbf1\).  The result is
\[
  \operatorname{Tr}
  \left[
    \rho
    (\mathbf1\otimes U_G^\dagger)(M\otimes\mathbf1)(\mathbf1\otimes U_G)
  \right]
  =
  \operatorname{Tr}\left[\rho(M\otimes\mathbf1)\right],
\]
which is
\eqref{eq:qcd-finite-glauber-unitarity-identity}.
\end{proof}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[What the Glauber lemma proves]
\label{ca:qcd-glauber-cancellation-status}
Proposition~\ref{prop:qcd-finite-glauber-cancellation-model} is the algebraic
unitarity identity that a Drell--Yan factorization proof must realize after
the leading regions, color flow, rapidity regulator, and measurement topology
have been fixed.  It does not prove by itself that QCD Glauber exchanges act
only on an unobserved tensor factor, nor that the contour deformations needed
to isolate the leading regions are valid.  Those statements are part of the
Glauber item in Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:qcd-drell-yan-tmd-datum}.  If the
observable measures hadronic radiation in a way that resolves the spectator
sector, or if a color exchange remains entangled with the measured hard
sector, the finite identity above no longer supplies the required
cancellation.
\end{controlledapproximation}

\section{Off-Forward Light-Ray Matrix Elements and GPDs}
\label{sec:qcd-gpd-light-ray-matrix-elements}

Generalized parton distributions are light-ray matrix elements between
different hadron momenta.  They do not require a rapidity subtraction in the
same way as TMDs, because the operator remains integrated over transverse
momentum.  Their new datum is off-forwardness.

Let \(p'\) and \(p\) be on-shell spin-\(\frac12\) hadron momenta, and define
\[
  P=\frac{p'+p}{2},
  \qquad
  \Delta=p'-p,
  \qquad
  t=\Delta^2,
  \qquad
  \xi=-\frac{\Delta\cdot n}{2P\cdot n}.
\]
For the symmetric light-ray separation
\[
  z^\mu=\lambda n^\mu ,
\]
define the quark vector GPDs \(H^q\) and \(E^q\) by
\begin{align}
  &\int\frac{\dd\lambda}{2\pi}\,
  \ee^{-\ii x\lambda P\cdot n}
  \bra{p',s'}
  \left[
  \bar q\!\left(\frac{\lambda n}{2}\right)
  W_{\square}\!\left(\frac{\lambda n}{2},-\frac{\lambda n}{2}\right)
  \gamma\cdot n\,
  q\!\left(-\frac{\lambda n}{2}\right)
  \right]_{\mu}
  \ket{p,s}
  \notag\\
  &\qquad =
  \bar u_{s'}(p')
  \left[
    \gamma\cdot n\,H^q(x,\xi,t;\mu)
    +\frac{\ii\sigma^{n\alpha}\Delta_\alpha}{2M}\,
    E^q(x,\xi,t;\mu)
  \right]
  u_s(p),
  \label{eq:qcd-gpd-definition}
\end{align}
where \(\sigma^{n\alpha}:=n_\mu\sigma^{\mu\alpha}\), and \(M\) is the hadron
mass.  The support and endpoint behavior of the distributions are properties
of the renormalized light-ray matrix elements and of the chosen hadronic
state; they are not imposed by a parton model.

\begin{proposition}[Polynomiality of GPD moments]
\label{prop:qcd-gpd-polynomiality}
Assume the renormalized twist-two local operators obtained from the light-ray
operator in \eqref{eq:qcd-gpd-definition} exist as local operator-valued
distributions between the hadron states under consideration.  Then the
\(N\)-th Mellin moments
\[
  \int_{-1}^{1}\dd x\,x^{N-1}H^q(x,\xi,t;\mu),
  \qquad
  \int_{-1}^{1}\dd x\,x^{N-1}E^q(x,\xi,t;\mu)
\]
are polynomials in \(\xi\) of degree at most \(N\), with coefficients that are
Lorentz-scalar form factors depending on \(t\) and \(\mu\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Expanding the symmetric light-ray operator in \(\lambda\) gives the local
twist-two tower
\[
  \bar q\,\gamma^{(\mu_1}
  \ii D^{\mu_2}\cdots\ii D^{\mu_N)}q-\text{traces},
\]
contracted with \(n_{\mu_1}\cdots n_{\mu_N}\).  Since \(n^2=0\), all trace
terms vanish after contraction with these \(n\)'s.  Lorentz covariance of the
off-forward matrix element gives a finite decomposition into symmetric tensors
made from \(P\), \(\Delta\), the metric, and the spinor bilinears
\(\bar u(p')\gamma^\alpha u(p)\) and
\(\bar u(p')\ii\sigma^{\alpha\beta}\Delta_\beta u(p)\).  After contraction
with \(n_{\mu_1}\cdots n_{\mu_N}\), each term contains
\[
  (P\cdot n)^{N-k}(\Delta\cdot n)^k
  =
  (P\cdot n)^N(-2\xi)^k
\]
for some \(0\le k\le N\), multiplied by a scalar form factor depending only on
\(t\) and \(\mu\).  Dividing by the overall powers of \(P\cdot n\) in the GPD
decomposition therefore gives a polynomial in \(\xi\) of degree no larger than
\(N\).  This argument uses only locality, Lorentz covariance, and the
existence of the renormalized local twist-two tower; it does not use a
probability interpretation.
\end{proof}

Deeply virtual Compton scattering and related exclusive processes use these
GPDs in coefficient-function convolutions.  As in inclusive DIS and TMD
factorization, the GPD itself is the renormalized hadronic light-ray matrix
element.  The factorization theorem connecting it to a measured exclusive
amplitude is an additional leading-power assertion with its own endpoint,
Glauber, and power-remainder data.

\section{Asymptotic Freedom and Exclusive Pion Amplitudes}
\label{sec:qcd-exclusive-pion-asymptotic-freedom}

Inclusive DIS uses forward light-ray matrix elements.  Exclusive pion
amplitudes use light-ray matrix elements between the vacuum and a one-pion
state.  This is the part of the pion \(S\)-matrix where asymptotic freedom
gives a direct large-momentum prediction: the short-distance subgraph is a
perturbatively renormalized quark-gluon amplitude, while the pion appears only
through a renormalized gauge-invariant light-ray matrix element.  The statement
is not that a pion is a weakly bound pair of on-shell quarks.  The pion datum is
the same hadronic state defined by the nonperturbative QCD sector; only the
coefficient multiplying its light-ray matrix element is perturbative.

Let \(P^\mu\) be the momentum of a charged pion and let \(n^\mu\) be a
future-directed lightlike vector with \(P\cdot n>0\).  In the isospin-symmetric
two-flavor theory, define the charged-pion light-cone distribution amplitude
by the renormalized bilocal matrix element
\begin{equation}
  \bra{\vac}
  \left[
  \bar d(\lambda n)\,
  W_{\square}(\lambda n,0)\,
  \gamma\cdot n\,\gamma_5\,u(0)
  \right]_{\mu}
  \ket{\pi^+(P)}
  =
  \ii f_\pi\,P\cdot n
  \int_0^1\dd x\,
  \ee^{-\ii x\lambda P\cdot n}\,
  \varphi_\pi(x,\mu).
  \label{eq:qcd-pion-lcda-definition}
\end{equation}
The Wilson transporter is the same path-ordered fundamental transporter used
in \eqref{eq:qcd-quark-light-ray-operator}.  The normalization of \(f_\pi\) is
the axial-current normalization of Chapter~\ref{ch:volume-ii-21},
\[
  \bra{\vac}A_a^\mu(0)\ket{\pi^b(P)}
  =
  \ii f_\pi P^\mu\delta_a{}^b .
\]
Setting \(\lambda=0\) in
\eqref{eq:qcd-pion-lcda-definition} therefore fixes
\begin{equation}
  \int_0^1\dd x\,\varphi_\pi(x,\mu)=1 .
  \label{eq:qcd-pion-lcda-normalization}
\end{equation}
The support interval \([0,1]\) is a property of the leading-twist light-ray
operator between the vacuum and the one-pion state.  It is not a probability
postulate.  The function \(\varphi_\pi\) is a renormalized distribution in
\(x\), depending on the factorization scheme and scale.

\begin{definition}[Exclusive pion factorization datum]
\label{def:qcd-exclusive-pion-factorization-datum}
An exclusive large-\(Q\) pion factorization statement consists of:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item a renormalized QCD matrix element whose external hadrons and currents
  are gauge-invariant;
  \item a light-ray operator basis, here represented at leading twist by
  \(\varphi_\pi(x,\mu)\);
  \item a hard coefficient \(T_H\), computed with external collinear partons
  and subtracted in the same scheme as the light-ray operator;
  \item a convolution prescription in the momentum fractions;
  \item a topology for the remainder, for example
  \(O(\Lambda_{\rm QCD}^2/Q^2)\) after excluding endpoint regions by the
  stated hypotheses, together with the order in \(\alpha_s\) to which
  \(T_H\) is known.
\end{enumerate}
The datum is part of the definition of the controlled approximation.  Without
it, a formula involving a pion distribution amplitude is only notation.
\end{definition}

The one-loop renormalization of the light-ray operator in
\eqref{eq:qcd-pion-lcda-definition} gives the Efremov--Radyushkin--Brodsky--
Lepage evolution equation
\begin{equation}
  \mu\frac{\dd}{\dd\mu}\varphi_\pi(x,\mu)
  =
  \frac{\alpha_s(\mu)}{2\pi}
  \int_0^1\dd y\,V(x,y)\varphi_\pi(y,\mu)
  +O(\alpha_s^2),
  \label{eq:qcd-erbl-evolution}
\end{equation}
where, in the trace-delta convention,
\begin{align}
  V(x,y)
  &=
  C_F
  \left[
  \theta(y-x)\frac{x}{y}
  \left(1+\frac1{y-x}\right)
  +
  \theta(x-y)\frac{1-x}{1-y}
  \left(1+\frac1{x-y}\right)
  \right]_+ .
  \label{eq:qcd-erbl-kernel}
\end{align}
The plus prescription acts on the \(x\)-variable:
\begin{equation}
  \int_0^1\dd x\,[K(x,y)]_+ f(x)
  :=
  \int_0^1\dd x\,K(x,y)\bigl(f(x)-f(y)\bigr),
  \label{eq:qcd-erbl-plus-prescription}
\end{equation}
for test functions smooth near \(x=y\).  Equation
\eqref{eq:qcd-erbl-plus-prescription} makes the conservation of the axial
current normalization manifest:
\[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,V(x,y)=0 .
\]

\begin{proposition}[Diagonalization of the leading ERBL kernel]
\label{prop:qcd-erbl-gegenbauer-diagonalization}
For \(n\ge0\), let \(C_n^{3/2}\) be the Gegenbauer polynomial orthogonal on
\([-1,1]\) with weight \((1-z^2)\).  The leading ERBL kernel preserves the
basis
\[
  \varphi_n(x):=6x(1-x)C_n^{3/2}(2x-1),
\]
and
\begin{equation}
  \int_0^1\dd y\,V(x,y)\varphi_n(y)
  =
  -\gamma_n^{(0)}\,\varphi_n(x),
  \label{eq:qcd-erbl-eigenvalue-equation}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
  \gamma_n^{(0)}
  =
  C_F\left[
  1-\frac{2}{(n+1)(n+2)}
  +4\sum_{k=2}^{n+1}\frac1k
  \right].
  \label{eq:qcd-erbl-anomalous-dimensions}
\end{equation}
In particular \(\gamma_0^{(0)}=0\) and
\(\gamma_n^{(0)}>0\) for every \(n\ge1\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The collinear conformal group acting on two light-ray quark fields has
\(SL(2,\mathbb R)\) quadratic Casimir diagonalized by
\(x(1-x)C_n^{3/2}(2x-1)\).  The one-loop kernel
\eqref{eq:qcd-erbl-kernel} commutes with this action after the plus
subtraction, because the singular part depends only on the projective
cross-ratio of the two light-ray insertion points and the endpoint factors are
fixed by the quark collinear spin \(j=1\).  Thus the kernel is diagonal on the
irreducible two-particle conformal-spin components.

To compute the eigenvalue, insert the polynomial test function and split the
integral into \(0<y<x\) and \(x<y<1\).  The plus prescription subtracts the
same polynomial at \(y=x\), so the integrand is locally integrable.  Expanding
\(C_n^{3/2}(2y-1)\) in powers of \(y\), each term reduces to beta-function
integrals and harmonic sums.  The coefficient of the highest-degree monomial
fixes the eigenvalue, because the kernel preserves polynomial degree.  The
result is \eqref{eq:qcd-erbl-anomalous-dimensions}.  For \(n=0\), the first
two terms cancel and the sum is empty; this is exactly the normalization
identity \eqref{eq:qcd-pion-lcda-normalization}.  For \(n\ge1\), the harmonic
sum dominates the negative rational term, so the anomalous dimension is
positive.
\end{proof}

Therefore a pion LCDA may be expanded as
\begin{equation}
  \varphi_\pi(x,\mu)
  =
  6x(1-x)
  \left[
  1+\sum_{n=1}^{\infty}a_n(\mu)C_n^{3/2}(2x-1)
  \right],
  \label{eq:qcd-pion-lcda-gegenbauer-expansion}
\end{equation}
with odd \(a_n\) vanishing in the isospin-symmetric charge-conjugation
channel.  At leading order
\begin{equation}
  \mu\frac{\dd}{\dd\mu}a_n(\mu)
  =
  -\frac{\alpha_s(\mu)}{2\pi}\gamma_n^{(0)}a_n(\mu)
  +O(\alpha_s^2),
  \label{eq:qcd-pion-gegenbauer-moment-rg}
\end{equation}
and asymptotic freedom drives all \(n\ge1\) moments to zero.  The ultraviolet
fixed shape is consequently
\begin{equation}
  \varphi_\pi^{\rm as}(x)=6x(1-x).
  \label{eq:qcd-pion-asymptotic-lcda}
\end{equation}
The approach to this shape is logarithmic and scheme dependent at finite
scale.  The statement \eqref{eq:qcd-pion-asymptotic-lcda} is therefore an
asymptotic consequence of the light-ray anomalous dimensions, not an empirical
model for the pion at moderate momentum transfer.

The spacelike charged-pion electromagnetic form factor is defined by
\begin{equation}
  \bra{\pi^+(P')}J^\mu_{\rm em}(0)\ket{\pi^+(P)}
  =
  (P+P')^\mu F_\pi(Q^2),
  \qquad
  Q^2:=-(P'-P)^2>0 .
  \label{eq:qcd-pion-em-form-factor-definition}
\end{equation}
At leading twist and leading order in the hard coefficient,
\begin{equation}
  F_\pi(Q^2)
  =
  \frac{4\pi\alpha_s(\mu)C_F}{N_c}\,
  \frac{f_\pi^2}{Q^2}
  \left[
  \int_0^1\dd x\,\frac{\varphi_\pi(x,\mu)}{x}
  \right]
  \left[
  \int_0^1\dd y\,\frac{\varphi_\pi(y,\mu)}{y}
  \right]
  +O(\alpha_s^2,Q^{-4})_{\rm fac}.
  \label{eq:qcd-pion-form-factor-factorization}
\end{equation}
The subscript ``fac'' means that the power remainder belongs to the
factorization datum of Definition~\ref{def:qcd-exclusive-pion-factorization-datum};
endpoint sensitivity can modify the practical convergence at accessible
\(Q^2\) unless controlled by an additional Sudakov or nonperturbative input.

\begin{proof}[Derivation of the leading hard coefficient]
Project each pion onto the color-singlet leading-twist collinear pair defined
by \eqref{eq:qcd-pion-lcda-definition}.  A single hard gluon must transfer
large transverse momentum between the two collinear quark lines; without this
exchange the electromagnetic current cannot convert the initial collinear
color-singlet into the final one at fixed large \(Q^2\).  The tree hard
subgraph contains one gluon propagator of virtuality \(O(Q^2)\) and one
internal quark propagator of virtuality \(O(Q^2)\).  Contracting the spin
projectors fixed by the axial matrix element gives the numerator
proportional to \(P\cdot P'\), and the color-singlet projection gives
\[
  \frac1{N_c}\,t^a_{ij}t^a_{ji}
  =
  \frac{C_F}{N_c}.
\]
The two endpoint denominators are the light-cone momentum fractions carried by
the active quarks.  With the LCDA normalization
\eqref{eq:qcd-pion-lcda-normalization}, the sum of the two photon attachments
to the charged pion gives
\eqref{eq:qcd-pion-form-factor-factorization}.  No on-shell colored external
state appears in the final formula; colored partons were only projectors used
to compute the short-distance coefficient in the chosen factorization scheme.
\end{proof}

Substituting \(\varphi_\pi^{\rm as}\) gives
\begin{equation}
  Q^2F_\pi(Q^2)
  \sim
  \frac{36\pi\alpha_s(Q)C_F}{N_c}\,f_\pi^2 .
  \label{eq:qcd-pion-form-factor-asymptotic-general}
\end{equation}
For \(N_c=3\), this is
\[
  Q^2F_\pi(Q^2)\sim 16\pi\alpha_{\rm ht}(Q) f_\pi^2
\]
in the common half-trace convention.  Equivalently, if one uses the
phenomenological convention \(f_\pi^{(130)}=\sqrt2\,f_\pi\), the same statement
is often written as \(Q^2F_\pi\sim
8\pi\alpha_{\rm ht}(f_\pi^{(130)})^2\).  The monograph keeps the
Chapter~\ref{ch:volume-ii-21} convention \(f_\pi\) fixed, so
\eqref{eq:qcd-pion-form-factor-asymptotic-general} is the convention-safe
formula.

The neutral-pion transition form factor is defined by
\begin{equation}
  \ii\int\dd^4x\,\ee^{\ii q\cdot x}
  \bra{\pi^0(P)}
  \operatorname T\,J^\mu_{\rm em}(x)J^\nu_{\rm em}(0)
  \ket{\vac}
  =
  \epsilon^{\mu\nu\rho\sigma}q_\rho k_\sigma\,
  F_{\pi^0\gamma\gamma^*}(Q^2),
  \label{eq:qcd-pion-transition-form-factor-definition}
\end{equation}
with \(k^2=0\), \(q^2=-Q^2\), and \(P=q+k\).  The low-energy endpoint is fixed
by the anomaly calculation of Chapters~\ref{ch:volume-ii-20} and
\ref{ch:volume-ii-21}:
\begin{equation}
  F_{\pi^0\gamma\gamma^*}(0)=\frac1{4\pi^2f_\pi}
  \label{eq:qcd-pion-transition-anomaly-normalization}
\end{equation}
in the present \(f_\pi\) convention.  At large spacelike \(Q^2\), leading
twist factorization gives
\begin{equation}
  F_{\pi^0\gamma\gamma^*}(Q^2)
  =
  \frac{f_\pi}{3Q^2}
  \int_0^1\dd x\,\varphi_\pi(x,\mu)
  \left(\frac1x+\frac1{1-x}\right)
  +O(\alpha_s,Q^{-4})_{\rm fac}.
  \label{eq:qcd-pion-transition-factorization}
\end{equation}
For the asymptotic LCDA,
\begin{equation}
  Q^2F_{\pi^0\gamma\gamma^*}(Q^2)\longrightarrow 2f_\pi .
  \label{eq:qcd-pion-transition-asymptotic}
\end{equation}
In the \(f_\pi^{(130)}=\sqrt2 f_\pi\) convention this is
\(\sqrt2 f_\pi^{(130)}\).  The anomaly value
\eqref{eq:qcd-pion-transition-anomaly-normalization} and the asymptotic value
\eqref{eq:qcd-pion-transition-asymptotic} constrain two different boundary
regimes of the same form factor.  They do not imply a unique interpolation.
Published high-\(Q^2\) measurements are therefore tests of the approach to the
factorized regime and of LCDA shape assumptions, not independent definitions
of the anomaly or of asymptotic freedom.

The BaBar/Belle tension in the neutral-pion transition form factor is best
formulated in exactly these terms.  A reported finite-\(Q^2\) trend can
challenge a chosen LCDA model, a treatment of endpoint regions, or an estimate
of power corrections.  It cannot by itself refute
\eqref{eq:qcd-pion-transition-anomaly-normalization} or
\eqref{eq:qcd-pion-transition-asymptotic}, because those two equations live at
opposite ends of the form factor and rest on different controlled arguments:
the first on the axial anomaly and the second on leading-twist factorization
plus ERBL evolution.  Any quantitative comparison to data must therefore state
the factorization scale, perturbative order, LCDA input, and power-correction
model before it is a QCD statement.

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Brodsky--Farrar scaling]
\label{ca:qcd-brodsky-farrar-scaling-status}
Consider a fixed-angle exclusive process
\[
  H_1+H_2\longrightarrow H_3+H_4
\]
whose leading Fock components contain \(n_i\) collinear elementary fields in
the corresponding leading-twist light-ray operator, and set
\(n=\sum_i n_i\).  If a leading-power exclusive factorization theorem holds,
if endpoint configurations are power suppressed in the specified scheme, and
if the hard coefficient is evaluated at momentum transfer of order
\(\sqrt s\), then
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal M(s,t)\sim s^{\,2-n/2}
  \quad\text{at fixed }t/s,
  \qquad
  \frac{\dd\sigma}{\dd t}\sim s^{\,2-n}.
  \label{eq:qcd-brodsky-farrar-counting}
\end{equation}
The derivation is the power counting of the hard coefficient after all
external hadrons have been replaced by their normalized leading-twist
distribution amplitudes.  It is not a dimensional-analysis argument applied to
hadron fields.  For example, a pion electromagnetic form factor has
\(n=4\) across the two pion light-ray operators and therefore scales as
\(F_\pi(Q^2)\sim Q^{-2}\), while fixed-angle
\(\pi\pi\to\pi\pi\) has \(n=8\) and gives
\(\dd\sigma/\dd t\sim s^{-6}\), up to logarithmic evolution and controlled
power corrections.
\end{controlledapproximation}

The pion \(S\)-matrix is thus accessed by different controlled descriptions in
different regions.  Chapter~\ref{ch:volume-ii-21} derives the chiral
low-energy amplitudes and anomaly couplings; Chapter~\ref{ch:volume-ii-07}
develops the analytic and dispersive language needed for the resonance
region; the present section gives the asymptotic exclusive regime governed by
light-ray factorization and asymptotic freedom.  These are not three theories.
They are three coordinate systems on matrix elements of the same QCD
operators, with different hypotheses controlling their errors.  A complete
nonperturbative construction of QCD would define the relevant matrix elements
first; chiral perturbation theory, dispersive methods, lattice calculations,
and hard exclusive factorization are then approximation or reconstruction
methods applied to that common object.

\section{Local Twist-Two Operators and Integer Moments}

The light-ray definition packages an infinite family of local operators.  For
quarks, the symmetric traceless spin-\(N\) operators have the form
\[
  \mathcal O_{q}^{\mu_1\cdots\mu_N}
  =
  \bar q\,
  \gamma^{(\mu_1}
  \ii D^{\mu_2}\cdots \ii D^{\mu_N)}
  q
  -
  \text{traces},
  \qquad N\ge1,
\]
with gauge-covariant derivatives in the appropriate representation.  The
parentheses denote symmetrization over Lorentz indices.  The gluon operators
are
\[
  \mathcal O_{g}^{\mu_1\cdots\mu_N}
  =
  F^{(\mu_1}{}_{\rho}\,
  \ii D^{\mu_2}\cdots\ii D^{\mu_{N-1}}
  F^{\mu_N)\rho}
  -
  \text{traces},
  \qquad N\ge2 .
\]
Both have twist two after subtracting traces.  Their hadron matrix elements
are fixed by Lorentz covariance up to scalar reduced matrix elements:
\[
  \bra{P}\mathcal O_{a}^{\mu_1\cdots\mu_N}(\mu)\ket{P}
  =
  2\,a_{a,N}(\mu)
  \bigl(P^{\mu_1}\cdots P^{\mu_N}-\text{traces}\bigr),
  \qquad a=q,g .
\]
The normalization of \(a_{a,N}\) is fixed already at tree level by replacing
the hadron with a single parton state.  Let
\(\ket{p,i,s}\) be a massless quark of flavor \(i\) and spin \(s\), and use
\(\bar u_s(p)\gamma^\mu u_s(p)=2p^\mu\).  Since each covariant derivative in
\(\mathcal O_{q_j}\) acts on the external plane wave as multiplication by
\(p^\mu\) at tree level,
\[
  \bra{p,i,s}\mathcal O_{q_j}^{\mu_1\cdots\mu_N}\ket{p,i,s}_{\rm tree}
  =
  2\delta_{ij}
  \bigl(p^{\mu_1}\cdots p^{\mu_N}-\text{traces}\bigr).
\]
Thus a quark target has
\[
  a_{q_j,N}^{\,q_i,{\rm tree}}=\delta_{ij},
  \qquad
  a_{g,N}^{\,q_i,{\rm tree}}=0 .
\]
For a single gluon state \(\ket{p,A,\lambda}\), the linearized field strength
is
\[
  F^{\mu\nu,A}(x)
  =
  \ii\bigl(p^\mu\varepsilon^\nu_\lambda
  -p^\nu\varepsilon^\mu_\lambda\bigr)\ee^{-\ii p\cdot x},
  \qquad
  p\cdot\varepsilon_\lambda=0 .
\]
The color- and spin-averaged partonic matrix element is
\[
  \frac{1}{2(N_c^2-1)}
  \sum_{A,\lambda}
  \bra{p,A,\lambda}\mathcal O_{g}^{\mu_1\cdots\mu_N}
  \ket{p,A,\lambda}_{\rm tree}
  =
  2
  \bigl(p^{\mu_1}\cdots p^{\mu_N}-\text{traces}\bigr),
\]
so
\[
  a_{g,N}^{\,g,{\rm tree}}=1,
  \qquad
  a_{q_j,N}^{\,g,{\rm tree}}=0 .
\]
Equivalently, the tree-level parton distributions are
\(f_{q_j/q_i}(x)=\delta_{ij}\delta(1-x)\),
\(f_{g/g}(x)=\delta(1-x)\), and the mixed quark-gluon distributions vanish.

Expanding the light-ray operator near zero separation gives these local
operators contracted with the lightlike vector \(n^\mu\).  Consequently the
integer moments of the parton distributions are the same reduced matrix
elements, with the precise flavor and charge-conjugation combination fixed by
the current channel:
\[
  a_{a,N}(\mu)
  =
  \int_0^1 \dd x\,x^{N-1} f_{a/H}(x,\mu)
\]
for the corresponding parton combination.  The local OPE and the nonlocal
light-ray factorization are therefore two presentations of the same
short-distance data.

Renormalization mixes operators with the same spin, twist, and quantum
numbers.  Taking integer moments of \eqref{eq:dglap-evolution} gives
\[
  \mu\frac{\dd}{\dd\mu}a_{a,N}(\mu)
  =
  \sum_b P_{ab,N}(g(\mu))\,a_{b,N}(\mu),
  \qquad
  P_{ab,N}(g)=\int_0^1\dd x\,x^{N-1}P_{ab}(x,g).
\]
The coefficient functions in the current OPE obey the dual evolution so that
the physical structure functions are independent of the auxiliary
factorization scale.  This is the local-operator form of perturbative
scaling violation in deep inelastic scattering.

For a spin-\(N\) leading-twist operator whose scaling dimension near the
ultraviolet is
\[
  \Delta_N(g)=N+2+\tau_{1,N}g^2+O(g^4),
\]
the one-loop running
\[
  \frac{\dd}{\dd\log\mu}\frac1{g^2(\mu)}
  =
  \frac{b}{2\pi^2}+O(g^2)
\]
implies logarithmic scaling of its matrix element and Wilson coefficient.
Equivalently, with
\[
  \omega:=\frac{2P\cdot q}{Q^2}=\frac1{x_B},
\]
the leading large-\(Q\) term in the \(N\)-th moment contribution has the form
\begin{equation}
  W_N(Q,\omega)
  \propto
  \omega^N
  \left(
    \log\frac{Q}{\Lambda}
  \right)^{-2\pi^2\tau_{1,N}/b}
  \left[1+O\!\left(\frac1{\log(Q/\Lambda)}\right)\right],
  \label{eq:qcd-dis-logarithmic-scaling-violation}
\end{equation}
up to the matrix of anomalous dimensions when several operators mix.  The
power \(\omega^N\) is the Bjorken-scaling kinematic dependence of a spin-\(N\)
operator; asymptotic freedom turns exact scaling into logarithmic scaling
violation.

\section{Endpoint, Large Spin, and the Cusp Coefficient}

The compact-\(x\) factorization statement in
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:qcd-dis-leading-twist-factorization} deliberately does not
claim uniform control as \(x_B\to1\).  In that endpoint region the invariant
mass of the hadronic final state,
\[
  W_X^2=(P+q)^2
  =
  M^2+Q^2\left(\frac1{x_B}-1\right),
\]
is much smaller than \(Q^2\).  The short-distance coefficient functions then
contain distributions supported near \(x=1\), such as
\([\log^k(1-x)/(1-x)]_+\), and the perturbative expansion must be reorganized.
The Mellin transform turns this endpoint problem into a large-spin problem.
For a distribution \(K(x)\), define
\[
  K_N:=\int_0^1\dd x\,x^{N-1}K(x).
\]
Using the \(D_0\) convention above, the nonsinglet one-loop kernel has the
exact moment
\begin{equation}
  P_{{\rm ns},N}^{(0)}
  =
  C_F\left[
    -2H_{N-1}-\frac1N-\frac1{N+1}+\frac32
  \right],
  \qquad N\ge1 .
  \label{eq:qcd-nonsinglet-moment-exact}
\end{equation}
This formula is a useful normalization check: at \(N=1\) it gives quark-number
conservation, and at large \(N\)
\begin{equation}
  P_{{\rm ns},N}^{(0)}
  =
  -2C_F\log N
  +C_F\left(\frac32-2\gamma_{\rm E}\right)
  +O(N^{-1}).
  \label{eq:qcd-nonsinglet-large-n}
\end{equation}
Therefore, with the convention
\(P=(g^2/8\pi^2)P^{(0)}+O(g^4)\), the large-\(N\) anomalous dimension contains
\[
  -\Gamma_{\rm cusp}(g)\log N,
  \qquad
  \Gamma_{\rm cusp}(g)
  =
  \frac{g^2C_F}{4\pi^2}+O(g^4)
\]
in the monograph's trace-delta normalization.  This is the same invariant
coefficient as the one-loop lightlike Wilson-line cusp coefficient: if
\(T^a\) denotes the common half-trace generator and
\(g_{\rm ht}=\sqrt2\,g\), then
\[
  g^2C_F=g_{\rm ht}^2C_F^{\rm ht}.
\]
The cusp coefficient is thus independent of the choice of generator
coordinates once the coupling coordinate is transformed with the action.

Endpoint resummation is not a new definition of the PDF.  It is an additional
factorization of the coefficient function in a region where the compact-\(x\)
remainder estimate is not uniform.  A precise threshold factorization theorem
must specify the hard current coefficient, the jet function for the nearly
collinear final-state radiation, the soft Wilson-line matrix element, the
contour prescription for Mellin or Laplace inversion, and a remainder estimate
in the joint limit \(Q\to\infty\), \(N\to\infty\).  The large-spin logarithm in
\eqref{eq:qcd-nonsinglet-large-n} is the operator-renormalization side of that
structure.  The small-\(x\) limit is a different boundary of the same DIS
observable and is not obtained by continuing the threshold expansion.

\section{\texorpdfstring{Small-\(x\) Boundary, Dipoles, and the BFKL Kernel}
{Small-x Boundary, Dipoles, and the BFKL Kernel}}
\label{sec:qcd-small-x-bfkl}

The compact-\(x_B\) factorization datum in
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:qcd-dis-leading-twist-factorization} also does not claim
uniform control as \(x_B\to0\).  Put
\[
  Y:=\log\frac1{x_B},
\]
up to a process-dependent finite shift fixed by the chosen rapidity
factorization scheme.  In the high-energy boundary \(Y\gg1\), powers of
\(g^2Y\) may compete with powers of \(g^2\).  The leading-logarithmic
small-\(x\) expansion is therefore not a new definition of QCD and not a
replacement for the hadronic tensor
\eqref{eq:hadronic-tensor-definition}.  It is a rapidity factorization of
regulated Wilson-line matrix elements in a kinematic region where the
ordinary twist-two evolution at fixed \(x_B\) is not uniform.

Let \(\mathbf x,\mathbf y,\mathbf z\in\mathbb R^2\) denote transverse
coordinates, and set
\[
  r_{xy}:=|\mathbf x-\mathbf y|.
\]
The leading transverse kernel is
\begin{equation}
  M_{\mathbf x\mathbf y\mathbf z}
  :=
  \frac{r_{xy}^2}{r_{xz}^2 r_{zy}^2}.
  \label{eq:qcd-dipole-transverse-kernel}
\end{equation}
The singularities at \(\mathbf z=\mathbf x\) and
\(\mathbf z=\mathbf y\) are not meaningful as separate real-emission
probabilities.  They are defined only after the virtual subtraction in the
evolution equation, or after an equivalent rapidity regulator and finite-part
map have been specified.

\begin{definition}[Regulated small-\(x\) dipole datum]
\label{def:qcd-small-x-dipole-datum}
A small-\(x\) dipole datum for a color-singlet probe consists of:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item a QCD regulator \(\mathcal R_\epsilon\) preserving background gauge
  covariance, or a gauge-fixed BV regulator with the quantum master equation;
  \item two nearly lightlike Wilson-line directions, a rapidity regulator
  \(\rho\), and a finite rapidity separation \(Y\);
  \item fundamental Wilson transporters
  \(U_{\rho,Y}(\mathbf x)\) and \(U_{\rho,Y}(\mathbf y)\), with transverse
  closures or boundary conditions that make the residual endpoint gauge
  transformations explicit;
  \item the renormalized color dipole matrix element
  \begin{equation}
    S_Y(\mathbf x,\mathbf y)
    :=
    \frac1{N_c}
    \left\langle
      \operatorname{tr}_{\square}
      \bigl[
        U_{\rho,Y}(\mathbf x)U_{\rho,Y}(\mathbf y)^\dagger
      \bigr]
    \right\rangle_{\epsilon,\rho,Y}^{\rm ren},
    \qquad
    N_Y(\mathbf x,\mathbf y):=1-S_Y(\mathbf x,\mathbf y);
    \label{eq:qcd-small-x-dipole-definition}
  \end{equation}
  \item a finite-part prescription for ultraviolet endpoint divergences,
  lightlike or near-lightlike rapidity divergences, and possible cusp
  divergences introduced by the chosen closures.
\end{enumerate}
The quantity \(S_Y\) is a Wilson-line matrix element.  Its connection to a
measured small-\(x\) structure function is an additional high-energy
factorization statement with its own impact factor, rapidity subtraction, and
power-remainder data.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Gauge invariance of the dipole matrix element]
\label{prop:qcd-small-x-dipole-gauge-invariance}
At finite regulator, the trace in
\eqref{eq:qcd-small-x-dipole-definition} is gauge invariant after the
endpoint closures or boundary conditions of
Definition~\ref{def:qcd-small-x-dipole-datum} are included.  A background
gauge-covariant finite-part prescription therefore gives a gauge-invariant
renormalized dipole matrix element.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Each Wilson transporter transforms by multiplication with the gauge
transformation at its two endpoints.  Along a closed contour the adjacent
endpoint factors cancel and the residual base-point factor is removed by the
cyclicity of \(\operatorname{tr}_{\square}\).  If the regulated Wilson lines
are represented instead as open lines ending at a rapidity boundary, the
boundary condition is part of the datum and supplies the same endpoint
cancellation.  The finite-part map changes only regulator and scale
coordinates and is assumed background gauge covariant; hence it cannot
introduce an uncanceled color index.
\end{proof}

\begin{hypothesis}[Leading-logarithmic dipole/BFKL evolution datum]
\label{hyp:qcd-leading-log-small-x-datum}
In a fixed-coupling leading-logarithmic rapidity scheme, the linearized
color-singlet dipole amplitude obeys
\begin{equation}
  \partial_Y N_Y(\mathbf x,\mathbf y)
  =
  \frac{g^2 C_A}{8\pi^3}
  \int_{\mathbb R^2}\dd^2\mathbf z\,
  M_{\mathbf x\mathbf y\mathbf z}
  \bigl[
    N_Y(\mathbf x,\mathbf z)
    +N_Y(\mathbf z,\mathbf y)
    -N_Y(\mathbf x,\mathbf y)
  \bigr],
  \label{eq:qcd-coordinate-bfkl-equation}
\end{equation}
where \(C_A=2N_c\) in the trace convention of
\eqref{eq:qcd-casimir-definitions}.  Equivalently, with
\[
  \bar\alpha_{\rm s}:=\frac{g^2C_A}{4\pi^2}
  =
  \frac{g^2N_c}{2\pi^2},
\]
the right-hand side is
\[
  \bar\alpha_{\rm s}\,
  \frac1{2\pi}
  \int\dd^2\mathbf z\,M_{\mathbf x\mathbf y\mathbf z}[\cdots].
\]
In the common half-trace convention,
\(g_{\rm ht}^2=2g^2\) and \(C_A^{\rm ht}=N_c\), so the product
\(g^2C_A=g_{\rm ht}^2C_A^{\rm ht}\) and the kernel coefficient are unchanged.

For a large-\(N_c\) dipole-factorization truncation of the Balitsky hierarchy,
the corresponding nonlinear equation for \(N_Y=1-S_Y\) has the additional
term
\[
  -\frac{g^2 C_A}{8\pi^3}
  \int\dd^2\mathbf z\,
  M_{\mathbf x\mathbf y\mathbf z}\,
  N_Y(\mathbf x,\mathbf z)N_Y(\mathbf z,\mathbf y).
  \label{eq:qcd-bk-nonlinear-term}
\]
At finite \(N_c\), the exact Wilson-line rapidity hierarchy contains higher
multi-trace operators; replacing them by the product in
\eqref{eq:qcd-bk-nonlinear-term} is an additional closure assumption, not a
theorem about continuum QCD.
\end{hypothesis}

\begin{proposition}[Conformal covariance of the transverse kernel]
\label{prop:qcd-bfkl-kernel-conformal-covariance}
The measure
\[
  \dd^2\mathbf z\,M_{\mathbf x\mathbf y\mathbf z}
\]
is invariant under translations, rotations, uniform scalings, and inversion
\(\mathbf u\mapsto\mathbf u/|\mathbf u|^2\), whenever the transformed points
avoid the inversion center.  Thus the leading fixed-coupling transverse
kernel is covariant under the real Mobius transformations generated by these
maps.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Translations and rotations preserve all distances and \(\dd^2\mathbf z\).
Under the scaling \(\mathbf u\mapsto\lambda\mathbf u\), the kernel
\(M_{\mathbf x\mathbf y\mathbf z}\) scales as \(\lambda^{-2}\), while
\(\dd^2\mathbf z\) scales as \(\lambda^2\).

For inversion, write \(\mathbf u'=\mathbf u/|\mathbf u|^2\).  The Euclidean
distance and area element transform as
\[
  |\mathbf u'-\mathbf v'|^2
  =
  \frac{|\mathbf u-\mathbf v|^2}
       {|\mathbf u|^2|\mathbf v|^2},
  \qquad
  \dd^2\mathbf z'
  =
  \frac{\dd^2\mathbf z}{|\mathbf z|^4}.
\]
Substituting these identities gives
\[
  M_{\mathbf x'\mathbf y'\mathbf z'}\,\dd^2\mathbf z'
  =
  \frac{
    r_{xy}^2/(|\mathbf x|^2|\mathbf y|^2)
  }{
    r_{xz}^2/(|\mathbf x|^2|\mathbf z|^2)\,
    r_{zy}^2/(|\mathbf z|^2|\mathbf y|^2)
  }
  \frac{\dd^2\mathbf z}{|\mathbf z|^4}
  =
  M_{\mathbf x\mathbf y\mathbf z}\,\dd^2\mathbf z.
\]
This proves the stated covariance.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Mellin eigenvalue of the leading BFKL kernel]
\label{prop:qcd-bfkl-mellin-eigenvalue}
Let \(0<\operatorname{Re}\gamma<1\).  For the power
\[
  f_\gamma(\mathbf x,\mathbf y)
  =
  \bigl(\mu_\perp^2 r_{xy}^2\bigr)^\gamma ,
\]
define the subtracted transverse integral by analytic regularization as in
the proof below.  Then
\begin{equation}
  \frac1{2\pi}\int_{\mathbb R^2}\dd^2\mathbf z\,
  M_{\mathbf x\mathbf y\mathbf z}
  \bigl[
    f_\gamma(\mathbf x,\mathbf z)
    +f_\gamma(\mathbf z,\mathbf y)
    -f_\gamma(\mathbf x,\mathbf y)
  \bigr]
  =
  \chi(\gamma)f_\gamma(\mathbf x,\mathbf y),
  \label{eq:qcd-bfkl-eigenvalue-equation}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
  \chi(\gamma)
  =
  2\psi(1)-\psi(\gamma)-\psi(1-\gamma),
  \qquad
  \psi(u):=\frac{\dd}{\dd u}\log\Gamma(u).
  \label{eq:qcd-bfkl-characteristic-function}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By translation and scaling it suffices to set
\(\mathbf y=0\), \(r_{xy}=1\), and \(\mu_\perp=1\).  The singular terms in
the three brackets are regulated in \(d=2-2\epsilon\) transverse dimensions.
The Euclidean beta integral
\[
  \int\dd^d\mathbf z\,
  \frac1{(\mathbf z^2)^a((\mathbf z-\mathbf x)^2)^b}
  =
  \pi^{d/2}
  \frac{
    \Gamma(d/2-a)\Gamma(d/2-b)\Gamma(a+b-d/2)
  }{
    \Gamma(a)\Gamma(b)\Gamma(d-a-b)
  }
  (\mathbf x^2)^{d/2-a-b}
  \label{eq:qcd-bfkl-beta-integral}
\]
is first valid in its convergence domain and then analytically continued.
Applying \eqref{eq:qcd-bfkl-beta-integral} to the three pieces gives
\[
\begin{aligned}
  J_\epsilon(\gamma)
  &=
  \pi^{1-\epsilon}
  \frac{
    \Gamma(\gamma-\epsilon)\Gamma(-\epsilon)
    \Gamma(1-\gamma+\epsilon)
  }{
    \Gamma(1-\gamma)\Gamma(\gamma-2\epsilon)
  },\\
  J_\epsilon(1-\gamma)
  &=
  \pi^{1-\epsilon}
  \frac{
    \Gamma(1-\gamma-\epsilon)\Gamma(-\epsilon)
    \Gamma(\gamma+\epsilon)
  }{
    \Gamma(\gamma)\Gamma(1-\gamma-2\epsilon)
  },\\
  J_\epsilon(0)
  &=
  \pi^{1-\epsilon}
  \frac{\Gamma(-\epsilon)^2\Gamma(1+\epsilon)}
       {\Gamma(-2\epsilon)} .
\end{aligned}
\]
The regulated subtracted integral is
\[
  J_\epsilon(\gamma)+J_\epsilon(1-\gamma)-J_\epsilon(0).
\]
Using
\[
  \Gamma(u+\delta)
  =
  \Gamma(u)\bigl(1+\delta\psi(u)+O(\delta^2)\bigr)
\]
and the corresponding expansion at the pole \(u=0\), the \(1/\epsilon\)
terms cancel and the finite part is
\[
  2\pi\,[2\psi(1)-\psi(\gamma)-\psi(1-\gamma)].
\]
Dividing by \(2\pi\) proves
\eqref{eq:qcd-bfkl-eigenvalue-equation}.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Fixed-coupling leading intercept and diffusion coefficient]
\label{cor:qcd-bfkl-intercept-diffusion}
For the leading fixed-coupling kernel in
\eqref{eq:qcd-coordinate-bfkl-equation},
\[
  \chi\!\left(\frac12\right)=4\log2,
  \qquad
  \chi\!\left(\frac12+\ii\nu\right)
  =
  4\log2-14\zeta(3)\nu^2+O(\nu^4).
\]
Thus a Mellin component near \(\gamma=\frac12\) evolves as
\[
  \exp\!\left[
    \bar\alpha_{\rm s}\,4\log2\,Y
    -\bar\alpha_{\rm s}\,14\zeta(3)\nu^2Y
    +O(\bar\alpha_{\rm s}\nu^4Y)
  \right]
\]
inside the fixed-coupling leading-logarithmic datum.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The reflection identities for the polygamma function give
\[
  \psi\!\left(\frac12\right)=-\gamma_{\rm E}-2\log2,
  \qquad
  \psi''\!\left(\frac12\right)=-14\zeta(3).
\]
Substitution into
\eqref{eq:qcd-bfkl-characteristic-function} gives the value at
\(\gamma=\frac12\).  Differentiating
\(\chi(\gamma)\) shows \(\chi'(\frac12)=0\) and
\(\chi''(\frac12)=28\zeta(3)\).  Expanding at
\(\gamma=\frac12+\ii\nu\) gives the displayed sign.
\end{proof}

\begin{controlledapproximation}[Status of small-\(x\) resummation]
\label{ca:qcd-small-x-status}
A small-\(x\) resummation used for a QCD observable must state:
the regulated Wilson-line operator being evolved; the rapidity variable and
subtraction scheme; the impact factor connecting the Wilson-line matrix
element to the measured process; whether running coupling, energy-scale,
collinear-improvement, saturation, or finite-\(N_c\) hierarchy effects are
included; and the topology of the remainder estimate.  The BFKL kernel in
Proposition~\ref{prop:qcd-bfkl-mellin-eigenvalue} is a theorem about the
leading transverse integral.  It is not by itself a nonperturbative
construction of high-energy hadron scattering, nor a proof of the growth of a
unitarized physical cross section.
\end{controlledapproximation}
